Character Creation

Welcome to Bonfire Character Creation! You'll notice that there's a lot of steps and, if you're familiar with other TTRPGs, that it's a bit longer and a bit more complicated than other games. Why is that?

The first is that it gives you, the player, more choice. Do you want to build a cunning fighter than actually using their brains instead of their brawns to defeat others? Do you want to play a sly diplomat that crushes her opponents' morale without even lifting a finger? Or perhaps you want to play a power wizard that concocts his spells on the fly, building the perfect one for each scenario?

More importantly, do you want those different characters to actually feel different when you play them? So that convincing some actually feels different than just beating them to death?

This is the first thing that Bonfire offers you.

The second thing is that it allows you to be surprised during creation: through your choices and rolls, you'll get a more fully formed character than in other systems. You'll get what you want with extra twists that help add interest and depth to your character that you wouldn't get in other systems.

And not only that, but you'll also have those choices, twists, and depth mean something in play. Is your character brash? You'll be rewarded for playing that way in the game.

So, what are you waiting for? Let's get started!

1. Roll Stat Scores

Your character has 6 attributes that define your character physically and mentally. These are Strength (Str), Dexterity (Dex), Constitution (Con), Intellect (Int), Wisdom (Wis), and Charisma (Cha). More on details are found in Chapter 2: Stat Scores.

Roll 3d6 for each of these Abilities to generate that score.

This should result in something similar to this:

Str: 13

Dex: 7

Con: 10

Int: 14

Wis: 11

Cha: 6

Bonfire is specifically balanced for you to roll 3d6 in order, with 10 being the average result but don't worry about feeling like you have low scores or they're not in the order you want: you'll have a chance to rearrange and modify them later.

But even if you have objectively lower stats than the rest of the company, you'll still be able to contribute in a meaningful way in your own area of expertise because Bonfire is built as a team game, so nobody is going to be good at everything.

In Bonfire, you'll almost always be weaker than your opponent: what makes a hero is not supernatural abilities, but the simple fact that he fights longer and harder for what he believes in than other men

2. Receive Crp

Alright, you have your scores. Now it’s time to determine how many Creation Points (or CrP, for short) you’ll start with. These CrP will be spent on modifying your character, buying them their skills and increasing their Scores. They may also be spent on rerolls at certain steps.

Even still, you may want to switch your stats around. This may be because you have almost the right stats, but you have a specific character concept in mind. For instance, using the example stats in Step 1, your party may need a diplomatic character more than a strong character. In this case, it would really help to swap Strength and Charisma.

You can freely switch around your stats as need but, in that case, you only receive 25 CrPs.

If you switch only 4 of your stats, you receive 50 CrPs.

If you switch 2, you receive 75 CrPs.

And if you keep your stats the way they are, with no changes, you gain 100 CrPs to work with.

3. Select Race

Your character’s race will change how they interact with the world and what they’ll be good and bad at so pick carefully.

Details are found in Chapter 3: Races so go there and pick one and come back here when you’re done.

4. Choose Your Archetypes

Your character has an area of expertise represented by two Archetypes.

You choose a Primary and a Secondary Archetype and pay the price in CrP for both based on your race’s Archetype Cost section. Descriptions of the different Archetypes are found in Chapter 4: Archetypes along with more details on how to combine them.

If you’ve chosen to reroll your stats and have no CrPs to work with, congratulations, you’re now in CrP debt and need to make it up by the end of Character Creation.

You must select two Archetypes before going further.

5. Record Archetype Abilities

This is more for Weird-Adept Archetypes, as they’ll head over to Chapter 11: The Weird to roll their starting spells but now is the time to record any free Skills, or Trainings you obtained free from your Archetype choice, as well as Archetype Abilities.

6. Rolls Flaws

All heroes have flaws. That’s what makes them relatable and human (even if they’re an orc). Character Flaws earn you additional CrP, which is great. Flaws can also be used in Confrontations to further the story.

For a list of Flaws flip to Chapter 5: Flaws.

If you’ve gone into CrP debt and you’re not out of it by the end of this stage, you’ll need to go back and reselect your Archetypes so that you are or go back to you starting set of stats and begin Character Creation all over again with them.

7. Adjust Stats

Now, it is time to do the final adjustments to your stats. This isn't your final adjustments: you'll have a chance to increase them again level up.

The price to increase a Stat is the Stat + 10. So, to get a Stat to 9 from 8, it would cost 18 CrP.

This can't bring a stat above 20.

8. Calculate Character Vitals

Now it’s time to calculate your character’s Honor, Stress Threshold, and Vitality.

These 3 things are important parts of the game and serve as the prime mechanics when running a Bonfire game. If you’re not familiar with them head over to Chapter 6: Character Vitals.

This chapter will also give you an overview of the character sheet that you’ll get more acquainted with later.

If you’ve already played Bonfire before, here’s a cheat sheet for calculating those things:

  • HONOR This is determined by your “Starting Honor” listed under your Charisma
  • STRESS THRESHOLD This is your three times your Wis score.
  • VITALITY This is Con score + Primary Archetype’s Vitality Die + Vitality Size Modifier from race, divided into 4 Categories.
  • MAX FAVOR While Servants are the ones that primarily use it, any person can petition the Divines for aid, although success mostly based on your Honor Category and whether or not you've been up with your Devotions. More on Favor is found in Chapter 12: The Divine.

Don't forget that you get a bonus to your CrP from the Honor of your last character. If this is your first character, you instead get 25 CrP. Enjoy.

9. Trainings & Skills

Trainings and Skills are additional areas of expertise that your character has obtained above his or her race and class.

Both cost CrP. Prices and descriptions can be found at the bottom of Chapter 9: Combat and in Chapter 7: Skills.

Note that you get the Advanced Language Skill for free in your native language with its Rank starting at your Int.

Out of Order Character Creation

If you’re a little bit more familiar with Bonfire Character creation, these last steps (step 9, 10, and 11) can be taken in any order you’d like, even skipping back and forth between them.

10. Define Confrontation Characteristics

Your character is more than just raw stats, skills, and abilities. At this step, you’re going to define more about who they see themselves as and how others perceive them by defining their Traits, Goals, and Devotions. Jump to Chapter 8: Confrontation.

11. Buy Equipment

Every character starts with a kit of gear, which has a list of per purchased starting gear as well as an extra bit of starting cash they you can spend on additional things. Proceed to Chapter 10: Equipment for a full list of available kits and gear you can pick up.

You may also cash in any left-over CrP for sp at 1 CrP for 10 sc, but you don’t have to. You can save your CrP to spend later at your level up.

After purchasing your equipment, adjust your Carry.

12. Transfer To Character Sheet

Congratulations: you’re on the home stretch! Finish your character off by transferring your notes to a fresh character sheet, an example of which, with a break down, is found in Chapter 6: Character Vitals. You can also find a download for the character sheet here.

Exploding Dice

You’ll notice an exclamation mark (!) behind a lot of dice notations. This marks the dice as exploding, which means that should the maximum of that dice is rolled, you get to roll it again, this time with a - 1, and add what you rolled to the total.

This continues for as long as you roll the maximum dice, however, the - 1 always stays a -1 one.

So, if you roll a 3d8! for damage, you get a 5, 8, 8. Since you rolled the maximum value on two of your dice, you roll those dice again, and roll an 8, and 5, giving you a subtotal of 32 ( 5 + 8 + 8 + 8 - 1 + 5 - 1 ) but since you rolled another 8, you get to roll that dice again, and you get a 1, netting you a 0 ( 1 - 1 ).

There are two things you should be aware of: 1d100! explode to a 1d20!, while 1d20! explode to a d6!.

The second thing is that explosion dice don’t add additional dice to the number. So, in the example above, all that damage is only counted as having been done with 3 dice (instead of the 5 that were actually rolled).

Dice Size Hierarchy

Bonfire plays around a lot with dice sizes, so it’s important to know what dice to grab in those cases.

Dice sizes go as follows:

d2 → d3 → d4 → d6 → d8 → d10 → d12 → d20

If a d4 is exploding and drops to a d3 or lower, it stops exploding.

If the dice size increases past a d20, you’ll add an extra dice starting at a d4. Further dice sizes will increase this smaller dice. This can continue ad nauseum, but no matter how many dice there are, they’re always considered to be rolled on 1 dice.

So, 3d20! + d10! is still considered 1 dice.

Stat Scores

Stat Scores represent different dimensions of your character and how good their baseline is at certain activities. These dimensions are Strength, Dexterity, Constitution, Intellect, Wisdom, Charisma.

Stat Checks

There many come a time where a Skill Check doesn’t exactly cover what needs to be tested. What skill covers trying to deadlift a boulder or remember a fact about a person? When skills fail and it’s simply a raw test of an ability, Stat Checks come into play.

Players making an unopposed ability check roll a d20 and try to get a result equal to or under their stat score. If the check is made at 1/2 the score, they're trying to roll equal to or under their score, rounded down. Should they do so, they succeed.

OPPOSED CHECKS

Opposed checks work almost the same. The player rolls a d20! + their relevant stat score vs an opposing d20! + any relevant modifiers (such as the boulder being really heavy or only their foes relevant stat score). The person with the higher total succeeds.

Strength

Strength (Str) represents your character’s pure brawn. How much can she lift and carry? How strong are her punches?

DAMAGE

This number is added to your damage whenever your character hits something with their fits or uses thrown ranged weapons. It’s the raw, physical force he can put into an object.

CARRY

This number represents the number of items a character can carry before he becomes slowed. More on Carry is found in Chapter 10: Equipment.

SKILL MOD

This number represents the bonus you apply to Skill Checks whenever you roll a Skill with this as a listed Stat. Pick the lowest if there are multiple Skills listed.

CONFRONTATION DIE

Sometimes your character’s strength can play into social situations, such as trying to intimidate your opponent. This is the die that gets added to your dice pool for Confrontations if your Strength is applicable.

Dexterity (Dex) is a measure of how agile your character is. Can she dodge arrows, or can she execute a graceful pirouette? Dexterity is crucial for avoiding blows in combat or traps in a hallway.

ATTACK

Being graceful allows your character to take advantage of openings others can’t. This number gets added to all attack rolls your character makes.

DEFENSE

If you can move quicker than your opponent, you can often get out of harm’s way before it becomes a problem. This number gets added to all melee defense rolls your character makes.

INITIATIVE

Another bonus of being quick on your feet is the ability to get moving quicker when manure hits the windmill. This number gets added to your initiative rolls at the beginning of combat.

SKILL MOD

This number represents the bonus you apply to Skill Checks whenever you roll a Skill with this as a listed Stat. Pick the lowest if there are multiple Skills listed.

CONFRONTATION DIE

Sometimes your character’s dexterity can play into social situations, such as trying to seduce your opponent. This is the die that gets added to your dice pool for Confrontations if your Dexterity is applicable.

Constitution (Con) represents your character’s overall health and toughness. Can he shrug off the Dancing Death or does he succumb to a head cold? Can she take a solid blow in combat and not even blink? These are the things Constitution oversees.

Constitution is the base of your starting Vitality so don’t neglect it.

MIN VITALITY

Every other level, a character gains a reroll of their Vitality Die. This number is the minimum amount that reroll can be.

So, if a Fighter with 15 Constitution gets a 3 on their reroll, they add 4 to that result to get it to 7. This cannot exceed the amount that can be rolled on your dice. If a wizard has a minimum reroll of 7, they will still only get 4 Vitality from their dice.

SKILL MOD

This number represents the bonus you apply to Skill Checks whenever you roll a Skill with this as a listed Stat. Pick the lowest if there are multiple Skills listed.

CONFRONTATION DIE

Sometimes your character’s constitution can play into social situations, such as convincing your opponent she really doesn’t want to fight you. This is the die that gets added to your dice pool for Confrontations if your Constitution is applicable.

Intellect (Int) measures your character’s raw knowledge: how much data can he remember? Can she do mathematical calculations or remember who the Elector of Stanitz is? Intellect doesn’t help in applying that knowledge, but it does give you knowledge to draw on.

ATTACK

Being able to pinpoint holes in your opponent’s defense allows you to see openings that others don’t. A cunning intellect can help land a telling blow. This number is added to all attack rolls your character makes.

LvL CrP

A character with a high Intellect is able to grasp concepts and skills quicker than others, allowing him to learn more things than others in an equivalent amount of time. This is the amount of CrP that a character gets when they level up. More on leveling is found in Chapter 13: Character Progression.

SKILL MOD

This number represents the bonus you apply to Skill Checks whenever you roll a Skill with this as a listed Stat. Pick the lowest if there are multiple Skills listed.

CONFRONTATION DIE

Sometimes your character’s intelligence can play into social situations, such as convincing someone that you’re right simply because you know more. This is the die that gets added to your dice pool for Confrontations if your Intellect is applicable.

Roll to Recall

Details are hard to remember, and notes can get lost or disorganized. To keep play moving, the player can make a Int Ability Check vs d20! to remember a piece of information that was heard in a previous session, such a person’s name or where someone came from.

To clarify: this can’t be used to remember information that was given to you this same session.

Wisdom (Wis) is applied knowledge. Does she process information quicker and learn from other’s mistakes? Does he understand life is more than just a set of numbers of probabilities? Can she see other’s viewpoints? Wisdom can also be defined as force of will, the ability to overcome physical problems with mental force.

DEFENSE

Having greater body awareness allows you to keep your form tight and your limbs out of danger and where they need to be. This coupled with the ability to read your opponent allows the wise character to keep from getting hit. This number gets added to all melee defense rolls your character makes.

INITIATIVE

Being able to process any situation quicker is important to staying alive. This number gets added to your initiative rolls at the beginning of combats so lower is better

SKILL MOD

This number represents the bonus you apply to Skill Checks whenever you roll a Skill with this as a listed Stat. Pick the lowest if there are multiple Skills listed.

CONFRONTATION DIE

Sometimes your character’s wisdom can play into social situations, such knowing exactly what to say to a grieving friend. This is the die that gets added to your dice pool for Confrontations if your Wisdom is applicable.

Charisma (Cha) represents force of personality. Does he bend others to his will? Is she the focus of any room she enters? Do people look up to them or what to be him? Charisma is not looks or even likeability: it represents this animal magnetism that people follow.

FAVOR

The gods are fickle creatures, bestowing their gifts on some and their ire on others, and often switch with the seasons, however, charismatic characters tend to do well for themselves.

This is the minimum amount of Favor a person gets whenever they roll to gain Favor. More information about that is found in Chapter 12: The Divine.

START HONOR

Being well thought of allows your character to hold his head high in any situation, giving him the edge. This is your character’s starting Honor. You can find out more in Chapter 6: Character Vitals.

TRAIT POINTS

Characters with strong personalities tend to have a lot of definable qualities that allow them to blend into any social group or a few really strong ones that people seem drawn to. These points are spent increase the number and/or strength of your character’s Traits.

CONTACTS

This is the number of unredeemed contacts a character starts with, reflecting previous relationships he's created before he became an adventurer. More on Contacts and how to redeem them is found in Chapter 7: Skills.

FOLLOWERS

This is the total number of Followers your character has to draw on during his adventuring career. More on Followers is found in Chapter 13: Character Progression.

SKILL MOD

This number represents the bonus you apply to Skill Checks whenever you roll a Skill with this as a listed Stat. Pick the lowest if there are multiple Skills listed.

CONFRONTATION DIE

Sometimes your character’s charisma can play into social situations, such seducing someone. This is the die that gets added to your dice pool for Confrontations if your Charisma is applicable.

Races

Which Race Should I Choose?

Your race effects character creation in 3 ways: Stat Score Modifiers, Gameplay Rewards, and Archetype Costs. If you're new to RPGs in generally, go for a race that interests you based on the flavor.

STAT SCORE MODIFIERS

These modify the base stats that you roll. You can use it to balance out your character's weak spots or you can use it to maximize what your character is already good it. We recommend the latter as Bonfire is a game built around teamwork: you'll have friends who will be good at things your character isn't.

Note that these adjustments can't bring score above 20 or below 1.

GAMEPLAY REWARDS

Each race is meant to encourage a certain type of play. For instance, orcs gain bonuses for starting things, like combats or Confrontations, so they reward players who are aggressive, while elves get rewarded for being careful with how they engage with others. These are noted under the Racial Temperament section in their summary.

ARCHETYPE COSTS

Some races can spend less time mastering things than others, freeing up time (CrP) to focus on other pursuits or becoming true masters of their vocation. This is reflected in the Archetype Costs.

You'll notice that some races will have Archetype Exceptions: these are based on the lore of that race for the Middle Realm, the official campaign setting of Bonfire. GMs should feel free to modify these prices. Actually, GMs should modify any prices to fit their setting.

Racial Preferences

Racial tensions exist in the Middle Realm and there’s bad blood between the different species, plus, some races get on other's nerves because of differing temperaments. When in a Confrontation against some races, you can sometimes gain Leverage to resist (or they get Leverage to convince you).

Racial Preferences
Races Being Judged
Races Judging
DwarfChangelingElfGauntMinotaurHumanOrcRatfolk
DwarfPreferredLikeTolerateTolerateTolerateTolerateToleratePreferred
ChangelingLikePreferredLikeDislikeHatePreferredDislikePreferred
ElfDislikeLikePreferredDislikeLikeTolerateHatePreferred
GauntDislikeLikeLikeTolerateTolerateTolerateToleratePreferred

HumanLikeTolerateLikeDislikeLikePreferredDislikePreferred
OrcHateTolerateDislikeLikeDislikeTolerateDislikePreferred
RatfolkPreferredLikeLikePreferredPreferredPreferredPreferredPreferred

Preferred: 3 points when trying to resist

Like: 1 point when trying to resist

Tolerate: No Bonus

Dislike: 1 point when trying to convince

Hate: 3 points when trying to convince

So, an elf is trying to convince an orc to do something. Orcs dislike elves as a whole: they're effete and cowardly and can be extremely passive-aggressive to an orc, so immediately they start off on the wrong foot, giving the elf 1 point to convince the orc. The elf, realizing that this is going to be harder than it needs to be because of the orcs bullheadedness and general lack of forethought, goes to the his human friend and tries to get him to sign on. Because humans like elves, the human would get an automatic 1 point to be convinced by the elf instead.

Orcs treat their own kin as Preferred for Racial Preferences.

Changelings

Changeling Summary

MODIFIERS

-4 Str

+2 Dex

+3 Int

Small Sized (- 1 ft to Measure, +3 to Melee & Ranged Defense, less movement, and require less food)

Vitality Size Modifier is 10

RACIAL TEMPERAMENT

Crafty

ARCHETYPE COSTS

Expert: 0: Fighter: 15

Servant: 10

Socialite: 5

Weird-Adept: 5

Changelings are strange little beings. The rumors are that their demons who've trade places with human children left out in the wild or that they're the stillborn children of wizards and witches. Either way, their wiliness and technical prowess make them welcome guests where every they end up.

APPEARANCE

Changelings are about the size of a 10-year-old human, with extremely pale skin, unusually long fingers and large eyes. Besides this, they appear like little humans, with wispy hair on their head and face.

They dress in whatever the area custom is but tend towards bright and clashing colors.

PERSONALITY

Changelings are wily and crafty, and, while not lacking in morality, tend to get caught up on whatever project they're currently on. They enjoy puzzles more than anything - the thrill of having everything click into place just perfectly is the finest thing a person can experience.

They also tend to be on the shy side, as much as possible, keeping out of the limelight. Worldly power and accolades hold little appeal for them, but there is a sense of wanting to be apart something greater than keeps them reaching out to the outside world.

Dwarves

Dwarf Summary

MODIFIERS

-3 Dex

+4 Con

-2 Cha

Small Sized (- 1 ft to Measure, +3 to Melee & Ranged Defense, less movement, and require less food)

Vitality Size Modifier is 20

RACIAL TEMPERAMENT

Unconquerable

ARCHETYPE COSTS

Expert: 5: Fighter: 0

Servant: 25

Socialite: 15

Weird-Adept: 25

Dwarves are called the 'Stonemen' not because they're made of stone but because they're hard as rock. They're obstinate and incorrigible and, as a rule, they never do anything that someone else wants them to do. As such, they're the most disagreeable beings in the Middle Realm. They're also the most straightforward, brave, and loyal beings as well.

APPEARANCE

Dwarves are the opposite of elves. They're short, barrel chested with thick hair growing all over their bodies. This hair ranges from coal black to a golden hue, depending on which hold the dwarf hails from. They also always support big bushy beards that are near hard as steel.

These beards are their pride and joy and they take great care in them. Woven into each beard is the tale of that dwarf's life and accomplishments as well as their job within the hold. You can learn a lot from reading a dwarf's beard.

Besides this and their tools, the dwarves really don't take care of themselves, eschewing anything showy or fancy, like nice fabrics or baths.

Dwarf anatomy is, thankfully, a mystery to most outsiders. All dwarves, to other races, appear human and use human pronouns, though in dwarvish, there are no pronouns because that's more bothersome. There is a rumor that there are female dwarves but that there's 0 sexual dimorphism in the species, which makes courting a very careful affair, but the running theory is that female dwarves are just anvils.

PERSONALITY

As stated before, dwarves are stubborn. They're very rarely, however, psychopathically so. More often, once they have decided something, they tend to get defensive and refuse to relent unless they absolutely have to.

This makes dwarven governments and social structures very slow moving and difficult to work with but, it also means that if you get a dwarf to agree with you, they will happily die on that hill.

In fact, the only time that a dwarf seems to be happy is when he's being stubborn about something.

Finally, dwarves do not ascribe to social niceties. It's not that they're incapable to understanding them or aware of them: they just don't think they're worth paying attention to, in the same way that most people don't notice insects.

Elves

Elf Summary

MODIFIERS

-2 Str

-4 Con

+4 Int

+2 Cha

Medium Sized

Vitality Size Modifier is 10

RACIAL TEMPERAMENT

Patient

ARCHETYPE COSTS

Expert: 5: Fighter: 10

Servant: 5

Socialite: 0

Weird-Adept: 0

The Elves are the first born of the Divines. Originally, the inhabitants of the Painted World, the source of all magic, they now inhabit the Middle Realm as mentally ethereal beings.

APPEARANCE

Elves are slender beings that are widely considered classically beautiful, though many find their features alien and off putting. They uniformly have long ears that taper to a point at the end.

Their eyes are pure white, with no iris or pupil visible, this matched with their sharp teeth, can give them a feline turn to their face.

Elves naturally survive off the ebb and flow of magic that drifts through the air of the Painted World. While still present in the Middle Realm, these winds are a sliver of their natural magnitude and so Elves need to find other sources; the main one being through the magic inherent in all living creatures. While vegetables do have magic in them, an Elf would have to consume 100s of pounds of lettuce each day to not die of starvation. The only realistic way of getting enough magic to survive is through the consumption of raw meat.

PERSONALITY

To describe an Elf as “careful” would be a huge understatement. They tend to live longer than other races, not because some supernaturally long lifespan, but because they're always careful about their actions. They see other races as brash and impetuous while they're in turn seen as slow and cowardly.

It's not they're incapable of great emotion or quick action but elves seem to understand that with every action comes a consequence, whether that action was well meaning or not, and that this karmic force is more powerful than any other law or power.

However, once set on a course, it is hard to dissuade an elf, for they do nothing lightly.

Gaunts

Gaunt Summary

MODIFIERS

-2 Str

+2 Dex

-3 Con

-3 Int

+2 Wis

+3 Cha

Medium Sized

Vitality Size Modifier is 10

RACIAL TEMPERAMENT

Salvation Secured

ARCHETYPE COSTS

Expert: 0: Fighter: 0

Servant: 25

Socialite: 0

Weird-Adept: 0

Gaunts are said to be depraved creatures stuck between life and death. They love filthy lucre more than what made them human. They're those that, for whatever reason, have sold part of their souls for either money or at a change at eternal life in the world to come.

APPEARANCE

Gaunts of all races look generally the same as the soul shiving process drains them of their vitality. Their skin turns ghost white, their hair a weak grey, and their eyes become milky as if they're blind. Their bodies becoming desiccated, thin and reedy.

They still need to eat, drink, and do other bodily functions - they are, even after all that, living.

Gaunts tend to dress in flamboyantclothing that is a mix and match of whatever they kind find. Most say this is because they loot the clothing off of those they kill but it's more likely because they just wear what they can find or because they wish to make up for their dull color palette

PERSONALITY

As stated, gaunts get a bad rep for being whollywithout morals but that's not always the case. Some have undergone the process because they need to feed their families or out of a powerful sense of devotion or religious zeal so actually gaunts run the spectrum of personality types: they're just saddled with their reputation because of an admittedly not small section of them.

What makes up the gaunt's personality is why he made the sacrifice to do what he did. Why was so precious to him that he would make such a huge sacrifice for? That's a complicated question and not easy to answer by the gaunt player should have their answer before play begins.

Humans

Human Summary

MODIFIERS

Medium Sized

Vitality Size Modifier is 15

Increase your Honor Dice by 1 size

Your Strong and Medium Traits start out with 1 extra dice

RACIAL TEMPERAMENT

We all have our theories on what personality traits that are shared by the human race, and I'm not interested in wading in on that debate so instead of having a Racial Temperament, they get special modifiers.

ARCHETYPE COSTS

Expert: 0: Fighter: 0

Servant: 0

Socialite: 0

Weird-Adept: 0

Humans are the first natives of the Middle Realm. They are creatures born from strife, who’ve carved for themselves a place in the world through fire, steel, and grit.

APPEARANCE

The Humans of the Middle Realm look like you and me. Their skin, eye, and hair color range widely, adapted to the region of that Human’s origin, with darker skins more common towards the equator.

If you don’t know what a Human looks like, I don’t know what to tell you.

PERSONALITY

The truth is Humans are odd and quirky individuals that seem to have the defining trait of their curiosity and ambition.

Truthfully, you probably have your own opinion about how humans behave and why they behave the way they do and nothing I write in this little blurb is going to convince you otherwise.

Minotaurs

Minotaur Summary

MODIFIERS

+4 Str

-5 Dex

+5 Con

-3 Int

-4 Cha

Large Sized (+ 1 ft to Measure, -3 to Melee & Ranged Defense, more movement, and require more food)

Vitality Size Modifier is 20

RACIAL TEMPERAMENT

Proud

ARCHETYPE COSTS

Expert: 10: Fighter: 0

Servant: 5

Socialite: 15

Weird-Adept: 20

Beastmen are uncivilized creatures of an untamed nature but not Minotaurs. Through the Bonfire they've formed a New Covenant with the Divines, remaking their minds in their image. They were the founders of the First Empire and their legacy is still cleaved to by the kings of the age.

APPEARANCE

Minotaurs are huge creatures that are half man and half bull. Specifically, the head and upper torse, as well as the legs are bull, while the chest, shoulders, and arms are those of a man.

Both male and female are larger than the average person, with males standing on average about 7 ft tall and the woman standing at around 6 ft tall. Males sprout horns, though they lack the strength to effectively gore with them like their bull counterparts.

Their skin color, as well as their fur color and pattern, vary by region, with traditional tanner skinned minotaurs coming from the south and light skinned ones coming from the north but during the days of the First Empire there was so much population movement that this is a trend rather than a rule.

Note that Minotaurs are more closely related to Beastfolk than they are to cows and so are, in fact, carnivorous.

PERSONALITY

Minotaurs cut royal figures and their personalities match. They have an extreme sense of pride and a great depth of feeling in accordance with their bestial nature.

They're extremely devoted to whatever cause they throw their weight behind and there is no difference to them between their opinions and themselves, making them very cocksure. This can, unsurprisingly, make them bullies as they care little for other's opinions about things.

Orcs

Orc Summary

MODIFIERS

+4 Str

+3 Con

-4 Int

-4 Cha

Medium Sized

Vitality Size Modifier is 15

RACIAL TEMPERAMENT

Aggressive

ARCHETYPE COSTS

Expert: 10: Fighter: 0

Servant: 15

Socialite: 20

Weird-Adept: 10

Heirs to a great empire long since lost to the ages, the orcs cling to tradition in the wake of uncertain and dark times. Some say that they value only strength but to truly known an orc is to know the soul of honor.

APPEARANCE

Orcs have dark green or grey skin with porcine nose and tusks that jut up from their lower jaw. They tend to be stocky, with thick muscles and hunched shoulders.

Their hair is wiry, closer to steel wool than anything else and their eyes are completely black, with no pupils or irises, giving them an indescribable inhumanness to it.

Naturally, orcs are scavengers, able to survive on practically anything, no matter how rotten or foul.

PERSONALITY

An orc’s life is defined by struggle: from birth to death, they conceptualize the universe as having a vendetta against them. This can often give them a martyr complex and make them morose traveling companions at times because they feel the weight of the world.

They can also come across as aggressive, which some have pointed out is a defense mechanism, but orcs would simply scoff at that.

There’s nothing an orc values more than their honor and the chance to prove themselves against a worthy foe. This is often seen in their deities across orcish cultures, which are almost exclusively pantheons of their greatest foes. It is taken for granted that you are only as good as your enemies.

Ratfolk

Ratfolk Summary

MODIFIERS

-6 Str

-4 Con

+3 Wis

+5 Cha

Small Sized (- 1 ft to Measure, +3 to Melee & Ranged Defense, less movement, and require less food)

Vitality Size Modifier is 10

RACIAL TEMPERAMENT

Helpful

ARCHETYPE COSTS

Expert: 0: Fighter: 15

Servant: 10

Socialite: 5

Weird-Adept: 5

Ratfolk are social creatures. They love people and being around people. Others find them pleasant to be around. As such, Ratfolk can be found as diplomats, traders, and minstrels .

APPEARANCE

Ratfolk are smaller and slimmer than other races, with lithe, fur covered bodies that range from auburn to dark black. They have beady eyes and long tails. For the most part, they appear like their smaller cousins, though with lighter frames and opposable thumbs.

PERSONALITY

As stated, ratfolk are people people. They're extremely social and, as a rule, are extroverted. They tend to be agreeable and try to get along with everyone but this shouldn't be taken as people pleasing or weak because ratfolk are clever - dangerously so.

People tend to think that because ratfolk are so easy going that they're push overs and that they can be taken advantage of but ratfolk sees it as "I'll scratch your back, you scratch mine" kind of deal so they're not just going to do things to do things. They very much believe in the social contract, but their animal nature makes them ruthless as some points.

In fact, ratfolk can be quite ruthless to those they deem outside their pack, which has earned them some reputation as having a herd mentality. For ratfolk the only war is total war.

Archetypes

Archetypes represent your character’s background training and starting skills and there are two types of Archetypes: Generalist and Specialist.

GENERALIST ARCHETYPES represent the overall theme. For instance, Fighter Archetypes tend to be good at things related to combat. So, if you’re looking to make a combat focused character, you can look there. They are Expert, Weird-Adept, Servant, Socialite, and Fighter. You must pick two starting out.

Generalists will have a wide variety of discounts within their theme that are good for just getting straight bonuses.

SPECIALIST ARCHETYPES represent a more focused version of the Generalist Archetypes. They’re more expensive but come with additional powers. When you purchase a Specialist Archetype, it replaces the Generalist Archetype of the same time. So, for instance, if you’re in Expert, you can replace it with the Ranger or the Thief.

Once you purchase a Specialist Archetype, you are stuck with it.

PURCHASING ARCHETYPES

First choose a Generalist Primary and a Generalist Secondary Archetype and pay the price in CrP for both based on your race.

You use the Vitality Die, the Skills & Trainings, and the Primary Drawback sections from the Primary, and combine both Archetype Abilities sections, though you remove 1 leveling ability from your Secondary Archetype, unless you Double Specialize.

All Generalists, except for the Servant, can be selected as both your Primary and Secondary Archetype, called Double Specializing. So, you can be a Fighter/Fighter but not a Servant/Servant.

The benefits for double specializing will be noted at the end of the Archetype.

If two characters have the same ability, unless it says otherwise, those abilities stack.

PURCHASING SPECIALIST ARCHETYPES At 1st level and at every level up, you can purchase a Specialist Archetype. If at 1st level, see the Specialist Archetypes at 1st Level sidebar below.

You’ll pay an additional 20 CrP for each one you’re replacing regardless.

Unlike Generalists, Weird-Adept Specialist Archetypes that you can double specialize in. So, you can be a Runegalder/Runegalder but not a Cateran/Cateran.

If you choose to double specialize in a Generalist Archetype and then later switch out one of your Archetypes for a Specialist, you retain that double specialist bonus until you swap out the second, but, at that point, if you specialize your secondary Archetype, you'll have to then forfeit an ability.

Your GM may choose to reject an Archetype combination based on the fact that the two Archetypes don’t fit together thematically. So, while a Thief/Priest (Beast Covenant) might be really powerful because of the Beast Covenant’s Shape Changing ability, if there’s not a Patron of Thieves and Animals in the campaign world, you’re out of luck.

Specialist Archetypes completely replaces everything from the Generalist Archetype they’re replacing though it doesn’t retroactively remove things you’ve already rolled for or free purchases.

So, a Fighter, with a d10 Vitality Die decides, at level 4 to become a Soldier with a Vitality Die of a d8. He doesn’t then reroll all his Vitality Die - from that point forward, he simply uses the d8 instead.

Remember that if you’re replacing your Secondary Archetype, you’ll still need to select a leveling ability from your new Archetype to remove.

Specialist Archetypes At 1st Level

If you’re more familiar with the game, your playstyle, and which Archetypes suit you, you might consider purchasing your Specialization(s) at 1st level. That’s perfectly fine, but you’ll still need to pay the CrP for both the Generalist and the Specialist.

You’re considered to have purchased your Generalist Archetype first AND THEN purchased your Specialist, which means that you still get any free stuff from abilities that say "at first level" from your Generalist, so Experts get some free skills and Weird-Adepts get their starting Rudiments.

Your Primary Specialist’s Vitality Die and Primary Drawback also replaces your Primary Generalist’s.

If you’ve already bought a Basic Training that a Specialist comes with, you receive its worth in CrP as a bonus. This doesn’t extend to Skills since their benefits stack.

Expert

Choose this Archetype if you want to use your wits to defeat your opponent or avoid combat altogether.

Experts are those that focus on real-world non-combat skills, as opposed to relying on the Divines, magic, or their sword arm as a source of strength. They tend to rely on Intellect and Wisdom, primarily, though there are Experts that focus on Strength, Dexterity, and Constitution for more physical skills.

VITALITY DIE

d8

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITES Two Different Ones of your Choice

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

SKILL ADEPT This character has a knack for skills. All Advanced Skills have their cost reduced by 1 CrP. They also gain a 10% discount to all Skill Suites. This stacks with other Skill Adepts.

SKILL FOCUS (CHOSEN SKILL SUITE 1, 3) At first level and every level other up, Experts receive 3 free skill purchases. These can be distributed between any Advanced Skills from the first Skill Suite you chose. These free purchases may not be doubled up on in the same level but are applied after Skills have been bought by the character.

SKILL FOCUS (CHOSEN SKILL SUITE 2, 3) At first level and every level other up, Experts receive 3 free skill purchases. These can be distributed between any Advanced Skills from the second Skill Suite you chose. These free purchases may not be doubled up on in the same level but are applied after Skills have been bought by the character.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

None

Expert Double Specialist

SKILL ADEPT

All Advanced Skills are reduced by 3 CrP and you gain a 30% discount to Skill Suites.

SKILL FOCUSES

Both Skill Suites gain an additional 3 free Advanced Skills per level.

Fighter

Choose this Archetype if you want kill monsters and worthy foes in mortal combat and like thinking on your feet.

War is a ladder by which capable people are able to climb the ranks of society. Fighters focus on combat and battle, either by training and discipline or by out maneuvering their opponent. Unsurprisingly, this Archetype focuses on Constitution, but how you approach combat may decide whether you favor Strength, Dexterity, or even Intellect or Wisdom.

VITALITY DIE

d10

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Athletics or Tactics

Fighters gain Weapon Basic Training in 2 weapons and Light Armor Basic Training.

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

IMPROVED ADVANCED TRAINING A Fighter is a master of weaponry and armor, spending years conditioning himself to be able to use the weapons of war in battle without breaking a sweat. All Advanced Training is discounted: Tier 3 by 3, Tier 2 by 2, and Tier 1 by 1.

MARTIAL TRAINING (ARMOR & SHIELDS - TIER 2) A Fighter picks things up as they go, otherwise, they get themselves and their companions killed. At first level and every level she's obtained, a Fighter receives 2 free Tier 2 Armor or Shield Advanced Trainings.

MARTIAL TRAINING (WEAPONS - TIER 2) A Fighter picks things up as they go, otherwise, they get themselves and their companions killed. At first level and every level she's obtained, a Fighter receives 2 free Tier 2 Weapon Advanced Trainings.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

None

Fighter Double Specialist

IMPROVED ADVANCED TRAINING

Each Tier’s discount is increased by 2.

MARTIAL TRAINING (BOTH)

Receive an additional 2 Tier 2 Advanced Trainings.

Servant

Choose this Archetype if you want harness powers beyond the mortal realm to alter the battlefield and circumstances to your favor.

Servants represent those that have devoted themselves to higher causes, lifting their eyes from the Middle Realm to a more pure order, whether that’s the Divines, the Ancestral Spirits, or the Bones of Ymir. Servants play the best with others, often modifying the other Archetype’s powers with Divine assistance.

VITALITY DIE

d6

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITES Trades and Lore

Servants get 3 free purchases of the Religion Advanced Skill for free.

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

CALLED & CHOSEN A Servant seeks to do the will of those who sent them, furthering their agendas in the Middle Realm and so they are blessed. They add their level to their Max Favor.

DEPTHS of DEVOTION A Servant understand the bonds of giving your life to a cause greater than your own and its strengths. They gain a free Devotion to their Divine, starting at 3. They also start Anointed in their cult.

FORMER LIFE A Servant can be called from anywhere and any walk of life. Select any Archetype ability. This can be either from the Generalist you chose as a Secondary or a Specialist within the category to which your Secondary belongs. Former Life has all the same effects as that ability, though it still counts as a separate leveling ability.

This ability stays with you after you replace the Servant Generalist Archetype, however, if it is a leveling ability, it stops leveling, even if your pick the Specialist Archetype it's from.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

None

Socialite

Choose this Archetype if you want to talk your way out of problems and inspire others to give you your way.

Socialites are people people. They seem to get a real kick out of interacting with others, especially if it ends with them getting their way. While others' first weapons are swords, a Socialite's first weapon is their charm. Unsurprisingly, Socialites tend to rely on Intellect and Charisma.

VITALITY DIE

d4

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Streetwise

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

STRONG PERSONALITY As a Socialite grows, she becomes more confident in who she is and what she wants. At 2nd level and every other level after that, a Socialite can increase the strength of one of their Traits by 1 dice (up to a d20) or they save them and cash in two of these increases for a new weak Trait starting at 1d4.

CAMARADERIE A Socialite is able to form quick and powerful bonds with those he is around. At 2nd level and at every other level, the Socialite, or someone he's been traveling with, can either increase the strength of one of their Devotions by 1 or gain a new one at strength 1.

WORK ON YOUR PERSONALITY A Socialite knows that time spent on your personality is never wasted. When increasing Traits through CrP, the Socialite receives a 4 CrP discount.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

None

Socialite Double Specialist

STRONG PERSONALITY

This starts at 1st level and is increased to every level.

CAMARADERIE

This starts at 1st level and is increased to every level.

Weird-Adept

Choose this Archetype if you want an eclectic set of powers that you can apply to most situations in a creative manner but may not be helpful for all problems.

Though much study and/or natural talent, Weird-Adepts can channel the Painted World, using its power to alter reality. Weird-Adepts rely more on clever applications of spells rather than outright doing damage and so can often subtly shift the playing field in their favor. They rely mainly on Intellect and Wisdom since they need a high Stress Threshold as it is extremely stressful to shape Weird.

VITALITY DIE

d4

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Weirdcraft

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

RUDIMENTARY KNOWLEDGE Weird-Adepts know the basics of shaping the Weird and so start out with 5 random Rudiments. They gain a new one every 3rd level.

APPLIED FOLKWEIRD While anyone can shape a simple cantrip, the Weird-Adepts knows how to apply those lessons to shape a real spell. After 10 seconds of concentration, the Weird-Adept generates a number of Spell Points equal to their Level + Weirdcraft Skill Suite Rank + applicable Weirdcraft Advanced Skill's Rank.

They receive the normal Fallout from shaping.

SKILL FOCUS (Weirdcraft Skill Suite) At first level and every level other up, Weird-Adept receive 1 free skill purchase in the Weirdcraft Skill Suite.

SKILL FOCUS (Weirdcraft, 2) At first level and every level other up, Weird-Adept receive 2 free skill purchases. These can be distributed between any Advanced Skills from the Weirdcraft Skill Suite. These free purchases may not be doubled up on in the same level but are applied after Skills have been bought by the character.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

None

Weird-Adept Double Specialist

RUDIMENTARY KNOWLEDGE

Start with 9 Rudiments, with 2 being your choices and the rest random. Gain a new one every other level.

APPLIED FOLKWEIRD

Shape after 7 seconds of concentration and gain SPs equal to twice your level + Weirdcraft Skill Suite Rank + applicable Weirdcraft Advanced Skill's Rank.

SKILL FOCUSES

You get these are every level up, instead of every other.

Adventurer

Choose this Archetype if you want a good range of skills and be able to help others in Skill Challenges.

Adventures gain the most free skills of all Archetypes allowing for the largest breathe of knowledge, however, they’re cheaper skills. They can also help others, giving them a chance to try again at Skill Checks they fail.

VITALITY DIE

d8

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITES Two Different, non-Lore Skill Suites

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

HELPING HAND The Adventurer is not just about knowing things but also giving others a helping hand in times of need. When another person uses an Adventurer’s help, either as an Asset, or one of his Helper Skills or Preparation, they receive an additional +1 to their roll. This bonus increases by +1 for every 2 levels the Adventurer has obtained.

MIDDLE NAME: DANGER For the Adventurer, danger is calming and straightforward and that’s what they crave. Whenever an Adventurer takes damage, they can heal that amount of Stress.

OUTTHINKING While they may not be the best with the blade, the Adventurer is often able to beat their opponents by outthinking them. Gain a use of your Honor dice whenever you use a Skill in combat, regardless of whether or not its successful. Gain an additional one for every 3 levels you've obtained.

SKILL FOCUS (Any < 7 CrP, 7) At first level and every level up, Adventurers receive 7 free skill purchases. These can be distributed between any Advanced Skills under 7 CrP in base cost (before Skill Adept). These free purchases may not be doubled up on in the same level but are applied after Skills have been bought by the Character.

SKILL ADEPT This character has a knack for skills. All Advanced Skills have their cost reduced by 1 CrP. They also gain a 10% discount to all Skill Suites. This stacks with other Skill Adepts.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

Adventurers tend to eschew book smarts for street smarts: the Lore Skill Suite and any Lore Advanced Skills cost double.

Assassin

Choose this Archetype if you want to dispatch unaware opponents quickly, either by stabbing your target in the back, by poisoning them, or by slitting their throats.

The Assassin is a master killer, gaining a chance to increase their damage against unaware opponents and being able silence helpless ones quickly. They're also masters of poison use, knowing how to most effectively apply their killer medicine.

VITALITY

d4

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Streetwise

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

BACKSTAB When using any small melee weapon against an unaware target (one that is either not aware of your presence or one that is unaware that you, personally, mean harm to them), the Assassin’s weappon's base damage explodes on the highest and second highest result. i.e., d4!s explode on natural 3s and 4s. They also gain an additional dice of damage at 1st level and every 2 levels after that when backstabbing, which doesn’t increase the total number of dice for /D armor but isn't effected by anything that would otherwise increase the weapon's damage.

If an opponent flees and the Assassin is within half their weapon Recovery, they may Backstab using half their additional damage dice from this ability, rounded up. This, however, he can do with any weapon (althougth he'll need to snapshot his attack if using a ranged weapon unless he attacks the same second they flee).

SILENT TAKEDOWN If an Assassin attacks an unaware opponent with any weapon and beat his victim's defense by more than 10, the attack has the opportunity to be silent. If the victim fails their Trauma check, they simply keel over quietly its duration, after which, they can get up and start yelling (should the Assassin have left them alive).

If, however, the Assassin beats their defense by 10 but their victim succeeds at their Trauma check, the Assassin has still managed to silence them for 3d6! seconds, however their victim isn't helpless and attack otherwise act normally.

IMPROVED COUP de GRACE An Assassin has studied the weak parts of their target’s anatomy and can quickly make a killer strike. Coup de Graces only take 5 seconds. This is always done completely silent.

COOL HEADED Where others would get blustered, the Assassin stays cool, even when he’s stressing. When making a Skill Check, lower the base amount of Stress you get by 2.

SKILLED POISONER An Assassin has intimate knowledge of poisons and how to use them. When someone is poisoned by the Assassin, increase that poison's Lethality by 1 for every level that Assassion has obtained.

If the first roll against the poison is greater than 10, the poison has been so artfully placed that it also silences the victim, only a success allows them to cry out.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

Being a trained killer is not an honorable profession and people don’t like murders around. If your profession becomes publicly known, you lose 5 Honor.

Mastermind

Choose this Archetype if you want to beat Skill Challenges more through use of Strategies rather than raw Ranks in a Skill.

The Mastermind is a plotter: preparing themselves and laying out plans before they step foot into the Skill Challenge. They get bonuses for utilizing all the options presented in the Strategies section, meaning that, by the time they step into the ring, they’re unbeatable in their element.

VITALITY DIE

d6

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE One of your Choice

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

FRIENDS in ALL PLACE A Mastermind has contacts and knows how to use them. When using an Asset, the Mastermind gains a +1 at first level and increases it by 1 for every level they’ve obtained.

MANAGE MINIONS Any Mastermind worth his salt will keep a stable of minions around to help him out, even if they're the other players. When he uses one of their Skills, or vice versa, as a Helper Skill, the Stress gain is halved.

PREP PAYS OFF People take pride in having their plans work out, the Mastermind doubly so. Whenever a reroll from Preparation results in a success when the original roll would have caused a failure, the Mastermind receives 1 free use of their Honor Die for the rest of the Skill Challenge.

The RIGHT TOOL for the RIGHT TIME If you’re careful with how you treat your equipment and come prepared, you can see yourself through a tough spot. Once per Skill Challenge and an additional time for every 2 levels they’ve obtained, ignore the degradation of a piece of equipment you use on a Check.

SKILL FOCUS (Any, 3) At first level and every level other up, Masterminds receive 3 free skill purchases. These can be distributed between any Advanced Skill. These free purchases may not be doubled up on in the same level but are applied after Skills have been bought by the Character.

SKILL ADEPT This character has a knack for skills. All Advanced Skills have their cost reduced by 1 CrP. They also gain a 10% discount to all Skill Suites. This stacks with other Skill Adepts.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

Failure means that the Mastermind didn’t plan as well as he should have. He gains an additional 2d6! Stress at the end of any Skill Challenge for each Obstacle that he fails, even if he got what he wanted out of the Challenge.

Opportunist

Choose this Archetype if you want to play a lucky character who can alter the unexpected to be in his favor.

There’s just something about these types of people that seem to warp probability in their favor. And those lucky few who use this to their advantage to go far.

VITALITY DIE

the higher of 2d6

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE According to your Secondary Archetype

Opportunists gain any free Skills & Trainings from their Secondary Archetype.

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

LUCKY The Opportunist is naturally blessed with the ability to get out of trouble and use that adrenaline that comes as death comes near to dodge the grim reaper and keep running. After the results are given, the Opportunist can take 2 Stress to modify his results by 1. These may be done with the following conditions:

  • They can never be used to make you a better fighter. Stress gained this way can only be used to dodge death or escape a bad situation but never to make your character a superman.
  • The character must think of a situation that saves his rear end, something that happens to him that’s to his advantage.

The key here is that it can’t be impossible but it can be highly improbable. The chandelier rope breaking right at that moment separating him from a blood thirsty guard, a pigeon flying across an archer’s view intercepting an arrow, etc. are all acceptable.

It can’t be the result of skill. Him deflecting the blade with his hand like a badass is right out.

Should the character be unable to think of a scenario that fits both of these criteria, he’s unable to gain Stress to save himself.

FALL FORWARD Some people seem to stubble into where they need to be, even when they completely fail. When the Opportunist fails a Check, takes damage, or loses a round, he gains a roll of his Honor Dice. This is limited to 1 initially (so failing a second roll won't do him any good at level 1), but for every 3 levels the Opportunist has obtained, he increases the max number of Honor Dice this ability gives him by 1.

NATURAL ADVANTAGE An Opportunist lives on his wits and his ability to use every advantage. At the start of every Combat, Confrontation, or Skill Challenge, he may change one thing about the field for every 5 Stress he takes. These changes must be consistent with an overarching setting (he can’t choose to have the inn change to a ship or flood right at that moment but he can choose to have a convenient chair or barrel right behind one of his enemies or reposition himself next to the fighter).

This Stress is lowered by 1 for every other level he’s obtained, down to 3, though he may use this ability multiple times, but it doubles the Stress penalty each time he does so. This resets the next time he has the opportunity to heal Stress.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

Luck is a top-heavy thing: Opportunists don’t get their Vitality reroll every other level, however, they do get bumped up to their Min. Vitality from their Constitution if they’re below it.

Professional

Choose this Archetype if you want to play a character that gets stronger as they fail to overcome Obstacles.

While other Experts focus on knowledge, the Professional focuses on when to apply that knowledge and how to use their time effectively. The work with the Clocks of the Skill Challenge primarily, rather than being just good at Skill Checks.

VITALITY DIE

d6

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE One of your Choice

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

UNDER PRESSURE When times get tough, the tough get going and the Professional is tough. When you or an ally hard fails an Obstacle, you gain an additional use of your Honor Die for the remainder of the Challenge. This increases by 1 Honor Die for every level you’ve obtained.

BUYING TIME The sands of the hourglass trickle onward but sometimes you can slow it down for a moment or two. During a Skill Challenge on a failed Check, for each point of Honor you spend to modify the roll, increase your roll by 2 instead. This can’t, however, turn the failure into a success so if you intend to change failure into success, you don't gain this benefit.

WATCHING EACH OTHER’S BACK Whenever one does their job, everyone can rest easy. If two or more allies are Multitasking, they both get a +1 to one of their rolls for every 2 levels the Professional has obtained.

SKILL FOCUS (Any, 3) At first level and every level other up, Professional receive 3 free skill purchases. These can be distributed between any Advanced Skill. These free purchases may not be doubled up on in the same level but are applied after Skills have been bought by the Character.

SKILL ADEPT This character has a knack for skills. All Advanced Skills have their cost reduced by 1 CrP. They also gain a 10% discount to all Skill Suites. This stacks with other Skill Adepts.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

The Professional is a man of reputation and so, when it is besmirched, it affects him gravely. For every 5 Honor you lose, lose an additional 1.

Ranger

Choose this Archetype if you want to have a good range of survival skills, use your team to overcome Obstacles, but also move quicker on and off the battlefield.

The Ranger’s strengths rely mostly in their survival skills, making them excellent to have in the wilderness but they also gain a bonus to their movement that allows them to out-pace others during skirmishes.

VITALITY DIE

d8

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Survival

ARCHETYPES ABILITIES

QUICK FOOTED The Ranger relies on being able to cross great swaths of land quickly, chasing down their prey. At first level and for every 2 levels he’s obtained, the Ranger increases his base movement rate categories by 1 foot. He can't increase it again until all other movement categories have been increased in a like manner.

A first level Ranger can choose Stroll/Crawling, Walking, Jogging, Running, Sprinting. If he chooses Walking, his Walk becomes 6 ft / second. At level 3, he can choose Strolling/Crawling, Jogging, Running, or Sprinting, but not Walking. After he's increased all by 1 ft, he can go back and increase his Walk again.

PUT YOUR HEADS TOGETHER For survival, communication is key and doing so quickly is often extremely important. When using each other as Assets, all allies of the Ranger have their Organization considered 1 better.

HIKING CONDITIONING A Ranger is used to running and jumping for hours on end with equipment on their back so gain a +1S to their Carry for every 2 levels obtained.

SKILL FOCUS (Survival, 5) At first level and every level up, Rangers receive 5 free skill purchases. These can be distributed between any Advanced Skills from the Survival Skill Suite. These free purchases may not be doubled up on in the same level but are applied after Skills have been bought by the Character.

SKILL ADEPT This character has a knack for skills. All Advanced Skills have their cost reduced by 1 CrP. They also gain a 10% discount to all Skill Suites. This stacks with other Skill Adepts.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

A Ranger finds armor restricting and irritating: all Armor Advanced Trainings are 2 CrP more expensive per Tier (Tier 1: 11 CrP, Tier 2: 16 CrP, Tier 3: 22 CrP).

Sage

Choose this Archetype if you want to play an extremely knowledge person as well as use that knowledge to give bonuses to your company.

The Sage gets some of the most expensive and cerebral skills for free but also, because of his intense training, he has the ability to instantly reroll any skill he chooses.

VITALITY DIE

d4

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITES Lore Twice

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

MEMORY TRAINING The Sage’s training doesn’t just revolve around studying but also on how to study, allowing them better recall of information than those without such mental discipline. The Sage may reroll 1 Int, Wis, or Cha based Skill Check for 7 Stress. They may do this multiple times but each time they do so between opportunities where they can heal Stress costs them double, however, they also lower this Stress gain by 1 for every 3 levels they’ve obtained, down to 3.

FRANK DISCUSSION You can often get more out of a discussion than you can simply thinking about something. When used as an Asset, the person receives a +1 to their Skill Check and an additional +1 for every 3 levels the Sage has obtained.

SKILL FOCUS (Lore, 5) At first level and every level up, Sages receive 5 free skill purchases. These can be distributed between any Advanced Skill from the Lore Skill Suite. These free purchases may not be doubled up on in the same level but are applied after Skills have been bought by the Character.

SKILL ADEPT This character has a knack for skills. All Advanced Skills have their cost reduced by 1 CrP. They also gain a 10% discount to all Skill Suites. This stacks with other Skill Adepts.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

The Sage has spent most of his time buried in study and so may take a bit longer to react to reality: they always roll an initiative die 1 size larger.

Thief

Choose this Archetype if you want to play an expert in stealth and intelligence gathering.

The Thief has the widest variety of skills, picking from a uniquely built suite, rather than a predetermined one on top of their other free skills.

VITALITY DIE

d4

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Streetwise

Thieves receive 3 free purchases of Language (Thieves Cant).

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

THIEF’S TRAINING At first level and every 2 levels they obtain, the Thief receives 4 free purchases in Advanced Skill from the list found below. This can be doubled up into a single skill or spread between any number of them.

Thief's Training Skills

A thief may choose from the following skills:

- Any One Selected At First Level: - Hiding

- Appraisal (Specific): - Law (Culture)

- Climbing: - Move Silently

- Distraction: - Scavenging

- Escape Artist

BROTHER/SISTERHOOD When you know others have your back and you have theirs, it’s much easier to keep your calm. Everyone within sight (or other form of communication) of the thief increases their Stress Threshold by 5. This bonus increases by 1 for every 2 levels the Thief has obtained.

SKILL FOCUS (Streetwise, 3) At first level and every level up, Thieves receive 3 free skill purchases. These can be distributed between any Advanced Skill from the Streetwise Skill Suite. These free purchases may not be doubled up on in the same level but are applied after Skills have been bought by the Character.

SKILL ADEPT This character has a knack for skills. All Advanced Skills have their cost reduced by 1 CrP. They also gain a 10% discount to all Skill Suites. This stacks with other Skill Adepts.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

Thieving is not an Honorable profession. A Thief loses 5 Honor should their profession become publicly known.

Wilderman

Choose this Archetype if you want to play a pioneer or trapper, raised by wild animals but with a kinship to the same.

The Wilderman is a savage by most standards. They tend to be those raised in the wild by feral creatures, or those mountain men that retreated to the frontier so long ago that they’ve lost the rounded edges that civilization originally bestowed on them.

VITALITY DIE

d12

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Survival Twice

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

ANIMAL AFFINITY The Wilderman has a natural connection to the beasts. As such, he can form bonds with them quicker than humans. A Wilderman can use one of his followers at any time to attract an environmentally appropriate animal companion instead.

You may never gain more than 1 animal companion at one time.

ENVIRONMENTAL CONDITIONING Being outside in all seasons and weather, hardens the Wilderman. He considers himself up to 40 degrees warmer or colder than the surrounding climate.

ONE PACK The Wilderman knows that you either survive together or die separately. Anyone can use anyone else’s Honor Dice; however they take Stress equal to what they roll on it.

ANIMAL FRIEND Being around animals allows you to really get in their head and communicate with them on a level that civilized people just can't. This ability allows the Wilderman to get into a Confrontation with any Natural Animals to move their disposition from Hostile to Neutral or from Neutral to Friendly, though not from Hostile to Neutral in one Confrontation. This is only temporary, however, ending a few hours after first contact.

SAVAGE MAN in a SAVAGE LAND A Wilderman is used to fighting in all conditions, good or bad. They gain a +1 to their Checks when they're suffering from penalties from terrain or weather. This increases by 1 for every 2 levels they've obtained.

SKILL FOCUS (Survival Skill Suite) At first level and every level up, Wildermen receive a free purchase in the Survival Skill Suite.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

A Wilderman finds no comfort in society and they often find themselves ill-at-ease in the company of others: all races are considered 2 steps down the Racial Preference table.

Barbarian

Choose this Archetype if you want to play a cunning fighter that uses combat Tactics to best your opponent, rather than raw skill.

“Barbarian” is often a derogatory term used by people who consider themselves civilized but the truth is that the Barbarian is a title of honor. The Barbarian is a survivor and survives on wit, rather than raw power.

VITALITY DIE

d10

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Survival

Barbarians also gain Armor Basic Training (Light) and 3 Weapon Basic Trainings, 1 for a 2 handed weapon, a ranged weapon, and small weapon

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

ADVANCED TACTICS A Barbarian is a skirmisher and doesn’t rely on formalized training methods like other fighters. As such, their greatest strength is the utilization of Tactics. At 1st level and at every 2nd level after that, a Barbarian can increase the bonus or lower the penalty for a Tactic by 1, though they can never make a penalty a bonus nor go beyond double a bonus’s original amount. So, the max you can get the Faint to is +10 to Attack and +0 to your Defense.

This doesn't remove requirements (such as moving) or special penalties (such as dealing half damaged while Feinting against people who Step Back or Retreat).

TRIBAL WEAPONRY Trained from birth with tribal weapons, the Barbarian thinks of disparate weapons all as extensions of his arm. At 1st level, the Barbarian picks a 2 handed weapon, a ranged weapon, and a small weapon. All these weapons are considered 1 group: any Advanced Training purchased for one of them is applied to every other weapon. They’re considered Tier 2 for price.

CONSTANT VIGILANCE Pay attention or end up as monster chow. Everyone receives a -1 to their Initiative for every 5 levels the Barbarian has obtained

HIKING CONDITIONING A Barbarian is used to running and jumping for hours on end with equipment on their back so gain a +1S to their Carry for every 2 levels obtained.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

Barbarians haven’t benefited fully from the learning of more advanced civilizations. All Skills with Int as a relevant ability cost 2 CrP more.

Berserker

Choose this Archetype if you want to play a warrior that charges into battle and gets stronger the more wounded they become.

The Berserker is a child of war, often raised from an early age in the most punishing conditions to harden them. In battle they fly into a primal rage, craving through enemies like warm butter.

VITALITY DIE

higher of 2d12

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE None

Berserkers receive 1 Weapon Basic Training.

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

PAIN TOLERANT The Berserker has learned to simply overpower his pain sensors and keep fighting. At 1st level, he gains a + 3 bonus to his Trauma check. This increased by 1 for every 2 levels he's obtained.

AGGRESSIVE FIGHTER The Berserker never backs down. In a Morale Confrontation, they can never be forced to take a defensive action.

SCARIFICATION For every battle and victim, the Berserker scars himself to commemorate his victory. Over time, these scars serve as armor as his skin hardens. The Berserker gains 1 DR at first level and for every 4 levels obtained. Against a weapon, use whichever is highest (whether it’s the /D or static DR). This ability does stack with armor but the scars chaff and rub, so double any penalties gained from wearing it.

This scarification is unsettling to look upon. The Berserker also gains a 2d8 Trait “Intimidating Presence” because of them. This is separate from the Trait “Battle Scars”.

BATTLE FRENZY These warriors are able to drive themselves into a crazed frenzy, giving them almost supernatural abilities. While in a Battle Frenzy, the Berserker doubles his bonuses from Pain Tolerant and Scarification and makes them temporarily immune to penalties from Stress, though they still gain Stress from Wounds as per normal.

The DR granted from Scarification also applies to the damage dealt by Running and Sprinting, however, it is effectively halved for Sprinting.

On top of this, whenever they kill an opponent, they heal an amount of damage equal to the amount under 0 he puts them. So, a Berserker deals 10 damage to a person with 6 Vitality left, bringing the enemy to -4 and healing the Berserker 4 Vitality.

The Battle Frenzy increases as the warrior nears death. When a Berserker is Hurt they gain an additional dice of damage equal to their Honor Die and when Wounded they gain another. This doesn't increase the effective dice number.

There are drawbacks to the Frenzy. The first is that the Berserker can take no defensive actions. This includes any defensive Tactics but also prevents him from actively crouching behind his shield for cover and, when doing aggressive actions, they are less careful, doubling their penalties from the same. Additionally, there is a price to pay for driving your body for so long; when you drop out of the Frenzy, you take enough damage, on one Wound, to drop you another Wound Category. You also gain no benefits from Taking a Breather after doing so until you drop another Wound Category (so you can't just heal it back up, sorry).

This Frenzy is awoken by the Berserker and takes 3d6 seconds to get into, during which time the Berserker beats his chest, screams at the sky, and just generally psyches himself up. The more wounded the Berserker becomes, however, the easier it is to get into the right frame of mind, so remove a d6 for every Wound Category he has dropped.

SHARED FRENZY Some of the manic power the Berserker commands overflows and invigorates his allies. Those on the Berserker’s side can Run for an additional 3 seconds per Berserker level and can Sprint an additional 1 second per Berserker level without taking damage or increasing that Running and Sprinting damage dice.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

Berserkers are killers and can sometimes get lost in the glory of battle. After downing every foe on the battlefield, they need to make a Wisdom check. On a failure, they’re unable to calm down and attack the nearest person, friendly or not. After every attack they make, they can make another Wis check to try and snap out of it. Failure indicates they keep attacking.

Brawler

Choose this Archetype if you want to play a streetbrawler that can grab, disarm, shift, and trip your opponent to your heart's pleasure.

On the streets or in the arena, you’ll find the Brawler, battling it out. For the joy of throwing their opponents around like a rag doll, they fight. Brawlers are unarmed fighters primarily, eager to toss anyone that opposes them aside.

VITALITY DIE

d12

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Streetwise

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

REGISTERED WEAPONS The Brawler knows how to appear like a threat, even when unarmed. They always count as having a weapon for Weapon Style.

IMPROVED ADVANCED TRAINING Brawlers train to be deadly artists with their fists and soon gain a knack for it. For Brawlers, Unarmed Advanced Trainings have a Base Cost of 5.

MARTIAL TRAINING A Brawler receives a free Weapon Advanced Training for Unarmed Combat for every level he’s obtained.

OPPORTUNISTIC FIGHTER Part of being a streetfighter is seizing every chance you get to get ahead. A Brawler and his allies score a Near Perfect Attack and Defense on a roll of 18 and 19.

IMMOVABLE By planting yourself and watching your structure, you can really push people around. You gain an effective + 1 to your Vitality Size Modifier for Knock-Backs. On top of this, you lower your enemy's Vitality Size Modifier by 1 for Knock-Backs as well. This bonus increased by 1 every level.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

Something about being a Brawler makes them shun weapons where they can’t get up and personal with their opponent. Ranged Weapon Advanced Trainings cost 2 CrP more.

Cateran

Choose this Archetype if you want to play a fighter that flanks their opponent, keeping them from moving or engaging others in combat.

The Cateran is all about flanking your opponent and keeping other fighters locked down. As such, they work best with other fighters.

VITALITY DIE

d8

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Tactics Twice

Caterans receives 1 Weapon Basic Training.

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

BABY-SITTING While an individual Cateran may vary in his ability to take care of infants, they all share the ability to keep combatants locked down.

Whenever a person engaged with the Cateran tries to disengage, the Cateran gets an immediate free attack that, if it hits, deals half damage. This happens regardless of where they are on the Clock and doesn’t affect when their next attack happens.

CLOSED OPENINGS Flanking is the art of dividing people’s attention and the Cateran has perfected that art. Anyone flanked by a Cateran lowers their attack die by 1 size, regardless of who they’re attacking.

MUTIEREN A Cateran knows to move their blade to get into places their opponents wouldn't expect. If facing an enemy whose weapon has a base Parry or who is carrying a shield, the Cateran receives a +1 to Attack +1 for every 2 levels they've obtained. This ability isn't effective against people who gained their Parry solely through training.

SHADOWING By keeping close to their opponent, the Cateran can negate people’s defensive posturing. By taking 7 Stress, a Cateran can negate any bonuses an opponent gets from moving, whether that’s shifting, stepping back, or whatever and also stops their opponent from moving.

The Cateran can do this as many times as they want but the Stress cost doubles each time they do so, though this resets once they’ve had time to destress. Also, this Stress cost is lowered by 1 for every 3 levels they’ve obtained, down to 3 Stress.

BUM RUSH A Cateran can also use his allies to more effectively flank their opponents. When flanking from the side, you and your allies lower your target’s defense die by 1, including the dice of those using shields (though they still get a chance to Parry). This doesn’t, however, give you any benefit for attacking from directly behind.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

The Cateran is a group fighter and fighting alone can be unnerving for him. When engaged with enemies alone and not flanking, the Cateran is unable to use his Honor.

Man-at-arms

Choose this Archetype if you want to play someone who uses their Advanced Trainings to gain even greater bonuses agains their opponents.

The Man-at-Arms uses his own know-how against his opponents. She gets more deadly the more Advanced Trainings she gains. With this she can adapt to who she is fighting where others can’t.

VITALITY DIE

d10

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Athletics

The Man-at-Arm receives 3 free Weapon Basic Training Trainings.

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

KNOW YOUR ENEMY A Man-at-Arms is good at watching her foe and exploiting weaknesses. For every 20 seconds she is either Threatening someone or someone is Threatening her, she gains a cumulative bonus to Attack, Defense, Recovery, or Damage. This bonus, and what she can choose to apply it to is based on her Advanced Trainings in the weapon, armor, or shield the opponent is using.

Tier 3 gives her a +1, Tier 2 gives her a +2, and Tier 1 gives her a +3. She can only apply this bonus to a metric she has an Advanced Training Bonus in.
