So, for example, if she is fighting someone with a slashing sword and she has a +1 to Attack and Defense with all Slashing weapons (Tier 2), that means, for every 20 seconds she is fighting that person, she can add an additional +2 to her Attack or Defense.

This bonus is applied to one metric per person and everything resets should that foe become completely unengaged with her. So, if the Man-At-Arms is Threatening two foes for 20 seconds, she can apply her bonus to attacking one, while the other bonus goes to defending against another. If one she is defending against leaves, she has to continue applying her bonus to attacking the other. Should that foe threaten her again, she gains no bonuses again him but can change to attacking him as well.

The time it takes to accrue this bonus is lowered 1 second for level the Men-at-Arms obtains, down to a minimum 1 second.

COUNTING COUP Part of being a Man-at-Arms is keeping a reputation for your skill in combat and this can often become a game that everyone gets caught up in. If you give yourself a penalty to Attack, you gain 1 Honor and gain Relaxation equal to that penalty if you score a hit. If you've already used this ability once this Combat, your allies may do so as well, gaining an additional point of Relaxation (but not Honor) for each teammate who's successfully couted coup before them.

MARTIAL TRAINING A Man-at-Arms receives his choice of a free Tier 2 or 3 Armor, Shield, or Weapon Advanced Training for every levels he's obtained.

IMPROVED ADVANCED TRAINING A Man-at-Arms studies the greatest weapon, armor, and shield techniques to pick them up easier. For them, Tier 1 Weapon, Shield, Armor Advanced Training has a Base Cost of 7, Tier 2 has a Base Cost of 8, and Tier 3 a Base Cost of 10.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

Men-at-Arms fight and when they lose, it’s hard on them: they lose 5 Honor for every combat they’re knocked unconscious or fail a Trauma check in due to humiliation.

Knight

Choose this Archetype if you want to play a heavy armored tank that inspires others to fight hard.

The Knight focuses on shield and armor, and with their larger Vitality Die, they tend to be pretty tanky. Additionally, their Inheritance allows them to get the more expense weapons for free.

VITALITY DIE

d12

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Tactics

Knights receive the Armor Basic Training (Heavy), Shield Basic Training, and 1 Weapon Basic Training for free.

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

IMPROVED ADVANCED TRAINING A Knight is a master of armor and defense, spending years conditioning himself to be able to wear armor and use a shield without breaking a sweat. For Knights Tier 1 Armor and Shield Advanced Training has a Base Cost of 7, Tier 2 has a Base Cost of 8 and Tier 3 a Base Cost of 10.

CHIVALRY From their strict code comes a strength and confidence that others can only dream of and envy. For the duration of a combat, you gain 1 free use of your Honor Die. You gain an additional free Honor Die for every level you obtain. You can only apply 1 of these bonus Honor Die to a single roll, though that doesn’t stop you adding Honor Dice that you’ve gotten from other sources.

CALL to VALOR A Knight is a hero and inspires others to rise above. For the duration of a combat all allies gain 1 free use of an Honor Die to share between them. They gain an additional free Honor Die for every 4 levels you’ve obtained. They can only apply 1 of these bonus Honor Dice to a single roll, though that doesn’t stop them adding Honor Dice that they got from other sources, and the Honor Dice is the size of the person’s Honor Dice that redeems it.

INHERITANCE This character may have had an extra leg up in life, allowing them the opportunity to start with better equipment than others. They gain a free weapon of their choice or a Courser mount and also gain 15 sc for each CrP cashed in at the end of Character Creation.

MARTIAL TRAINING A Knight receives a free Tier 2 Armor or Shield Advanced Training for every level she’s obtained.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

The Knight is a creature of Honor and respects Honor where they find it. They may be killers, but they have a code, whether articulated or not. A Knight may never use a long-ranged weapon on a foe that has greater than Average Honor.

Skirmisher

Choose this Archetype if you want to play an extremely mobile guerilla fighter that gains bonuses for ambushing.

Skirmishers never stay in one place longer than they have to and so are rewarded for constantly being on the move. They’re also adept at making the most of their enemies' disorientation, either from surprise or from the chaos they cause.

VITALITY DIE

d6

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Athletics

Skirmishers gain 1 Basic Weapon Training for free. They also gain 4 free purchases in the Endurance Advanced Skill

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

DIRE AMBUSH Catching an enemy off guard can spread confusion and disorientation that can limit an enemy’s ability to respond. Whenever the Skirmisher hits a surprised enemy, that enemy receives -2 to Attack and Defense for the next 7 seconds. Additionally, should they move above a Walk during this time, they gain an additional -2 for each Movement Category above such for that duration.

COMBAT READY A Skirmisher is ready to go at any time. They lower their Initiative Dice down by 1 size per level they’ve obtained, down to a d2.

ATTACK on the RUN Skirmishers have a special gift when it comes to aiming and moving. Instead of lowering their Attack Dice by 2 per Movement Category when using ranged weapons, they lower it by 1 per Movement Category instead.

GUERILLA FIGHTING Skirmishers are masters at getting in, doing some damage, and getting out, causing confusion as they move.

If someone attacks the Skirmisher while she is at a Jog or higher, or misses an attack when she disengages with someone, the enemy is left open for two seconds. If hit within that window, then the enemy receives a -3 to Attack for 7 seconds + 1 every level.

RAID TACTICS Confusion allows those to dart in and out, dealing terrible damage. While receiving penalties from the Skirmisher, enemies are unable to capitalize and get no free attacks when someone disengaged with them.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

The Skirmisher moves and so quickly loses her edge when pinned down. She receives a -2 for every 5 seconds she hasn’t moved at least 5 ft in combat.

Soldier

Choose this Archetype if you want to play a warrior that sticks close to the rest of the company and allows them to adapt more quickly to changing situations.

Bonfire character are not meant to stand alone, and this goes double for the Soldier, who work the best with others. They’re able to shadow others around the battlefield and really focus on being good at one or two weapons.

VITALITY DIE

d8

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Tactics

Soldiers receive either the Armor Basic Training (Light) and Shield Basic Training or Armor Training (Medium). On top of this, they gain 1 Weapon Basic Training for free as well.

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

SMALL UNIT TACTICS Soldiers work as a team. If they or anyone they’re adjacent uses a tactic that moves them (Shift, Step Back, etc.), the Soldier or their adjacent ally may also use that Tactic with no penalties.

IMPROVED ADVANCED TRAINING Soldiers rely on others to make up for their weaknesses, as such, that gives them greater freedom to really specialize in what they’re good at. For Soldiers Tier 1 Weapon Advanced Training have a Base Cost of 6.

BUDDY SYSTEM Soldiers fight as a unit, moving and acting as one where possible. When an adjacent ally switches Tactics, the Soldier may immediately switch to that Tactic as well. On top of this, they also receive a +1 to their Trauma Threshold, which increased by 1 for every level the soldier has obtained

MARTIAL TRAINING A Soldier receives a free Tier 1 Weapon Advanced Training for every level he’s obtained.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

A Soldier focuses so much time drilling with his preferred weapon that he can often forget that principles with one weapon can apply to another. All Tier 3 Weapon Advanced Trainings are 2 CrP more expensive.

Tactician

Choose this Archetype if you want to play someone that is extremely versatile, being able to switch weapons, weapon styles, and tactics on the fly, as well as gaining a greater benefit from resting.

The Tactician is a jack of all trades but master of none, focusing on being slightly less skilled at a multitude of weapons. This means that the Tactician will probably have the right weapon for the right enemy. On top of this, the Tactician is skilled at the use of Combat Tactics (hence the name) which allows them to seize opening that others can’t. Overall, the Tactician focuses on versatility.

VITALITY DIE

d8

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Tactics

Tacticians receive the Armor Basic Training (Medium) and 2 Weapon Basic Trainings for free.

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

QUICK OR DEAD A Tactician lives on his wits. While others rely on training, he works on instinct and so can often take advantage of situations that others can’t. By taking 5 Stress, this ability allows the Tactician to change his Combat Tactic, Weapon Style, weapon he is using, regardless of where he is on the Clock or whether or not the dice have been rolled.

He must qualify for the Tactic to use it (so he can’t suddenly Charge if he’s not already at a Run). If you chose to swap out weapons, he is never counted as unarmed, it happens, for all intents and purposes instanteously, and he doesn't need to wait his weapon speed for his next attack - he simply waits the difference between their Recoveries (down to a minimum of 0 seconds).

You can use this ability multiple times, however its Stress price doubles each time you do it between periods of Relaxation, but the Stress it inflicts is lowered by 1 for every 2 levels you’ve obtained to a minimum of 1.

SECOND WIND Finding the perfect time rest is what the Tactician is all about; he gains 1 additional Vitality for every level he's obtained when he Takes a Breather.

He also knows how to properly cover people when they’re trying to rest. If he is within his Measure + 5 ft of an ally, they gain 1 additional Vitality for every 2 levels he’s obtained when Taking a Breather.

SKILL FOCUS (Tactics, 4) At first level and every level up, Tacticians receive 4 free skill purchases. These can be distributed between any Advanced Skill from the Tactics Skill Suite. These free purchases may not be doubled up on in the same level but are applied after Skills have been bought by the Character.

SKILL ADEPT This character has a knack for skills. All Advanced Skills have their cost reduced by 1 CrP. They also gain a 10% discount to all Skill Suites. This stacks with other Skill Adepts.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

A Tactician focuses so much on being versatile that their specific specialization suffers. All Tier 1 Weapon Advanced Trainings costs 4 CrP more.

Thug

Choose this Archetype if you want to play someone slips through armor and wears down their opponent so they can't fight back.

The Thug is designed to hit hard and make each strike count. As such they have abilities that remove an enemy’s damage reduction and increase the chance to knock someone out.

VITALITY DIE

d6

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Streetwise Twice

Thugs receive the Armor Basic Training (Light) and 1 Weapon Basic Training for free.

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

CRITICAL STRIKE Sometimes the winner isn't the one that can deal out the most pain but the one who knows where to put the pain. At first level, the Thug gains a +1 to effective damage when deciding whether or not an attack triggers a Trauma Check though this extra "damage" isn't added to the d20! roll. This bonus increases by 1 for every other level the Thug has obtained.

RUN 'EM RAGGED At the beginning of combat or a Skill Challenge, the Thug gains a pool of Stress equal to 5 times his level. On a successfully hit or against any Check that's opposed by another person (even if they're unaware of him), he may subtract an amount of Stress from that pool. If he does so, he inflicts that much Stress on his target, which is healed when the person Takes a Breather.

PRECISION ATTACK The Thug is an expert at making every attack count. At first level, he lowers the DR of his opponent by 1 and an additional 1 for every other level he's obtained. For /d DR, this is subtracted from the final total.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

The Thug never really rises above his street rat origins: the Leadership, Administration, Rally, and Recruiting Advanced Skills all cost double.

Vanguard

Choose this Archetype if you want to play someone that charges in and tries to get as many people to attack them as possible.

The Vanguard is the first in the fray, usually engaging multiple enemies at the same time and trying to do as much damage as possible to soften them up for their allies to follow.

VITALITY DIE

d10

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Tactics

Vanguards receive the Armor Basic Training (Medium) Training and 1 Weapon Basic Training for free.

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

AGAINST THEM ALL When they’re in the thick of it is when the Vanguard thrives. The Vanguard gains their Honor Dice to their Attack rolls against 1 opponent when engaged with 2 or more enemies.

IN, OUT, & AROUND Knowing how to slip and out of your opponent’s guards allow the Vanguard to get in and out of a jam quickly.

By gaining 5 Stress, the Vanguard may change their engagement zone with one opponent, without any associated penalties.

So, if they’re Threatening their opponent, they could move to Engaged or they could move themselves out to Not Engaged without giving their enemy that free attack.

Additionally, if their enemy has successfully employed the In Their Guard Tactic, the Vanguard can move them back out to simply Engaged.

They can done this multiple times by doubling the Stress gain each time it’s used. This resets after they’ve been able to gain Relaxation. This Stress is also reduced by 1 for every 2 levels the Vanguard has obtained.

CROWD CONTROL Surrounded by enemies, the Vanguard learns to use the crowd against themselves, forcing his enemies to get in each other’s way.

A Vanguard can use his full defense against an additional opponent if the two opponents are adjacent to each other and, should anyone try to disengage with him, he may take 5 Stress, in which case, he gains a free attack against them although this is at half damage.

FIRST STRIKE The Vanguard hits hard and hits first. Or at least, they try to.

At the beginning of combat, Vanguards receive a pool of Measure equal to 1 ft + 1 per every level they’ve obtained. When they first become Engaged with an opponent, they may spend ft from that pool to temporarily increase their Measure to determine who strikes first.

So, a level 6 Vanguard would have a pool of 4 ft to work with. If wielding a Stiletto (Measure 1.5 ft) and closing in to Engage with an enemy wielding a Rapier (Measure 4 ft), he could spend 3 ft of it to allow him to get his hit off first, perhaps crippling his enemy before they have change to respond. Doing so would leave him with 1 ft in his pool for the rest of combat.

After that, combat resumes as normal, so he wouldn’t be able to attack the Rapier wielder if he is being Fended Off.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

Vanguards are a position of Honor, and they don’t take charging into battle lightly. A Vanguard loses 1 Honor for every battle they’re not the first on either side to land a melee attack.

Ashcaller

Choose this Archetype if you want to play a servant that heavily relies on the social aspect of the game.

The Ashcaller is a person that carries the legacy of those he loves with him. They’re able to call upon the spirits of the dead to aid him both through a manipulation of the Middle Realm but also as a font of wisdom.

VITALITY DIE

d6

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Lore

Ashcallers receive 2 purchases of the Religion (Ancestors) Advanced Skill for free.

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

SACRED ANCHOR The Ashcaller can summon the spirit of any person whose bones they carry. This summoning is how the Ashcaller invokes their Miracle.

When an Ashcaller prays to a particular spirit, they enter into a Confrontation with them with a number of rounds equal to the amount of Favor spent, trying to convince them to help. At the end of the Confrontation, the Miracle is invoked and the Ashcaller rolls his Honor Dice with a bonus (or penalty) equal the difference in points. This Confrontation takes 1 second per round.

The spirit, of course, regardless of win or lose, gains the Devotion “Tired of the Ashcaller” with a value of 1, or increasing it by 1 if they already have it.

Additionally, the other ancestor spirits become a bit jealous, gaining the Devotion “Dislikes the Ashcaller” at value of 1, or increasing it by 1 if they already have it.

ANCESTOR COVENANT As part of their initiation into their order, the Ashcaller is gifted with the bone of one of their Ancestors and tasked with honoring their legacy. This is often a minor ancestor so this bone doesn’t start as a Relic but may become one as a result of play.

Playing the Spirits of the Dead

Summoned spirits of the dead are not their full personalities but merely shards of what they once were: their strongest characteristics shine through but the subtlety of the once living person is often lost.

So, spirits will often only have 3 Characteristics. Often this is just their 3 Strongest Traits but it can also be their Devotions, Flaws, Temperament, or even Goals, or some combination.

Spirits' personalities should make getting them to invoke certain Miracles easier or harder. After all, kind, sweet, Aunt Mildred won't want to summon a plague on a village and so will resist harder and Uncle Vortigern the Mad.

For the first spirit, the players should be encouraged to fill this out and know at least something about the bones of the person they carry.

The Ashcaller may also harvest and sanctify bones, according to how accepted ancestor worship is in the area, allowing them to summon more spirits. If these were NPCs (or even PCs), simply take the 3 Characteristics that you felt best defined them and use that for their spirit.

TONGUE of the DEAD Whenever an Ashcaller invokes a Miracle and any of the Honor Dice explode, the next Confrontation with a spirit you get a free use of your Honor Die. This bonus does stack if multiple dice explode.

HONORING & HONORED The Ancestors smile on those that strengthen their legacy. Whenever an Ashcaller gains Honor, decrease the “Tired of” and “Dislikes” Devotion of their spirits by that amount. Completely reset these Devotions if the Ashcaller goes up an Honor Category.

ETERNAL FAVOR An Ashcaller is loved for their devotion to their Ancestors beyond others. They add their level to their Max Favor.

DEPARTED COUNCIL By reading the embers and smoke of their holy fires, the Ashcaller is able to channel the knowledge of those left behind.

By spending an Honor Die, they’re able to summon spirits and use them as an Asset for a Skill Check. The spirit’s Knowledge and Organization is considered Poor, although the Ashcaller can increase one or the other every 3 levels they've obtained.

They also receive 1 free purchase of the Religion (Ancestors) Advanced Skill at each level up.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

Ashcallers have turned their back on the Divines and so are unable to gain any benefits from others spending Favor. Additionally, Miracles invoked against them automatically get their full Honor Dice value.

Because of their Anointing, they're also unable to take another Servant Archetype as a Secondary, nor are they allowed to double specialize in this one.

Concert

Choose this Archetype if you want to buff up your companions in all areas of the game and buff up yourself in the process.

The Concert is a people’s person in the deepest sense. They help others be their best self, buffing others by linking their souls together.

VITALITY DIE

d4

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE According to your Secondary Archertype

Concerts receive double the Skill & Trainings of your Secondary Archetype. Replace any instances of “or” with “and”

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

CONDUIT of the SOUL The Concert is a vessel for the divine in all living things. They add their level to their Max Favor.

SOUL UNITED The Concert, by using the links between people, is able to strengthen themselves and others.

A person is considered Soul Linked if the Concert has a Devotion that includes a person or vice versa. This can be met with a general Devotion.

If they met both conditions (both have a Devotion to each other), they’re considered Soul Fettered. This doesn’t count if both have a general Devotion to one another: at least one Devotion has to be specific to either the Concert or the other person.

ONE BEING Any Miracle is considered in her Covenant when invoked on someone the Concert is Soul Linked to.

On top of this, if it is someone they’re Soul Fettered with, she gains half the Favor (rounded down) spent this way back.

WE'RE ALL FRIENDS The Concert has a unique ability to just chill everyone out and get them to relax, even around age old enemies. If someone who she is Soul Linked with is about to be attacked by a sentient foe, before the first blow is actually thrown, the Concert can spend 5 Favor to initiate a Confrontation to get both sides to back down.

If it is someone she is Soul Fettered to, she may do this for only 3 Favor.

MUSE The Concert inspires others to rise to the challenge just solely based on her strong belief in them. When starting a Confrontation, Combat, or Skill Challenge, the Concert receives 2 uses of her Honor Dice that she may give to anyone she is Soul Linked to.

If they are Soul Fettered, that person receives the max value of the dice when they redeem them.

She gains an additional Honor Die for every level she’s obtained.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

A Concert’s being is linked to others and so their fates are entwined. If someone who is Soul Linked to the Concert dies, they gain 20 Stress each time.

However, if someone they are Soul Fettered with dies, they gain no extra Vitality and no Vitality Die roll on level up. If more than one dies, that subtract 1 for each person from their Max Vitality.

Because of their Anointing, they're also unable to take another Servant Archetype as a Secondary, nor are they allowed to double specialize in this one.

Liminalist

Choose this Archetype if you want to command other beings that enhance or expand your skill set and don’t mind taking the risk that they might burst free and kill you.

The liminalist is one that reaches, not for the other realms, but for the endless, shapeless void between them, pulling the demons from them and bending them to their will. A liminalistis to a demonologist what a theoretical mathematician is to an engineer.

VITALITY DIE

d6

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Lore

Liminalists are seekers of unknowable things. They receive 3 free purchases of Religion (All).

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

HEWN OBLIVION The liminalist, though a combination of will and exploitation of Divine power, is able to pull demons, leftovers of creation, from the aetherial void and binds them to his will. Demon stats can be found in the Bonfire Bestiary.

The liminalist spends 1 or more Favor to bind a demon with a Circle value equal to the total of his roll. So, if he spent 2 Favor in the summoning, with an Honor Dice of a d6!, he could get a demon between Circles 2 and 12.

There are different types and categories of demons, each with different abilities that can get a specific job. Some are brutish and stupid, while others are cunning and skillful. Some come linked with certain symbols, such as gateways or the birth of children, that give them powers related to them.

Demon Summoned
Roll (d20)DemonShort Description
1AmayonHurts those around it
2AstarothInflicts Stress
3BelphegorSpawns smaller demons
4DeumusianScares those around it
5 - 6GargoyleBig ol' brutes
7Jack of All Trades
8 - 9ImpManipulators
10Incubus/SuccubusChanges people's personality
11JanusarianUnkillable in zone
12 - 13MerihemRepositions things/people around
14PadagogusFortifies your Resolve
15 - 16SabnockWeakens those around it
17 - 18ScoxMailer demon
19 - 20SycophantSecret Tellers

The demons pulled are randomly rolled on the Demon Summoned table.

The demon appears within 5 ft of the summoner and rolls a d3 initiative dice.

Demons are notorious shapeshifters and beguilers but through this ability, the liminalist is able to force them (somewhat) into a single shape, though this is often a grotesque and twiced form.

Demons, even relatively dumb ones, are intelligent creatures and will struggle to overcome their bindings. Anytime you change a demon’s command, the demon rolls a d20 + its Circle (and the Circle of any other demons controlled by the same liminialist) in a one round Confrontation.

If it wins, the summoner loses control and the demon goes rogue. See the A Demon Unbound sidebar for more information.

Any Servant in the area can try and gain control of it; spending Favor and rolling Honor Dice. If the total is greater than the rogue demon’s Circle, they gain control... for now.

Demons are wily creatures, always trying to find loopholes in their orders and while there are implicit bindings in the summon that prevent obvious loophole breaching, they’ll do the bare minimum of what’s asked of them.

This binding does make them more susceptible to suggestion as well and others may enter into a Confrontation with the demon to get it to do or reveal things, on one condition: it can’t go against their summoner’s orders.

So, a demon ordered to patrol a hall can be forced to reveal information about its master or how many people are in each room, but it can’t be forced by others to stop patrolling (or even not attack the players, should it be told to kill anyone in the hall).

The summon lasts for 1 minute but can be increased by 1 minute if the control spends additional Favor. Demons are forced to stay within eyesight of their current controller.

If the liminalist dies or suffers a Mental Breakdown, the demon is unsummoned.

A Demon Unbound

A demon that’s escaped its bindings is a terrible thing as their full power is unleashed, directed at the one who brought them into existence.

The demon gets back the full complement of its shapeshifting powers. Not only can it change its overall size but any exponential areas to modify drop to the one for one price.

They can shift all their points once a second as well.

The demon first seeks to kill its summoner out of revenge and then, if they’re still around, it seeks any who were working with the summoner. After doing so, it’ll try to do as much damage as it possibly can before it winks out of existence.

SEE the UNSEEN As a liminalist, you learn to get a feel for the void and what ‘could be’ in the ‘is not’ that can be. He can modify his d20 roll on the Demon Summoned table by an amount equal to his level in either direction.

HUBRIS BRIDLED The worst thing a liminal can do is summon a demon from a higher Circle than he has power to control and so he learns to fight his confidence and learn to control his ego, projecting this to others around him.

The liminalist can take Stress to raise or lower Honor Dice results by a like amount, however, he can never lower it below 1 or raise it above its max value

He may also do so for others but takes twice the Stress.

CLERICAL ERROR The Liminalist doesn’t ascribe to one faith but games the system to gain favor because he knows the Divines’ celestial accountants aren’t keeping that close of an eye on things. They increase their Max Favor by their level

They also gain Favor as Servants do, although the performance of the rituals is more lip service than actual belief in most cases and so don’t start with the normal Devotion that Servants start with.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

Liminalists who focus on their craft have more powerful bindings but that can be a problem. Should the liminalist die or suffer a Mental Break, any demons he has bound become unbound instead of simply becoming unsummoned.

Because of their cavalier attitude towards faith, they're also unable to take another Servant Archetype as a Secondary, nor are they allowed to double specialize in this one, nor become Anointed.

Paragon Acolyte

Choose this Archetype if you want a smaller but stronger array of powers that benefits greater from your Honor.

These people take hero worship to another level and by emulating their idols, they convince the already shaky reality that they’re the reincarnation of said hero, giving them amazing powers.

VITALITY DIE

d8

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Any One Relating to His Hero's Story

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

PARAGON’S LEGACY The Paragon Acolyte can channel his hero, allowing him to recreate events from their life on a smaller scale. The player selects 5 feats that the hero performed during their lifetime and, whenever they invoke Miracles related to one or more of those feats, they increase the Honor Dice they get from Favor by 1 size. It is increased an additional size for every 4 levels the Paragon Acolyte has obtained.

LIKE STORIES of OLD Feeling the power of the old stories rush through your veins, it allows you to soar higher than mortals dare. Whenever you roll the maximum amount on their Honor Dice, you gain another use of your Honor Die.

MANIFEST DESTINY Fate is always on the side of the hero, then and now. By spending a point of Favor, you can turn one of your Confrontation, Skill Check, or Defense die to its maximum size. You can do this once at first level and an additional time every 2 levels.

MANTLE HERO At the end of each day, the Paragon Acolyte receives 1 Favor for every point of Reputation in their strongest Reputation, minimum 1, but does not gain Favor by Holy Days or Sacrifices.

GREATER BEING Linked to their hero’s spirit, they can increase the amount of Favor they can get. Their Max Favor is their Honor Category + their level.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

Every hero has a weakness that can lead to their downfall. During character creation, the Paragon Acolyte tells the story of the hero’s downfall. When it becomes relevant, the Paragon Acolyte cannot spend Honor or Honor Dice to help him.

Because of their Anointing, they're also unable to take another Servant Archetype as a Secondary, nor are they allowed to double specialize in this one.

Priest

Choose this Archetype if you want your companions to benefit from their Favor more and receivea kick-back for doing so.

Priests focus on shaping Miracles on other people rather than themselves, making them a good support Archetype for other classes. Their Miracles vary widely based on their patron Divine.

VITALITY DIE

d6

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE None

Priests receives 3 purchases of the Religion (The Priest’s Covenant) Advanced Skill for free

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

DIVINE COVENANT During Character Creation, a Priest selects 1 Covenant and 1 Cosmic Link, representing their deity’s sphere of influence and personality, respectively.

Covenants change which Miracles the Priest has access to while Cosmic Links change the ways you gain and spend Favor.

SHEPHERD of the PEOPLE If someone else prays for a Miracle within sight of the Priest, the Priest can spend his own Favor to increase the effective cost of that Miracle. This ability doesn’t work on those Anointed into other cults. He gains half, rounded down, of the Favor spent this way back.

HONOR of the DIVINES If you or someone you've spent Favor on rolls the maximum value on your Honor Die while invoking a Miracle, you gain an extra use of your Honor Die.

FAVORED of the DIVINES The Priest’s mission isn’t a selfish one, but it does have some benefits and they’re loved for their devotion to their Divines beyond others. They add their level to their Max Favor.

CATECHISM By studying the holy texts, the Priest is about to discern the will of the Divines and better understand the Higher Realms. They receive a free purchase of the Religion (Divines) Advanced Skill at first level and at every level up.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

A Priest has sworn themselves to a Higher Power and as a token of their Covenant, they must select a taboo; an action or thing they must never do, such as cut their hair or eat meat. This must be appropriate to the Divine and be approved by the GM before play begins.

Because of their Anointing, they're also unable to take another Servant Archetype as a Secondary, nor are they allowed to double specialize in this one.

Shaman

Choose this Archetype if you want to play a servant with a more solid list of Miracles that affect the world beyond just bonuses.

A Shaman is one who invested their second soul into a Bonfire, thus they carry a part of the flame with them where they go. They are a divine elementalist, with a larger selection of Miracles than your average priest but they’re not pulled from the traditional Miracle list.

VITALITY DIE

d10

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Lore

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

LINKED to the BONFIRE The Shaman has the soul of the Bonfire and so is a generator of holy power that flows from them. They increase their Max Favor by their level.

SHAPE YMIR The Shaman shapes the world through their connection to it and so their Miracles are more immediate than other servants. They may pray for any spell from the Animism, Calling, and Occultism Traditions with their Honor Dice from Favor behaving like a Channeling Dice.

Miracles cast this way always have a Shape of Circle and an Origin of Aura. These Rudiments do not increase the Drain of the spell and the Shaman can choose to have it effect either those linked to the Shaman (i.e. anointed into the fire cult) or everyone else.

PURIFY the MORTAL COIL The Shaman can remove their mortal coil to manifest their true nature but doing so may kill them. For every 2 Vitality the Shaman sacrifices, they gain 1 temporary special Favor.

This Favor doesn’t count towards your Current Favor and can be immediately added to keep a Miracle going. All damage dealt this way goes on one Wound and the Favor is wasted if not used before the next sun rise.

MANTLE of FIRE The Shaman’s power projects out from him to protect those he wishes. By sacrificing 1 Vitality, the Shaman can make something within the Shape of a Miracle immune to its affect.

MASTER of the DARK The Shaman can read the flames and ashes, gaining insight into things others can’t see. Starting at 2nd level and at every other level up after that, the Shaman receives either 1 free purchase of either the Lore or Survival Skill Suite.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

The Shaman literally glows with inner light, giving enemies a +10 to spot them.

Additionally, when they invoke a Miracle, the Bonfire swells within them, making 10 ft around them Bright Illumination. The Shaman is penalized as well if they don’t close their eyes, though there’s no permanent damage.

Because of their Anointing, they're also unable to take another Servant Archetype as a Secondary, nor are they allowed to double specialize in this one.

Symbolist

Choose this Archetype if you want to spend your Favor to gain permanent bonuses to help you and your companions adapt as needs be.

The Symbolist is the word and the law, both being sacred to him. His worships reality itself and channels the innate power in the corpse of Ymir to shun magic and miracles. He grips the law so tightly as to bend it to his will.

VITALITY DIE

d10

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Survival

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

LINKED to the BONES of YMIR Harnessing the divine energies of the Middle Realm, the Symbolist is able to become a part of the world in a more real way. He gains Favor equal to his Honor Category + 1/2 his level. Unlike other Servants, he can’t gain additional Favor through the normal means (sacrifices and holy days): this Favor is static and only increases with level.

MARKS of the EARTH Through ceremony and ritual, the Symbolist is able to invoke Miracles that are normally reserved only for the Divines. Given an hour, the Symbolist can endow a mark on him or another person. During the ceremony, he selects a certain number of his Favor and “locks” into the mark.

Doing so essentially invokes a Miracle on that person, however, unlike a normal Miracle, it persists for as long as the person marked wishes it and there is a distinct chance of failure: the Symbolist must roll over 10 on their Honor Dice. He gains an additional roll of the Honor Dice for every Favor he locks in.

If the Miracle is unsuccessfully invoked at the end of the ceremony, the mark, and the Miracle by extension, didn’t take and that Favor is freed once more, however, the Symbolist can’t try the ceremony again on that person until they increase an Honor Category.

If it was, that Miracle active, blessing the Symbolist and/or marked person. The mark can only be removed at the will of the person or Symbolist and can’t be removed by normal means (so washing won’t get rid of it). The Favor is “locked” and can't be used for other marks and Miracles until released.

Unlike normal, the Miracle doesn’t give the full Honor Dice as a bonus whenever the Miracle is applicable: instead the person gains a +1 (or -1 depending on what the person wants when they roll) for each Favor locked into that Miracle when applicable.

Like normal Miracles, however, this can modify things you normally couldn’t, like Movement speed or Knock-Back, or what-have-you. The GM may also increase this bonus if he feels it is appropriate (getting a +1 to your equipment breaking isn’t that big of a deal so increasing it to +3 wouldn’t be out of place, for example).

Should the Symbolist die, all his marks are released. Also, should the Symbolist’s Favor drop below their currently locked Favor (from lowering an Honor Category, for example) they’re forced to unlock one of their marks and dispel a Miracle.

LAW of AVERAGES The Symbolist is a pillar of certainty in a sea of chaos. If the Symbolist rolled under the average on a dice, he may gain 5 Stress and the next roll someone makes gives them a +1 bonus to their roll. Additionally, if he rolled over the average, he may spend 5 Stress for the next roll to be at a -1 penalty.

This bonus is also increased by 1 for every 2 levels they’ve obtained and can negate perfect attacks and defenses.

CONDUIT of REALITY The Symbolist can invoke Miracles from the following Covenants: Dream, Guardians, Adversity, Battle, Beauty, Fate, Fire, Home, Honor. He is unable to invoke any Miracles outside of these Covenants, even for the normal price.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

By anchoring themselves to the Bones of Ymir, the Symbolist cuts off his connection to the God’s Realm in a way: other Servants are unable to invoke beneficial Miracles on him and they also increase their Honor Dice by 1 size when invoking destructive Miracles on him.

Because of their Anointing, they're also unable to take another Servant Archetype as a Secondary, nor are they allowed to double specialize in this one. Also, due to their inherent link with Ymir, they're unable to take a Weird-Adept Archetype as their Secondary.

Advocate

Choose this Archetype if you want to be supportive in a Confrontation without being the center of attention and responsibility.

While other Socialites like the limelight, the Advocate doesn’t mind playing second fiddle and in fact, thrives there. When supporting others in a Confrontation, the Advocates gets a lot of bonuses.

VITALITY DIE

d4

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Lore

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

RETHINK AN ARGUMENT Advocates tend to be more introspective than other Socialites, which allows them to wait on an argument until they can articulate their thoughts more clearly. When making an Appeal, the Advocate can put aside a number of dice that they rolled a 1 on equal to 3 + their level. This dice isn't added to their total for points or Stress.

They can later bring it back in, adding it to another round’s total with a +2 for every round that dice has sat out. This can bring the total over the dice's maximum value.

FLANKING POINT The Advocate can really use his unassuming nature to really hammer home a point. If multiple pieces of Evidence are presented in a round of a Confrontation, and the opposition picks yours to respond to, you gain an additional point.

WALLFLOWER BLOOM The Advocate really shines when not center stage. When making an Appeal, if you roll the least number of dice (or are tied for it) and your side wins the round, gain an additional point.

HELPER'S PORTION Sometimes the reward is just to know you've helped. When the person that started the Confrontation is dividing out the Honor, if the Advocate takes the least amount, they gain 1 Honor + 1 for every 5 levels they've obtained.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

Advocates can kind of lock up when they’re in the driver's seat. When they’re the only one in a Confrontation, Evidence and Appeals give them 1 less point.

Armiger

Choose this Archetype if you want to play a battlefield commander, using the Morale rules to win combats.

The Armiger is one that has been granted the right to bear a cost of arms, either their personal sigil or their liege lord. People are naturally drawn to these individuals and they find their strength in the support of this crowd.

VITALITY DIE

d8

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Tactics

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

RISING the BANNER Armigers attract the best and brightest to their banner. As such, they gain double the bonus to attracting followers from Honor. On top of this, they only gain the -1 to their roll for every other follower they attract.

FORCE of PERSONALITY No matter the situation, Armigers are able to leverage their likeable personalities. When Rallying a broken person, they may gain another use of their Honor Die and an additional Honor Dice for every 2 levels. This additional use of the Honor Dice lasts until the end of the Confrontation and doesn’t need to be spent right then.

STANDARD An Armiger has the right to bear a heraldic crest that identifies him. He may emblazon this on a banner or his shield, but by having it proudly displayed, while he is still fighting, all his allies use his Honor category to determine their starting Morale category.

SKILL FOCUS (Tactics, 4) At first level and every level up, Armigers receive 4 free skill purchases. These can be distributed between any Advanced Skills from the Tactics Skill Suite. These free purchases may not be doubled up on in the same level but are applied after Skills have been bought by the Character.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

Armigers are standards of the people and when they fail to live up to that, they’re judged more harshly. If the Armiger is forced to retreat from a Combat or Confrontation for any reason, they lose 5 Honor.

Champion

Choose this Archetype if you want to play a traditional hero: beating foes through force of spirit and inspiring others to do the same.

A crusader for a cause, paladin of the king, a knight errant questing for his love. These are Champions. Their oaths and devotions are the weapons they wield and, from sacrifice to a cause greater than themselves, strength.

VITALITY DIE

d10

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Tactics

Champions gain Armor Basic Training (Heavy), Shield Basic Training and 1 free Weapon Basic Training.

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

POWER of DEVOTION Zeal is a powerful force and can sharpen the mind and bring out the best in someone when properly channelled. Whenever redeeming an Honor Die while doing something related to their Devotion, they also add that Devotion to the roll.

FANATICAL PRESENCE Your oath is sacred and only death can prevent you from the fulfilment of your duty and others can see that. This total faith in your path makes the going easier for others.

During a Morale Confrontation that relates to the Champion’s Devotion, whenever an argument involves him, one of those dice gets a +1. This is increased by 1 for every level you’ve obtained.

Multiple Devotions don’t stack in this case. You may add this bonus regardless of whether or not you're the party captain and anyone on the Champion’s side is eligible for this benefit.

SOLEMNITY of CAUSE A Champion considers his obligations with a solemn contemplation and as his beliefs are challenged, the stronger they grow. Whenever he wins an Appeal that involves at least 1 of his Devotions, he takes no Stress.

IRON RESOLVE Nothing, not even apparent defeat, can sway a Champion from their course of action. In a Confrontation that is related to at least one of their Devotions, when the Champion loses an Appeal, they gain a +1 to their next round if they Appeal again. This is increased by 1 for every 3 levels they've obtained. they

Those on his side are also bolstered by this surety and gain the same bonus if the Champion gets it.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

Champions take their oaths very seriously and don’t take new ones on lightly. Anytime they can purchase Devotions for CrP, the price of a new Devotion is 10 CrP x the number of Devotions the Champion already has.

Diplomat

Choose this Archetype if you want to play someone that bends others to their will through sheer force of personality.

The Diplomat is a strong-willed character that makes the most of emotional Appeals: learning how to use them to great effect to sway his opponents.

VITALITY DIE

d4

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Streetwise

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

CAREFUL WORDING A Diplomat has the grace and tact to be able to reword an argument in the most effective way possible. The Diplomat can spend 10 Stress to reroll all of the dice for one side when they Appeal in a Confrontation. For his and his allies’ Characteristics, take the higher of the two results. For the enemy, take the lower of the two results.

STRONG PERSONALITY As a Diplomat grows, she becomes more confident in who she is and what she wants. At 2nd level and every other level after that, a Diplomat can increase the strength of one of their Traits by 1 dice (up to a d20) or they save them and cash in two of these increases for a new weak Trait starting at 1d4.

GREY EMINENCE In his arena, he is king, and nothing can shake him. For the duration of a Confrontation the Diplomat gains 1 free use of their Honor Die. They gain an additional free Honor Die for every level they’ve obtained. They can only apply 1 of these bonus Honor Dice to a single roll, though that doesn’t stop them adding Honor Dice that they got from other sources.

RESILIENT CHARACTER Surprisingly, those with the strongest personalities have the greatest power to resist abuse and not second guess themselves. When using an Appeal, half the Stress you would get.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

Diplomats put their reputation on the table whenever they engage in a Confrontation. They lose 5 Honor whenever they lose a Confrontation.

Foil

Choose this Archetype if you want to play someone that convinces people through using their weaknesses against them and protecting yourself from their charms.

The Foil focuses on using the other person when convincing them of something. He can steal the opponent’s dice in Confrontation and when things get tough, he can tag in another person to take on the Confrontation.

VITALITY DIE

d4

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Streetwise

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

MIRRORING By agreeing with your enemy, you can sometimes lull them into a false sense of security, causing them to lower their guard. A Foil can take 10 Stress and make a guess at a Characteristic his opponent has. If he’s correct, that Characteristic loses 1 dice for every 2 levels he’s obtained, down to 1 dice. He also automatically receives points equal to the dice removed.

So a level 7 Foil who correctly guesses a 3d6! characteristic, lowers it to d6! and gains 2 points.

GASLIGHTING A Foil’s particularly devious when it comes to other’s flaws and weaknesses. A Foil can guess a character’s Mental or Behavioral Flaw. If correct, and they successfully use it in an Appeal, they gain an additional point.

CONTEMPT A Foil can pretend he doesn't care, thus shaking his opponent's confidence in their arguments. If a Foil starts the round, Appeals, and loses, they can take 10 Stress. If they do, they gain half the points they would have gotten if they had succeeded. They reduce the Stress inflicted by 1 for every 4 levels they've obtained, down to 3 Stress.

SHIFT BLAME There’s strength in numbers, especially when those numbers are used as a shield. When his side makes a successful Appeal, the Foil can sacrifice 1 Honor to choose whose dice gets added as points instead of going with the lowest. That person, however, is thrown headfirst into a stressful situation, suddenly becoming the center of attention, giving them 3 Stress for every point of difference between what they’re added and what would have been added. This penalty is lowered by 1 Stress for every 10 levels the Foil has obtained.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

Foils are so good at mirroring others that they often forget to reflect on themselves; It takes them twice as much CrP to improve their Traits.

Fusilier

Choose this Archetype if you want to play someone that uses firearms to stun and overpower people through use of fear.

Firearms are new and exciting but also dangerous. While not as damaging or as far reaching as other ranged weapons, they do terrify in a primal way, a thing that Fusiliers have learned to exploit.

VITALITY DIE

d6

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Tactics

Fusiliers receive 1 free Weapon Basic Training for the firearm of their choice.

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

STANDARD ISSUE Fusiliers often tend to gain their firearms from the military and a lot of time, they take them home (much to the chagrin of the quartermasters). They may start the game with 4 handgonnes, 10 fire lances, or a hakenbuchse.

OF LEAD & POWDER A Fusilier trains with guns, pushing their skills to the limit, allowing to get creative in their uses. Fusiliers may wield and fire handgonnes with one hand and count as small weapons for the 2 1 Handed Weapons Style. They’re also able to deploy a hakenbuchse’s trip pod in 2 seconds instead of 5 seconds and they get 2 uses out of each fire lance.

With all firearms, a Fusilier can light the brand in a swift motion, taking no time at all, lowering the firing time by 4 seconds.

ROAR of the BEAST There’s something terrifying of the smell of smoke and the rage of fire and a Fusilier knows how to use this to their advantage. If in a Morale Confrontation, enemies that are Appealing to those flinching gain an extra 2d6!.

Further, those that travel with the Fusilier gain an immunity to this after a combat and lower their flinch times against all firearms by 1 second per shot they weren't hit by.

Roar of the Beast Lite

If you’re not running the Morale rules, here is another option to not have the Fusilier nerfed because of this change:

The Fusilier can select a number of flinched enemies up to his Warfare Skill Rank to gain an additional -2 to their Defense for each Wound Category they've dropped.

BOOMSTICK By adding just a little something to the powder mix, the Fusilier can make that bang from the firearm going off exceptionally loud. The minimum amount of time an enemy flinches from a Fusilier’s firearm going off increases by 1 for every 2 levels they’ve obtained.

MARTIAL TRAINING A Fusilier receives a Tier 1 Weapon Advanced Training in the Firearm of his choice for every level he’s obtained.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

Due to all the gunfire a Fusilier has been around, they have a harder time hearing than others. The Listening Advanced Skill costs 6 CrP instead of 4.

Knave

Choose this Archetype if you want to play someone that beats their opponents though sheer force of apathy.

The Knave is a mean villain - mean in the sense of being crude and villain in the sense of being low class, but unlike others, the Knave doesn’t seem to mind and that’s where their strength lies.

VITALITY DIE

d6

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE None

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

UNIMPRESSED A Knave knows that silly titles are only there to buttress insecurities. Others gain no benefit from their Reputation, Honor, and/or Stat Confrontation Dice when engaging in Confrontation with the Knave.

PLAYING DIRTY While others hoard their precious Honor for the sake of not having people talk bad about them, the Knave doesn’t care and so she can use her as a weapon. A Knave can lose 3 Honor to increase one of her Characteristic dice by 1 and reroll all non-exploded dice she’s using in her Appeal that round. She can also increase 1 extra dice by 1 size for every 2 levels she’s obtained.

FOOL’S BEARING By deflating yourself, you can deflate others. Each round, a Knave can pay X Honor or X points to lower all non-Flaw Characteristic dice by X sizes for everyone in that round (including the Knave and her allies). This follows the normal rules if a Characteristic would drop below a d4!, however, the Knave’s never drop below 1d4!.

This ability shrinks a single dice an additional size for every 2 levels she’s obtained.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

Knaves aren’t really heroes at the end of the day, even if they try to be. Shrink their Honor Dice by 1 size.

Monteback

Choose this Archetype if you want to play someone that convinces their opponents through fast talking: coming on strong for a quick win but suffering in the long game.

The Mountebank is one of tricks and quick thinking. He relies on dazing the person with words, hoping they won’t take the time to catch onto his tricks.

VITALITY DIE

d4

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Streetwise

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

FAST TALKER If you can get someone to agree quickly, so much the better. You start the Confrontation gaining an additional d8! to each Appeal but shrinks one size each round, down to a d4!. You gain an additional dice for every 2 levels you've obtained. You only get this bonus if you choose to Appeal that round. The dice shrinks even if you use Evidence that round.

However, if you’re unable to convince your target by that time, the next round you receive no bonus dice from this ability and each round after, you instead reduce the size of one of your dice if you Appeal.

JACK of ALL TRADES You don’t have to know everything but you should act like you do. The Mountebank has mastered that art and so they increase the dice they gain from their Skills by 1 size.

KEEP 'EM OFF BALANCE The Mountebank knows how to make a mark sweat and uses that pressure to have them start making rash decisions in his favor. If your opponents lose an Appeal, they also add the lowest dice's result in Stress.

SKILL FOCUS (Streetwise, 4) At first level and every level up, Montebacks receive 4 free skill purchases. These can be distributed between any Advanced Skills from the Streetwise Skill Suite. These free purchases may not be doubled up on in the same level but are applied after Skills have been bought by the Character.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

The Mountebank is the devil in disguise and his untrustworthy nature makes him never quite sure if you can trust him. You lower everyone’s Racial Preference towards you by 1, bottoming out at Hate.

Noble

Choose this Archetype if you want to debuff your enemy while gaining strength through winning Appeals.

The Noble is typically aloof and hard to impress and so can convince people simply by making them unsure about their conviction, shrinking their dice in Confrontation.

VITALITY DIE

d4

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Tactics

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

NOBLE BEARING By reminding others of their lower station in life, you can remind them just how petty their needs are. You inflict 1 point of Stress for every dice your opponent(s) brings in each round up to your level.

RETHINK YOUR WORDS Assail the throne of a noble’s grace with caution, for you are at his will and pleasure. Whenever the Noble, or one of his allies, wins an Appeal, you may force the enemy to reroll their dice on their next Appeal, taking the worse of the two results.

ROYAL BACKGROUND Nobles form an elite class of society, giving them a strong sense of self and confidence. Their Devotion to their clan starts at a 4 and they gain the Trait “Noble Heritage” at 3d6! for free. This doesn't replace any of their 5 free Traits and may be increased in the normal matter.

If the player wants, they can swap out the "Noble Heritage" Trait for the "Parvenu" Trait, representing either new nobility or a non-noble bloodline, such as being the scion of a wealthy merchant family.

GOOD BREEDING In victory or defeat, the Noble is gracious. At the end of a Confrontation, the Noble receives 1 Honor automatically. This bonus is increased by 1 Honor for every 2 levels he’s obtained.

All his allies also automatically gain 1 Honor, though this doesn’t increase as the Noble levels.

INHERITANCE This character may have had an extra leg up in life, allowing them the opportunity to start with better equipment than others. They gain a free weapon of their choice or a Courser mount and also gain 15 sc for each CrP cashed in at the end of Character Creation.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

Nobility is a collective illusion and so those of royal blood, no matter how limited strive to keep that illusion in place. Nobles lose 1 Honor and gain 1 Stress whenever they're not referred to by either their proper title, "my lord", or "sir".

In the case of Parvenus, the character is more aware of their low-born roots and will do everything they can to separate themselves from the commoner class. As such, they're required to spend 10% of their coin (both starting and acquired during play) on nice clothes and lodgings (however, they gain no additional Relaxation for doing so).

Officer

Choose this Archetype if you want to use the Morale rules to allow your company to adapt and rally to snatch the from the jaws of defeat.

The cunning Officer is able to read a battlefield like a book and with a single command, swings the fulcrum of battle in her side’s favor. He is the party leader and the standard to which others flock.

VITALITY DIE

d6

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Tactics

Officers receive the Armor Basic Training (Light)

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

MOMENTUM Those in leadership can often turn a small victory into a large one. Whenever the Officer wins a round, they gain a bonus d6! the next round for each successive time they’ve done so.

FOG of WAR The Art of War is the art of information and the Officer knows how to wage that war. Against a Panicked person (or group), Evidence gives an additional point.

ESPRIT de CORPS The Officer can push others to limits they didn’t know they had in them to fight for their comrades. At first level, while the Officer is conscious, any ally that can see him gains a positive Devotion to the company starting at strength 1. This is increased by 1 for every level he’s obtained.

BATTLEFIELD MANEUVERING Careful planning and strategic movement can help win over the day. The Officer can sacrifice an Honor Die to allow anyone on the battlefield to either switch Tactics or Shift without a penalty at that second. This can be done after a roll is made and the results given and the Officer can either sacrifice his Honor Die or one that the person who is benefiting from this ability has.

MARTIAL TRAINING An Officer receives her choice of a free Tier 2 Armor, Shield, or Weapon Advanced Training for every 2 levels she’s obtained.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

Officers don’t really know how to fight alone and may take the better part of valor in a combat. When fighting alone, Officer characters gain 1 Stress every time they put up dice in a Morale Confrontation.

Philosopher

Choose this Archetype if you want to become stronger as you let your opponent win rounds so that you can crush them with one fell swoop.

The Philosopher reserves his strength, allowing his opponent in a Confrontation to escalate for him. While others suffer strain from not meeting the argument straight on, the Philosopher uses it to his advantage.

VITALITY DIE

d4

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Lore

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

RHETORIC By knowing the fundamentals of how to form an argument, a Philosopher can stop and point out the logical fallacies in another’s argument (even if they’re not there). A Philosopher can flip a dice over one side, to a lower number. They can flip an additional dice for every level they’ve obtained.

So, they can move a 7 on a d10 to 5, 3, 2, but not 10, or a 6 on a d12 to a 2 or 3 but not up to 8, 9, or 12.

STOIC Philosophers are trained so that petty things like emotion arguments don’t have as strong an effect on them and their opponent can tell. If a Philosopher uses Evidence against an opponent's Appeal or his opponent Appeals and he responds with Evidence, he gains an additional point.

CLOSING REMARKS Regardless of whether they want to hear it or not, the Philosopher knows how to make you listen. Whenever a Philosopher pushes, he gains 1 point.

PRACTICE DEBATE Even if you don’t get what you want, you can often get practice for next time. Whenever a Philosopher loses a round, they gain 1 use of their Honor Die in their next round. This increases by 1 use for every other level they obtain, however, they can’t use more than 1 per round.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

The Philosopher tries to not let things get personal: when they make an Appeal, they don't half their Stress gain if they win.

Rascal

Choose this Archetype if you want to play some that relies more on the circumstances of the Confrontation than on their raw stats.

The Rascal gains a few skills, but their main strength is their cunning ability to avert danger, though any brush with death leaves him shaken. On top of this, in Confrontation, the Rascal wins because he can leverage circumstances in his favor.

VITALITY DIE

d6

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Trades

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

LUCKY The Rascal is naturally blessed with the ability to get out of trouble and use that adrenaline that comes as death comes near to dodge the grim reaper and keep running. After the results are given, the Rascal can take 2 Stress to modify his results by 1. These may be done with the following conditions:

  • They can never be used to make you a better fighter. Stress gained this way can only be used to dodge death or escape a bad situation but never to make your character a superman.
  • The character must think of a situation that saves his rear end, something that happens to him that’s to his advantage.

The key here is that it can’t be impossible, but it can be highly improbable. The chandelier rope breaking right at that moment separating him from a blood thirsty guard, a pigeon flying across an archer’s view intercepting an arrow, etc. are all acceptable.

It can’t be the result of skill. Him deflecting the blade with his hand like a badass is right out.

Should the character be unable to think of a scenario that fits both of these criteria, he’s unable to gain Stress to save himself.

GREASE PAINT & GLITTER If there's one thing that a Rascal knows, it’s how to position themselves in the most advantageous light. In a Confrontation, once per round, the Rascal increases one dice 1 size. This is increased by 1 for every level he’s obtained. This can either be his or his allies’, it doesn’t matter.

Once he’s increased all dice in a round 1 size, he may then go back and increase them again, and so on.

SKILL FOCUS (Any, 2) At first level and every level other up, Rascals receive 2 free skill purchases. These can be distributed between any Advanced Skill. These free purchases may not be doubled up on in the same level but are applied after Skills have been bought by the Character.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

A Rascal favors no weapons as they tend to get you killed: all Weapon Advanced Trainings are 2 CrP more expensive per Tier (Tier 1: 11 CrP, Tier 2: 16 CrP, Tier 3: 22 CrP).

Augur

Choose this Archetype if you want to a weird-adept with a wider of rotating range of strengths, giving some breathe of powers and greater power.

An Augur is one who watches the stars. The times and seasons are linked to the swirl of constellations overhead and the ways of magic. Those that watch them carefully can harness their power. An Augur gains bonuses based on the passage of time, making them change with the times.

VITALITY DIE

d4

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Lore and Weirdcraft

Augurs receive 2 free purchases of Navigation Advanced Skill and 1 free purchase of Mathematics Advanced Skill.

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

Daily Omen Boon
Day of the Week Tradition
1stAnimism
2ndCalling
3rdCharm
4thGlamour
5thInvestiture
6thOccult
7thSortilege

JUDICII STELLATUM As part of their training, Augurs are taught how to harness the magic that drifts down from the stars and constellations. This gives them a steady pool of Spell Points whenever they cast a spell.

At first level, all spells the Augur casts have 7 SPs. This can be spent to modify the spell that they’re shaping. It does take a moment to summon the astral forces, so shaping a spell takes 3 seconds.

They increase this by 1 SP for every other level they obtain.

LECTIO COTIDIE At the beginning of each day, the Augur reads the signs and divines which of the astral winds, and thus which Weird Tradition, is most dominant on that day. This happens in a cycle based on the days of the week.

When shaping a spell from the Tradition linked to the day, the Augur receives an extra d4! SP to spend on that spell. This extra dice is increased by 1 size for every 3 levels they obtain.

If you lose track of the day of the week, you’ve lost track of the stars and don’t gain the bonus for that day.

Weekly Omen Boon
Week of the MonthCategory
1stShape
2ndRange
3rdOrigin
4thAll

SIGNUM HEBDOMADA The Augur knows each week brings a new fate and with it, new boons. The Augur gains an additional bonus of 1 SP whenever shaping a spell that applies to the particular Rudiment. This is increased by 1 SP for every 5 levels they’ve obtained.

If you lose track of which week, you’ve lost track of the stars and don’t gain the bonus for that week.

VESTIBULUM OMEN The calends are a special time, when the moon is new and the stars are able to shine; unfiltered, they empower the Augur. The Augur has a pool of 3 Honor Dice that they can use for spell shaping any time during the month. This pool is increased by 1 Honor Dice for every level they’ve obtained.

This pool refreshes on the first day of every month.

If you miss the first day of the month, you’ve lost track of the stars and don’t gain the bonus for that month.

LIBRO DIEBUS An Augur keeps a Book of Days where they store their divination knowledge. They gain 3 Rudiments of their choice at 1st level and an additional Rudiment every other level.

SKILL FOCUS (Weirdcraft & Navigation) At first level and every other level up, Augurs receive a free purchase of the Weirdcraft Skill Suite and Navigation Advanced Skill.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

Augurs are extremely superstitious since everything is controlled by fate and the stars. Bad luck means a bad fate. They take 1 Stress every time they roll a 1 on a d20.

They also find other types of Weirdshaping strange and so are unable to take another Weird-Adept Archetype as their Secondary, however, they are able to double specialize in their Primary.

Augur Double Specialist

JUDICII STELLATUM

This starts at 7 SP base and is increased by 1.5 SPs (rounded down) per level.

LECTIO COTIDIE

Incease the number of SPs you get to a d6!.

SIGNUM HEBDOMADA

This is increased to 1 additional SP for every 3 levels you’ve obtained.

LIBRO DIEBUS

This is increased to 2 additional Rudiments with a new one every level.

Mage

Choose this Archetype if you want to raw power and flexibility.

The mage is one that allows himself to be buffeted by the astral winds and so channels great power but also is in great danger. The mage has the most raw power of the Weird-Adept Archetypes but it could backfire on him.

VITALITY DIE

d4

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE According to your Secondary Archetype

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

WILD MAGIC SHAPING The Mage is able to channel the power of the stars, harnessing it and creating magical energy. While doing so the weird-adept must stand still and he glows with light, being illuminated by a column that reaches above them. This light is equivalent to a candle’s brightness.

After 7 seconds, the Mage gains their Spell Points. Unlike other Archetypes of this type, however, a lot is left up to chance. The Mage rolls randomly for the Shape, Origin, and Range of the spell and d3! SP that they can spend on the Effect (which you select after learning what the Shape, Origin, and Range is).

They also gain an additional d3! “free” SP that can either be spent on the Effect, or to modify what they rolled on the tables on a 1 to 1 basis.

When considering Drain, the Mage only has to worry about the Effect’s Base Drain and so, essentially, gets the other Rudiments for free. As long as he has more Spell Points than Drain, he can keep the spell cast.

You can also suffer weirdburn from keeping a spell up too long: if your spell’s Drain is greater than your current SP, the spell is still cast, but you and everyone within 200 ft takes 1 Stress for every point you’re over.

Going back to the above example: if you have 9 SP, and you keep the spell up for 15 seconds, you and those within 200 ft take 4 Stress ( 20 - 3 - 3 ). Should you continue to keep the spell up, you’d take an additional 3 Stress every 5 seconds.

It is recommended that even though you don’t technically get those points until after that 7 second duration, that you roll everything ahead of time and figure out what you’re going to cast ahead of time. The GM is not obliged to stop the count for you if you haven’t been spending those 7 seconds wisely.

You can stop shaping at any time; however, you take Stress equal to the amount of SP you have left - Weird is a powerful primal force and once unleashed, it is not stopped without cost. You also cannot cast or keep up a spell and Channel. This doesn’t remove those SP but the Mage does lose 1 SP every 6 seconds.

Channeling in Armor

Wild Magic Users (Mages and Wizards) both draw their power from the stars. As such, anything that gets between them and this, makes channeling more difficult. While this is negligible while wearing clothing, armor, being a mite bit heavier, does slowdown Spell Point acquisition.

  • Light Armor increases channeling time by 5.
  • Medium Armor increases it by 10.
  • Heavy Armor increase it by 15.

WILD SURGE CONDUIT The Mage puts himself more at danger than other casts but is able to experience greater power. If the total number of SP from channeling is greater than 4 + level, a Wild Surge occurs.

In addition to whatever happens with the spell, it is also recast. The new version, however, is Circularly Shaped at Full Range and with an Origin of either Aura or Far, as the weird-adept sees fit. They also take Stress equal to how much they were over.

EMPOWERED CHANNELING A Mage relies on an innate understanding of the flow of magic through his body and overtime he can increase its effectiveness.

Not starting at first level but happening after every level he's obtained, the Mage can either increase the size of any 1 of his dice by 1, or decrease her channeling time by 1, down to a minimum of 3 seconds.

She may also, independently, decrease her channel time by 1 but this costs an amount of CrP equal to X, down to a minimum of 3 seconds.

ASTRAL FULCRUM There is nothing between the Mage and the raw Weird and that allows her to force what others can't. The Mage can take 10 Stress in which case they gain all their SP in the first second. This is in addition to the normal Fallout.

However, they still need to complete the channeling: if they don't, they receive an additional 10 Stress. As they become more powerful, however, they learn how to mitigate that danger, lowering the Stress inflicted by 1 for every 4 levels they've obtained.

UNLEARN DOGMA As the Mage grows in power, the can set aside things that are holding them back. At each level up, a Mage can forget a non-Effect Rudiment. If they do so, they gain an Effect Rudiment of their choice.

METHOD of LOCI A Mage gains 2 new Rudiments at 1st level but an additional Rudiment every other level. Any new Rudiments must be Effect Rudiments.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

The Mage rejects martial prowess as a role and so all Weapon Advanced Trainings are 2 CrP more expensive per Tier (Tier 1: 11 CrP, Tier 2: 16 CrP, Tier 3: 22 CrP).

They also find other types of Weirdshaping strange and so are unable to take another Weird-Adept Archetype as their Secondary, however, they are able to double specialize in their Primary.

Mage Double Specialist

SKILLS & TRAININGS

double specialize Mages gain 2 purchases of the Weirdcraft Skill Suite.

WILD MAGIC SHAPING

Increase all channeling dice to d4!s

WILD SURGE CONDUIT

Increase your Wild Surge threshold becomes 5 + (level * 2)

EMPOWERED CHANNELING

This ability now starts at first level. Your free dice automatically increases every 3 levels. This is in addition to the normal increase.

METHOD of LOCI

Increased to 0 additional Rudiments and new one every level

Runegalder

Choose this Archetype if you want to play a weird-adept and are familiar with other games' spellcasters.

Unlike other magic-users, the Runegalder seals magical power in his bond, allowing him to not risk his body when working with supernatural forces. This allows him to cast quickly and consistently but limits the amount and flexibility of his spells.

VITALITY DIE

d6

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Lore and Weirdcraft

Runegalders receive 3 free purchases of Literacy in their native language.

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

VANCIAN SHAPING The Runegalder chains the power of spells to various runes that he then invests, sealing them with his blood until he’s ready to release them.

Every 24 hours, the Runegalder can seal 3 spells. He can also bind an additional spell for every 3 levels he’s obtained. This means that he may cast those spells at any time by simply speaking the rune they’re linked to, once prepared.

Speaking the rune releases it from its binding so speaking the same rune again before he’s resealed it will not recast the spell - the spell’s power is gone.

He may cast a spell multiple times per day, but he’ll need to bind each instance of the spell to a different rune.

Speaking a rune in this way doesn’t affect the Runegalder and so he ignores Fallout to himself.

He may also unseal a rune without actually shaping it, but he is not able to immediately reseal a new rune right after.

The Runegalder's magic is 'dead' and so is less potent than other types of magic, thus allowing some to shrug off their spells.

When shaping a spell, the Runegalder rolls a d20! + 10 + their level. All those that would be affected by the spell roll a d20! + their level. If their total is above the Runegalder's, they're unaffected by his magic. This roll is made regardless of whether or not the person wants to be affected by the spell.

ARCANE COMPONENTS The Runegalder gains 3 additional random Rudiments and gains an additional 2 Rudiments every level.

GRIMOIRE This is the Runegalder’s spell book and keeps the spells that he binds to runes. Unlike a normal spell book, however, the spells are scribed in meteorite ink and blood that seals their magic power in the text itself. This means that the Runegalder’s Grimoire does the channeling latently for him.

At first level he constructs 3 spells using his known Rudiments and an additional 1 at level up. These spells can’t have a Drain greater than 7 + their level (so at 1st level, his spells can only have a Drain of 8) when it is scribed into the Grimoire. A spell’s Rudiments cannot be redistributed and changed: spells in the Grimoire are immutable.

Note that spells cast by the Runegalder only last their Interval unless their Effect is stacked, in which case, it either increases that Interval by a like amount or gains the Stacking bonus but not both. This is decided when the spell is cast.

Spells inscribed at different levels count as completely different spells and must be sealed to different runes. So, if the Runegalder has a 8 SP Flash Grenade and a 11 SP Flash Grenade, he would need two runes to cast both. He couldn’t simply bind “Flash Grenade” to one rune and then choose which he wanted to use in the moment.

SKILL FOCUS (Weirdcraft, 1) Through the course of her career, a Runegalder seeks to further their knowledge of the occult. They receive 1 free purchase of the Weirdcraft Skill Suite at every other level up.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

The Runegalder uses his body as a prison for latent magical energies which wears on a person over time. He ages at twice the normal rate.

They also find other types of Weirdshaping strange and so are unable to take another Weird-Adept Archetype as their Secondary, however, they are able to double specialize in their Primary.

Runegalder Double Specialist

VANCIAN CASTING

You can seal a new spell every other level.

ARCANE COMPONENTS

You start with 1 additional Rudiment and gain 3 each level.

GRIMOIRE

New spells have 8 + ( level x 2 ) Drain.

SKILL FOCUS

Skill Focus is increased to every level.

Sourcerer

Choose this Archetype if you want to extremely power and flexibility but don't mind waiting around a bit for it.

An ethereal being in a physical world, the Sourcerer draws his magic from an internal well within them. As such, they don’t cast spells so much as manifest them into existence. Unlike most other weird-adepts, the Sourcerer doesn’t rely on luck or Astral Winds, but instead generates power from within. This is a slower process making Sourcerers less helpful in the moment but more powerful given a bit of time.

VITALITY DIE

d8

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE According to your Secondary Archetype

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

MANIFEST SOURCERY Whether born under a certain constellation or through a long-lost bloodline, the Sourcerer has a special connection to the Painted World. They’re a font of magic, making them very powerful and very dangerous.

Drawing from within is consistent but takes time. Every 10 seconds, you add the 10s digit of the number of SP’s in your pool into your SP pool, minimum 1. So, after 50 seconds of manifesting, you would have 15 SPs ( 1 + 2 + 3 + 4 + 5 = 15 ).

Sourcerers don’t suffer from normal Fallout and can continue to Manifest for as long as they want, however, this power comes with a price. Being a conduit of the unworldly saps their life and every time they add SPs to their pool, they take damage equal to that pool.

Manifesting requires light concentration so they can do other things while shaping spells but if it’s something particularly difficult (like combat or doing mathematics), the Manifesting time is doubled. You can also stop Manifesting at any time but your SP pool will atrophy at the rate of 1 SP per 6 seconds.

POWER OVERWHELMING As the Sourcerer grows, they also grow in power and can stay between two worlds longer. They reduce the amount of damage taken from manifesting by 9 + their level, though they always take at least 1 damage.

TRADITION ATTUNED A Sourcerer is always attuned to a certain Weird Tradition and, at 1st level, knows all Effects from that Tradition and 1 random Rudiment of each type besides that. Starting at 2nd, you can choose a second Tradition. At these level and at every other level you obtain, you may select an Effect from that secondary Tradition or roll for another random Rudiment. At 11th level you gain access to a 3rd Tradition's Effects.
