DRAGON SKIN A Sourcerer is a well of Weird, therefore, to some exact, absorb Weird that is thrown at them but it comes at a cost. When affected by a spell, the Sourcerer can lower the effect by 1 at 1st level and an additional 1 for every 4 levels they obtain.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

Because of Sourcerer is basically a native of another world, their bodies do all they can to shlof off the mortal coil. Every Wound takes 1 day longer to heal

They also find other types of Weirdshaping strange and so are unable to take another Weird-Adept Archetype as their Secondary, however, they are able to double specialize in their Primary.

Sourcerer Double Specialist

POWER OVERWHELMING

This is increased to 12 + twice your level.

TRADITION ATTUNED

At 1st level you are attuned to 2 Traditions, knowing all the Effects from both. Starting at 2nd level and another time at 8th level and another time at 15th, you can choose another Tradition. At this level and at every level you obtain, you may select an Effect from any available Tradition.

Speaker

Choose this Archetype if you want to shape spells quickly and consistently.

There is the surface level of things and then there’s how things truly are. By striking the threads of magic, a Speaker is able to touch reality and bend it to her will, changing it as she pleases. The Speaker has a variable amount of Spell Points available to her, giving her some breathing room as well as more flexibility when it comes to shaping times.

VITALITY DIE

d4

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Lore

Speakers also have a natural talent for languages: They quadruple their Lore when determining their starting Language Rank.

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

ADAMIC COMMAND To know the First Language is to know the words of the Divines, heard as whispers on the mortal plane. Speakers spend decades learning to correctly pronounce each syllable and its meaning; learning the subtleties that each inflection brings. As they grow in power, the words they speak take on more power.

Once the Speaker decides what their spell will look like (Shape, Origin, Range, and Effect) and what its Drain will be, they roll 3d3 (note that these dice don’t explode). If the result is higher than the Drain cost, the spell comes into being. The Speaker is free to roll less dice and/or smaller dice, if they so desire.

Speaking words of power takes actually time, specifically 1 seconds per dice rolled.

If 3 - your current Stress Penalty (minimum 1) of the dice you roll come up as 1s, the Speaker has made a major mispronunciation and the GM rolls for a random Effect from a random Tradition but with otherwise identical dimensions to the spell the Speaker wished to cast.

Since Speakers are not channeling astral power like other magic users, the Stress they gain from Fallout is 6 - their level + number of spells cast in the last 24 hours down to a minimum of 1.

DICTION TRAINING As a Speaker gains experience, she becomes more able to get around the trickier parts of the Divine syntax and so can add more force and power to her spells. Every level, she may either add another d3 to her Adamic dice pool or increase the size of one of those dice by 1 (up to a d12).

LEXICON A Speaker starts with 2 additional random power words or Rudiments to start off and they gain an additional Rudiment every other level.

SKILL FOCUS (special) Through the course of her career, a Speaker seeks to further their knowledge of the occult. They receive 1 free purchase of the Weirdcraft Skill Suite and 2 free purchases of the Language Advanced Skill at every level up.

POLYGLOT Speakers naturally pick up languages in ways that others can only dream of. The Language Advanced Skill is half cost for them and any language that the polyglot gains Rank 4 or above in is considered a native tongue for them.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

Obviously, Speakers can’t have the Stutterer or Mute Flaws. Gaining either of those two Flaws prevents them from shaping.

They also find other types of Weirdshaping strange and so are unable to take another Weird-Adept Archetype as their Secondary, however, they are able to double specialize in their Primary.

Speaker Double Specialist

ADAMIC COMMAND

your starting Adamic dice pool starts at a 4d4s

DICTION TRAINING

You add d4s instead. You can also go up to d20

LEXICON

Increased to 0 additional power words and new one every level

SKILL FOCUS

This is increased to every level

Warlock

Choose this Archetype if you don't mind your power coming from the blood of both friend and foe alike.

The Warlock has gone down a dark path and has begun to unlock the innate magic in all living creatures. As such, they tend to be social pariahs because the process of extracting that magic is random and painful. Still all power has a price and Warlocks happily pay it.

VITALITY DIE

d10

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Weirdcraft Twice

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

THE BLOOD PACT The Warlock has performed a secret ritual and has joined the Blood Pact, allowing a Warlock to instantly pull Weird from the living creatures around him.

This gives him 1 SP per second per person within 10 ft but deals that amount of damage to those he’s pulling from. This includes himself but he also takes an additional damage per second.

This blood pull is unaffected by armor but is blocked by other living beings, if they’re closer. Essentially, if a person would give you cover from a ranged attack, they also protect you from the blood pull.

Otherwise these SPs act exactly like normal and can be instantly used to shape a spell.

This amount is increased by 1 SP and damage per second every 6 levels.

This pull is not stealthy at all as the blood is torn from skin and flies to the Warlock. Additionally, it is not fully controlled and goes on for a minimum of d4! Seconds. A warlock may shape and keep up a spell even when pulling.

WASTE NOT Even when not actively pulling, blood has an innate attraction to the Warlock.

Anytime anyone within 25 ft of him takes damage, part of the spilled blood is drawn to the Warlock, giving him 1 SP + 1 for every 6 levels he's obtained. This is regardless of how much damage was dealt.

Otherwise, this behaves (but doesn't stacks with) the blood pull (including being blocked by others).

DRAIN the VESSEL A Warlock’s own blood is seething in the Weird of the Pact: each damage he takes from the blood pull is worth double the SPs.

FONT of POWER A Warlock’s spells doesn’t come from an outside force but is, instead, projected from him. This results in the Aura Origin having a Drain of 0, instead of 5 and the Touch Origin having a Drain of 1.

However, the Far and Near Origins have their Drains increased by 1.

FORBIDDEN KNOWLEDGE A Warlock gains 2 additional random Rudiment at 1st level and an additional Rudiment every other level.

SKILL FOCUS (Weirdcraft, 1) Through the course of her career, a Warlock seeks to further their knowledge of the occult. They receive 1 free purchase of the Weirdcraft Skill Suite at every other level up.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

People don’t like Blood Magic. By most people’s standards, even at its best, it’s dangerous and random and so Warlocks are not well liked. Warlocks are considered 1 level lower on the Racial Preference table for everyone that knows they’re a Warlock.

They also find other types of Weirdshaping strange and so are unable to take another Weird-Adept Archetype as their Secondary, however, they are able to double specialize in their Primary.

Warlock Double Specialist

THE BLOOD PACT

You now pull blood (and SP) from every person within 20 ft and increases by 1 Damage and SP for every 5 levels.

FORBIDDEN KNOWLEDGE

Increased to 0 additional Rudiments and a new one every level.

Wizard

Choose this Archetype if you power and flexibility but don't mind sacrificing a bit of power for a bit more stability.

Wizards, make no mistake, are still Wild Magic weird-adepts and are no wimps when it comes to raw power, but unlike the Mage that completely gives himself over to the whims of magic, the Wizard uses his study and training to lower the hills and increase the troughs, giving more consistency.

VITALITY DIE

d4

SKILLS & TRAININGS

MAIN SKILL SUITE Weirdcraft

ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

WILD MAGIC SHAPING The Wizard is able to channel the power of the stars, harnessing it and creating magical energy. While doing so the weird-adept must stand still and he glows with light, being illuminated by a column that reaches above them. This light is equivalent to a candle’s brightness.

After 10 seconds, the Wizard gains d10! Spell Points (SP), which is a single pool that can be spent to shape the Weird on the fly out of any Rudiments he knows. The spell’s Drain is then subtracted from the Wizard’s Spell Point pool when he casts it and at the Interval. As long as he has more Spell Points than Drain, he can keep the spell cast.

Let’s say that you have a spell that is Shaped like a Cone (Drain 3), has a Range of Full (Drain 0), an Origin of Aura (Drain 3) and has a Base Drain of 2 from its Effect. That means the Drain of that spell is 8 ( 3 + 0 + 3 + 2 ).

If it has an Interval of 30 seconds, when you cast that spell, it costs you 8 SP and then, after 30 seconds, it costs you another 8 SP, for a total of 16. As long as you have SPs you can keep a spell active.

You can also suffer weirdburn from keeping a spell up too long: if your spell’s Drain is greater than your current SP, the spell is still cast, but you and everyone within 200 ft takes 1 Stress for every point you’re over.

It is recommended that even though you don’t technically get those points until after that 10 second duration, that you roll your SP ahead of time and figure out what you’re going to cast ahead of time. The GM is not obliged to stop the count for you if you haven’t been spending those 10 seconds wisely.

This channeling dice increased by 1 for every other level the Wizard has obtained.

You can stop shaping at any time; however, you take Stress equal to the amount of SP you have left - Weird is a powerful primal force and once unleashed, it is not stopped without cost. You also cannot cast or keep up a spell and Channel. This doesn’t remove those SP but the Wizard does lose 1 SP every 6 seconds.

Wild Magic comes with some additional dangers, however. Should the Wizard roll more SPs than 8 + his level, he suffers a Wild Surge but untrained in it, he is unable to use it to the best of his ability.

The spell is recast, however, its Circularly Shaped at Full Range and with an Aura Origin. They also take Stress equal to how much they were over.

WEIRD MEDIUM The Wizard is a bit more impersonal with his relationship with the Weird, preferring to use Weird Mediums as the fulcrum of the Weird around him. At first level, he may choose one from the following list.

Should he find himself without his Weird Medium, he’s in trouble. His threshold for Wild Surges drops to 5 regardless of level.

Weird Mediums List

ANCESTOR BONES

This magic user was gifted the bones of his ancestors, powerful wizards from ages past that are able to give their descendants some of their prowess.

At 1st level, a Wizard with Ancestor Bones as his Weird Medium lowers his channeling time by 1 second. He also lowers it by an additional second for every 5 levels he’s obtained, down to a minimum of 2.

INVESTED ITEM

This Medium comes in many shapes and sizes. By binding her soul to an item, a Wizard can make a metal object an extension of her power.

While holding this item, she may cast any spell as if the hand was free. For armor, the Invested Item offsets the penalty to shaping by 1 Drain for every 5 levels the Wizard has obtained. This can only offset the penalty, and never lower it below the base speed. For weapons and other items, they may also cast spells with a Touch Origin on a successful hit, storing one spell indefinitely until it’s used. If it is a ranged weapon, Touch spells are cast from the ammunition. Needless to say, this a much favored Medium of battle mages.

ORB

These are often called a Seer’s Orb, as this is favored by Wizards of the Occultism Tradition. Orbs are often glass, but those of other materials are not uncommon, though they tend to be precious metals or stones. The only requirement is that they’re larger than your fist. Orbs bend reality, gaining an automatic increase to any spell’s Range by half of its Base Range for every 3 levels of the Wizard.

SPELL BOOK

A large tome, traditionally, the spell book is the favored Medium of the more scholarly magic user.

The Spell Book is not simply incantations jotted down or notes about rituals - it’s an extension of the Wizard’s brain. As long as he’s touching it, he automatically gains the ability to shape using any Rudiment in the book.

Wizards who select this Weird Medium gain 2 extra starting Rudiments, however, these are only stored in their Book. They also gain a new Rudiment every 3 levels, which is also stored there, meaning that if they lose the book, they lose those Rudiments.

SPELL TATTOOS

Painted Men are common in the frozen tundraof Askemark. The metal heavy ink serves to store channeled magic and allows the Wizard to keep invested power for longer.

With Spell Tattoos, the time it takes to lose a SP when not channeling is doubled for every 4 levels the Wizard has obtained. This also lowers the Stress taken from stopping a spell with SP left by 1 per every 3 levels.

STAVE

Traditionally made of holly wood harvested with a silver sickle at midnight on the night of the new moon, Staves serve as extensions of the Wizard’s soul, much like an Invested Item, but because it’s not made of metal, it holds different properties.

While welding a Stave in one hand, the Wizard offsets the Fallout from shaping a spell by 1 every 3 levels the Wizard has obtained. This can't lower it below 0, however, but does extend to the people within 50 ft of them as well.

FAMILIAR

Favored by the traveling Wizard, a familiar is a small animal or homunculus that is bonded to the Wizard’s soul. Because of this connection, a wizard can see and hear through their Familiar’s eyes and ears as well as channel SP through it, as long as it is standing still, allowing the Wizard full movement even when channeling.

Familiars are small sized creatures. The player selects three candidates, but the GM makes the final decision on which creature came when she called, unless the Wizard opts to have built herself a homunculus.

A Wizard who would get 2 Weird Mediums but chooses familiar twice may select a medium or large sized creature or any small sized creature of her choice.

WAND

The Wand is an exact tool, a tool of precision. It is favored by more aggressive spell weird-adepts because it makes their spells hard to resist.

While shaping with a Wand, the Wizard gains a free Stack of one of the spell’s Effect Rudiments for every 3 levels they’ve obtained.

SYLLABUS A Wizard gains 3 random Rudiments at 1st level and an additional Rudiment every other level.

SKILL FOCUS (Weirdcraft, 1) Through the course of her career, a Wizard seeks to further their knowledge of the occult. They receive 1 free purchase of the Weirdcraft Skill Suite at every other level up.

SKILL ADEPT This character has a knack for skills. All Advanced Skills have their cost reduced by 1 CrP. They also gain a 10% discount to all Skill Suites. This stacks with other Skill Adepts.

PRIMARY DRAWBACK

The Wizard’s study can sometimes leave her with a divorced relationship to reality that can make them somewhat obtuse. When bringing in Traits, Wizards reroll their highest dice roll.

They also find other types of Weirdshaping strange and so are unable to take another Weird-Adept Archetype as their Secondary, however, they are able to double specialize in their Primary.

Wizard Double Specialist

WILD MAGIC SHAPING

Channeling dice is increased to d20! and increases every level. Wild Magic threshold becomes 9 + ( level x 3 ).

WEIRD MEDIUM

You get two and need to lose both before suffering penalties.

IMPROVED ARCANE TRAINING

Increases to every other level.

SYLLABUS

Increase to 1 additional Rudiments + 1 new Rudiment every level.

SKILL FOCUS

This is increased to every level

Flaws

Every person has flaws; little quirks of their personality or odd behaviors. These flaws are often a way of dealing with troubles in their life, letting off Stress or rationalizing their behavior to others. Other times they’re artifacts of a hard life, like a soldier whose missing an arm.

Benefits & Penalties

Flaws in Bonfire are a tradeoff: they’ll make your character less able to do things in certain arenas or harder to be around but allow you to invest in abilities and powers elsewhere. This is represented by the CrP bonus that you get from taking Flaws

Another bonus is that by overcoming a character's Flaws, a person gains confidence and Honor. Essentially, this means by applying your Flaws to your detriment, your character becomes stronger.

This is done very simply by saying that you think a Flaw would make something harder for your character in this situation and then giving yourself a -d4! to your Skill, Attack, or Defense roll or giving your opponent d4! Leverage. Regardless of whether or not you succeed, they gain Honor equal to your penalty.

The GM may award more Honor or inflict you with a larger penalty as seems appropriate for the situation. After all, if it's something your character really struggles with and it gives them a -d8!, it makes sense that they would get an equivalent amount of Honor for overcoming the challenge.

So, note that if you're the one to bring up your Flaws, you get Honor regardless but if the GM has to do so, you only get Honor if you succeed so it is always better to bring them up yourself (unless you have a very inattentive GM).

Gaining Flaws

There are two ways to select Flaws: Rolling and Cherry Picking. Rolling gives you more CrP per Flaw but Cherry Picking gives you more control.

ROLLING FLAWS

Flaw Table Table

1 - 25Background
26 - 50Behavioral
51 - 75Mental
76 - 100Physical

Roll on the first table below and then roll on the corresponding table.

You can spend 1 CrP to reroll at any time but once you’ve committed to a table, you have to roll on that table.

Each Flaw after the first loses 5 CrP of its value per previous Flaw to a minimum of 0 CrP received. So, the 3rd Flaw you roll will be at a -10 CrP.

CHERRY PICKING

For the roleplayers among us with a specific character idea in mind, you may Cherry Pick your Flaws.

Each Flaw after the first loses 10 CrP of its value per Flaw to a minimum of 0 CrP received. So, the 3rd Flaw you pick will be at a -30 CrP.

Flaw Descriptions

While most Flaws can be reasonably looked up, some might need some clarification which is why they're listed below or additional penalties. We've also provided some handy tables you might find useful for figuring out the details of that Flaw.

ADDICT

Addiction
Roll D20Name
1 - 5Drugs
6 - 10Sex
11 - 15Gambling
16 - 20Alcohol

You can, of course, choose whatever addiction you feel fits your character, but we’ve provided a table you can use to generate one for you.

ATHEIST

The way of the divine is a mysterious path, and someone mistake it for no path at all. Some refuse to believe that intelligent higher powers exist and so forfeit some of the blessings while others find worshipping such beings laughable, like giving reverence to the biggest bully on the block.

BLIND, TOTAL

This character has completely lost his sight. He sees only pure white or pure black, unable to sense any movement around him.

In melee combat, they defend and attack with a 1d6! And ranged combat is right out, however, if you insist, you’ll be attacking and defending with a 1d4, so enjoy your fumbles, you stubborn bastard.

Additionally, any Skill Challenges involving sight halves the person’s Skill Rank.

BOAR FACED

This is the polite way of say that someone is ugly as sin. This could be the result of parentage or a bad accident, either way, people don’t like being around them or dealing with them. As mean as it might be, people judge books by their covers.

DARK SECRET

There’s something that this character is hiding and she’s worried that she’ll be found out. She’ll jealously guard every aspect of her life if she can for fear of being found out.

DEBTOR

This character has gotten into trouble financially. This character starts with 5d20 + 150 sc of debt instead of gaining a like amount to start off with. All their equipment much then be purchased on a credit of 50 sc that is also taken out of their debt. If they don’t make payments on it, they may find themselves on the bad end of the law or the loan shark they borrowed from.

DERANGED

There are holes in this character’s brains and he’s starting to slip into madness. The nature of this neurosis is up to the character.

The character doesn’t suffer the effects of Stress until it matches his Wisdom score, at that point, he has an episode and doubles his total Stress. Once, he’s recovered (dropped his Stress back down below his Wisdom), he suffers a permanent reduction 1 to both his Intellect and Wisdom.

EPILEPTIC

Something is not wired up just right in this character’s brain and that causes them to have little short-outs.

When something triggers a Trauma check for the character, or their Stress reaches above their Int score, there is a 1 in 8 chance of the character having a seizure, in which they’re completely helpless for the next 1d3 minutes.

EXCOMMUNICATED

This character has invoked the wrath of an angry god, calling down divide judgement on his head. This is more commonly a member of the faithful who's fallen away or lost his way or willfully defies the cult’s teachings, but less commonly, it’s an outsider whose been declared an enemy of the faith.

Excommunicated members cannot gain the blessings of any miracles related to a single Covenant. Additionally, baleful invocations from priests of the deity that excommunicated them half their threshold.

FATED

Certain character’s bear a strange sign on them that marks them for doom. The cruel strings of fate weave together to form a noose for them.

At creation, the GM rolls 1d8!. This is the number of sessions the character has before Fate begins to sharpen her shears. After that point, the character takes extra damage each time they're hit equal to how many sessions have passed since then.

FERAL

The wild and untamed lands are home to frontier men and families. Occasionally, children escape and are raised only by the wild, occasionally wolves.

Feral characters still receive any free skills from their Archetype but any additional skills they try to pick up can only be from the Atheletics and Survival Skill Suites.

HALF-LIFE

This character has died and forced back to life, maybe against his will. This character is affected by the Force Bind Spirit spell, though the Duration is set to 1d4! - 2 (minimum 1) years and a day. Why he came back is up to you. Perhaps he had some unfinished business or perhaps he was targeted accidently. In any case, now he lives a half-life.

HAUNTED

Mostly commonly, this character has done something to dishonor his clan and has been since been haunted by one of their ancestors, displeased by their actions.

The spirit takes the corporeal form of a rotting corpse wearing its death mask, bothering the possessed at all hours to restore his family’s honor and stop being such a failure. The ancestor will do nothing to protect their descendant and often make life harder for them when they can.

Unfortunately, decades, if not centuries, in the grave have made the ancestor more than a bit senile. Even if the character is to obtain Great Honor, the ancestor doesn’t care; what it really wants is for the character to sacrifice themselves in a heroic way or perform suicide.

This character doesn’t heal Stress naturally and loses 1 Honor at the end of every session.

This Flaw may be paid off for half cost if the character has lasted 2 sessions in Great Honor, however it goes back up to full price if they slip out of Great Honor later.

HEMOPHILIC

These guys love to bleed. Well, they may not love it but they certainly do it a lot more than the rest of us. They take an additional d4 points of damage every time they're wounded.

IDIOT SAVANT

This character was born gifted. Or in other words, they were born with the ability to understand something but nothing else. This character picks an Advanced Skill or Training; all other Skills and Trainings cost double. The chosen Skill or Training now costs half.

IMPISH

This character loves getting into trouble, mostly through pranks of all kinds. While she’s not inherently malicious, her pranks tend to be unwelcome.

IMPOTENT

If this character was a tree, he’d have particularly softwood, if you know what I mean. His lack of confidence in his abilities in the bedroom, tend to affect the other parts of his life, often snowballing; he loses an additional Honor for every 10 lost.

INBRED

Often a curse of the nobility that get too close to their cousins, inbreeding can stunt the mental capacity of their offspring. Typically, this is pretty mild for the most part, but it means that increasing this character’s Intellect score costs double.

LIMP

Something isn’t working just right, whether from a birth defect or a war wound, causing this character to hobble along at a slower pace. Characters with a limp move at half their speed at all times.

MISSING ARM

Most likely this is the result of some terrible accident or horrific war wound, though some people are born with an arm missing.

A character with this Flaw is unable to wield two handed weapons, employ bows or crossbows, or anything else that needs two hands.

This Flaw may be rolled multiple times, with the second time you take this flaw making it worth 60 CrP, as it prevents the character from using any weapons, and makes them unable to cast spells with Somatic components

MISSING EAR

While it won’t limit your ability to hear entirely, the shape of the ear does make it easier to hear things.

The first time you roll this Flaw, all Listening Checks take a penalty of -3.

The second time, all Listening checks are 3 Difficulties harder and your initiative dice becomes one worse. You gain 25 CrPs instead of 20 (in addition to the CrPs from the first time you picked this Flaw up).

MISSING EYE

You can imagine that a character with one eye gone would have an issue with his depth perception. You’d be correct.

The first time a character gains this Flaw, he automatically attacks second when engaging in melee, even if his weapon has the greater reach and everything is counted as two range categories further for ranged weaponry.

The second time this Flaw is rolled, the penalties are replaced by those of the Blind, Total Flaw and he gains an additional 25 CrP.

MONOTHEIST

For this character, there is only one true god, and all other divines are false deities or the work of devils.

He will refuse help from pagan clerics and is bound to only miracles within his chosen Covenant.

MULE

While they may not show it, this character is the result of mixed ancestry and something about their unnatural genesis makes them sterile, unable to promulgate. While this will definitely make creating a dynasty an issue, certain carousers may hardly consider this a Flaw.

NO DEPTH PERCEPTION

This character has a hard time reading distances making it so that he automatically attacks second when engaging in melee combat, even if his weapon has the greater reach and everything is counted as two range categories further for ranged weaponry.

OPUSPHOBIA

Opusphobia is defined by a fear or repulsion of a certain career choice. Someone with this Flaw may dislike horse merchants because he sees them all at crooks or innkeepers because he’s afraid they’re working with the Thieves Guilds.

PASSIONLESS

Whether because of imbalance in their brain or they haven’t really found that thing that calls to them, a Passionless character has problems really being interested in any given subject they try to engage in. Any situation die they gain from their Skills are always one smaller.

POOR

Some characters don’t have the financial leg up that others have. These characters must choose the following Equipment Kit during Step 11 of Character Creation.

You can, of course, choose whatever fear you feel fits your character, but we’ve provided a table you can use to generate one for you.

REFUGEE

Fleeing from their homeland for either economic, religious, or conflict reasons, this character finds themselves in a foreign land. Their flight has forced them to leave much of their belongings behind, halving their starting cash and they tend to be unfamiliar with the language and customs. Their native language is not the main one for this area and the Language and Law of the country they’re fleeing to costs double as they had to learn it under stressful circumstances

SECRET IDENTITY

For whatever reason, whether they’re hiding from enemies, or they want to put their old life behind them, this character is trying to keep their past a secret. When this flaw is rolls, this character selects one of their Archetypes to be the remnant of their past. Any mention of the Archetypes abilities nets this character 1 Stress.

SELF MARTYR

Life doesn’t feel complete if people don’t know how much you’re sacrificing for them.

SENSITIVE

This character has superb senses compared to others; however it makes it challenging for them to function sometimes as they can just get overloaded.

SENSITIVE HEARING

This character is incredibly prone to noise. Other’s normal talking voice sound to them like they’re yelling. You’ll think this would help them suss out noise more effectively but instead it makes it harder to hear because there’s too much sensory input.

TALKER

Whether around the campfire or in stressful situation, this person can’t keep their mouth shut. They’ll just talk and talk, only stopping to take necessary breathes.

THRALL

Thralls are those taken in raids or the children of slaves. Technically, they’re ‘free’ but they have a social stigma that follow them. Thralls gain no extra starting cash and half the amount of equipment the kit normally starts with and starting a Confrontation with someone of high status automatically gives you 3 points.

VOW of POVERTY

The Middle Realm corrupts and those that wish to come closer to the Gods’ Realm sometimes eschew worldly possessions. This character only keeps enough wealth on them to buy basic food to sustain them for that day, all other wealth is donated to any local cults. They give their goods to the needy, not fellow adventurers. Their Max Favor is increased by 1.

Character Vitals

The purpose of this chapter is to condense all the rules for calculating things about your character so that it can keep the other chapters to just rules you’ll need at the spur of the moment during gameplay. To this end, these rules are missing why they’re important and what you’ll actually use them for, but they do reference the chapter where more is to be found.

Stress

Working under pressure can get to you. When your crew mates are relying on you to pull out a win, it can mess with your head. Your character can become stressed under these circumstances and stress can later manifest in odd behaviors.

Characters can gain Stress in a lot of ways and those are discussed in their various sections - taking damage, making Skill Checks, etc. - the only one we’ll go over here is from acting against your character’s Characteristics, especially when not playing them would be a huge benefit.

STRESS PENALTIES

Stress affects almost everything you do, making your life harder and your character becomes emotionally pent up.

Every 10 points of Stress gives you a penalty of 1 to Defense and Skill Check rolls.

Honor Through Accountability

In the heat of the moment, it’s hard to keep track of all the bonuses and penalties that apply to situations, especially the penalties and especially Stress penalties, which change during the fight.

Because of this, it isn’t required that you apply Stress penalties. However, if you do, you gain 1 Honor and the other side also applies their Stress penalty without that extra Honor.

If the GM reminds you that you need to apply your Stress, you don’t get anything but the penalty.

HEALING STRESS

Stress heals slowly over time but there are several things you can do to speed it up.

The first is to give into his nature. By role playing his Flaws in a detrimental way, a character can relieve 1 or more Stress (GM’s option, although it should be about the same amount of Stress healed as was applied by the penalty). This means that when a character sees a situation where his Stress could give him a disadvantage, he can bring it up the GM. If approved, the character heals Stress. The GM may also suggest this option as well if she things the situation warrants it.

The second way is through hobbies. Hobbies are based off your character's Confrontation Characteristics, but besides that, they can be anything, from whoring it up to spending time with the family or working in their shop.

You gain 1 point of Relaxation for each hour spent on a hobby. You can get additional Relaxtion per hour but you'll need to spend money. Specially, each sc spent per hour gives you an equivalent amount of Relaxation.

So, if you're spending time on your hobby (we'll say blacksmithing) and you rent out an actual forge at 2 sc per hour for 3 hours, that would mean that, at the end, you'd gain 9 Relaxation (1 free + 2 for the sc spend * 3 for the number of hours), but it would cost you 6 sc.

Finally, you can indulge in creature comforts. This can be done by buying a nice bedroll or even hiring someone to set up your camp for you so you can relax at the end of the day. The rule of thumb is that each applicable Trait the equipment you have gives you an additional point of Relaxation when applicable. So, an extra soft, double padded, and tailored bedroll will always do you good, but a waterproof tent will really only give you a bonus in inclement weather.

When your Relaxation matches your current Stress, you heal 1 Stress and your Relaxation drops to 0 again. Yes, that means that the more Stressed you become, the harder it is to decompress yourself.

Also, as an aside here; the Musician and Cooking/Baking Advanced Skills also help heal Stress, so you can look into those.

MENTAL BREAKDOWNS

When your Total Stress is more than your Wis * 3, called your Stress Threshold, you've gotten to the point that you just can't take it anymore. This results in a Mental Breakdown for your character.

When this happens, they do everything in their power to separate themselves from the stressor as quickly as possible. If they're in a scenario that directly threatens their life (like combat or dangling from a cliff), they'll separate themselves as quickly as possible but will pay little attention to their companion's safety. At this point, they're so overwhelmed, they don't really care.

A character having a Mental Breakdown can still gain Stress but should they gain enough to go over twice their Stress Threshold, they suffer a heart attack and die.

Even if your character doesn't suffer a heart attack, they'll be shaken and changed from the experience. When they dip below their Stress Threshold again, they lower 2 Traits by 1 dice.

Vitality

Vitality represents how close you are to passing out and dying. It is both your health and stamina. As you take damage, you will get closer to death and gain more penalties based on your Fatigue.

Vitality is divided into 4 categories which are, in order, HURT (H), BLOODIED (B), WOUNDED (W), CRITICAL (C). Each of these make up a fourth of your Vitality.

To calculate your base Vitality add a roll of your Primary Archetype’s Vitality Die to your Constitution + their Vitality Size Modifier.

Divide that by 4: that’s the amount of the Vitality in each Category. Your Trauma Threshold is twice that (rounded up). Trauma is talked about more in Chapter 9: Combat.

For fractions on Wound Categories, round up on Hurt but down on the rest.

Record your Vitality Die roll on your character sheet.

FATIGUE

As stated, the more damage you take, the harder the fight becomes. When this happens is noted by your Fatigue

Fatigue is matched to a Wound Category: hitting that Wound Category means that you start rolling your defenses, skill Checks, and Appeals on 1 dice smaller.

Your Fatigue starts a Critical, however, it can be lowered by wearing armor and wielding shields you're not fully trained in.

CHANGING EQUIPMENT WHILE WOUNDED Since Fatigue is partly determined by the shield you're using, a quick way to up your Fatigue is to simply drop you shield.

Now, the flip side of this is that if you become MORE encumbered while wounded, you could get Fatigued quicker.

TAKING A BREATHER

Pausing and resting for 30 minutes heals you half the damage and Stress (rounded down) that you've take since the last time you've Taken a Breather.

If the rest is broken for any reason, you lose all benefit from it.

HEALING

Combat is dangerous. Even if you survive, you could end up with wounds that you carry with you for months on end.

Each time damage is done, it is tracked in a new wound.

Wounds heals at a slow rate. Each point takes a number of days equal to the damage done to heal it 1 point.

So, a 5-point wound takes 5 days to become a 4 point wound, which takes 4 days to becomes a 3 point wound, and so on. That means it takes 15 days to completely heal ( 5 + 4 + 3 + 2 + 1).

Thankfully, each wound heals simultaneously. So, if you have 3 separate 4 point wounds, you’ll be completely healed by day 10.

RECUPERATION (HEALING WITH RELAXATION) Another option you can do to speed up long-term healing is to rest and indulge yourself.

If the only Stress your character has is from Wounds, any points of Relaxation gained that day are taken off the days to heal off your Wounds.

This is somewhat limited however since you can only drop a single Wound's days to heal by the amount it had left on that Severity. So, if I have a 10 Severity Wound, with 8 days of healing left, gaining 11 points of Relaxation, would only reduce it to a 9 Severity Wound with 9 days left to heal that day. However, if I also had another Wound, I could use that otherwise wasted Relaxation on it.

Honor

Honor is a measure how not only how a person measures their own integrity but also how other people see them. Honor isn’t about doing the commonsense thing; it’s about doing the heroic thing. People who run from a fight, even when outnumbered, lose Honor. People who let others talk bad about them and don’t get even lose Honor.

The question of Honor isn’t a question of good and evil; many evil men have been honorable. It’s more about living up to the ideals of your culture and being true to your inner self.

BONUS CrP

Bonus Honor
Honor of Last CharacterBonus Crp
Great Honor50
High Honor35
Average Honor25
Low Honor10
Dishonor0

If this is your first Bonfire character in a campaign, you receive a bonus 25 CrPs.

If you’re here because you’ve had a character die, this bonus CrP is based on the Honor category your character was in when they died.

STARTING HONOR

The Honor category in which you start is determined by your “Start Honor”, listed under your Charisma. You start at the bottom of the corresponding category.

HONOR CATEGORIES & BONUSES

Honor has its benefits. Confidence allows you to push yourself a little bit more than you otherwise would. During the game, you can spend your Honor points to influence anything, rolls or static metrics, whenever you want on a 1 to 1 basis. Doing so lowers your Honor but might save your character’s life. So, if you roll a 13 and your opponent rolls a 14, you could spend 3 Honor to beat their total. Likewise, if an enemy deals 8 damage to you and you have 6 Honor, you could spend all of it and only take 2 damage.

Additionally, each category has an Honor Dice, which can be rolled to add or subtract like Honor.

Honor cannot go above 25 or below 0. The size of the Honor Die is also determined at the beginning of session and doesn’t change during play even if the category does.

DISHONOR (0 - 5 Honor, No Honor Die) The lowest category, this person is unsure that they have what it takes to be a hero and so every decision is laced with hesitation and uncertainty.

LOW HONOR (6 - 10 Honor, d4!) This character hasn’t really proved anything, one way or another. Others and herself are waiting for her to make her mark on the world.

AVERAGE HONOR (11 - 15 Honor, d6!) Having reached this category, the character has shown that they have potential and some follow through.

HIGH HONOR (16 - 20 Honor, d8!) She has now separated herself from the common rabble and can stand a head above the crowd.

GREAT HONOR (21 - 25 Honor, d10!) This rare sliver represents those who can perfectly balance being ahead of others but not so much so that they invoke the ire of those below them as well as being confident while not being cocky.

END OF SESSION HONOR AWARDS

At the end of each session, the players will elect each other’s characters for things they think that character deserved Honor for. It is generally poor form to elect yourself but is also reasonable if you pulled off something amazing and the rest of the group didn't seem to notice.

These elections need to fit into one of these three categories:

STRENGTH This character demonstrated strength based on how their character’s culture defines strength, which could be physical prowess but could also be cunning or grifting.

MASTERY This is given when a character solves a tricky problem or came up with a creative solution. Note, this shouldn't be given for good rolls unless the players want to lose Honor for bad rolls; this is about out of the box thinking.

COURAGE When the chips were down, did your character give up the fight or did they really show what it means to be a hero and stare down death?

ROLEPLAYING Did the player really role play his character? Where his decisions about what he thought gave him the best chance to win or was it about what his character thought would be a good idea? Note, that since players are electing each other, jackasses who use “that’s just what my character would do” to dick over the party won’t get rewarded for this much. This should be specifically linked to a character's Confrontation Characteristics.

GAINING HONOR DICE Whenever you go up an Honor Category, you gain a free use of your Honor Dice. Also, when you reach 25 Honor, you get one as well, even though you didn't technically go up a category. Once used, they go away but they stay with your character as long as they live.

Certain Archetype abilities may also give you them temporarily, in which case, the Archetype will note for how long you have them.

For each of these categories, the GM can also dock Honor from a character. Did they run away, or did they conveniently forget any Characteristics that would have screwed them over?

That and spending Honor are the two main ways of losing Honor.

Skills

Skills are used as a way to determine the success or failure of a given action, based on what your character knows about the given subject or about how to perform the given task.

You don’t have to use these rules all the time, i.e., you don’t have to roll to see if your character successfully walks across a room, but at times they’re a good way to semi-randomly determine the outcome of a tricky task, i.e., walking across a room full of traps.

Skill Introduction

There are two types of skills that you’re going to be pulling from: Skill Suites and Advanced Skills.

Skill Suites represent broad swathes of knowledge that cover a variety of subjects. Suites are hard to increase because there’s so much ground to cover but can be used if you don’t have the specific Advanced Skill. An example of this is the Survival and Lore Skill Suites.

Advanced Skills are more tightly focused, covering one intellectual discipline. They’re easier to master but may not be applicable in every case. An example of this would be the First Aid, Fire Building, and Foraging skills in the Survival Skill Suite and the Law, History, and Medicine skills in the Lore Skill Suite.

ACQUIRING SKILLS

Throughout your character’s career, she’ll acquire and improve her skills. Both types of skills are purchased with CrP, that is spent either at Character Creation or on leveling up. All skills have a unique cost that represents how easy or difficult they are to master. You pay the price as noted in the section below, you improve the skill.

CALCULATING RANK

SKILL SUITES For all your Skill Suites, your starting Rank is 0, unless noted in the following example:

ADVANCED SKILLS Your starting Rank for Advanced Skills is the Rank for the mother Skill Suite.

PURCHASING A SKILL Advanced Skills cost their Base Cost + (Current Rank * 2), while Skill Suites cost their Base Cost Base Cost + (Current Rank * 5). If you have Skill Adept, both have a minimum of 1.

Every purchase increases your Rank in that Skill by 1. Purchases of Skill Suites also raises the Rank of any child Advanced Skills you’ve already purchased, so that’s nice.

SKILL SPECIALIZATIONS

It often pays to specialize. After all, many dissertations cover extremely minute subjects with incredible depth and drawing on that well of knowledge can be a huge benefit.

Skill Specializations represent an area of knowledge within an Advanced Skill that your character spends extra time versing themselves in. As such, they gain a bonus.

Skill specializations come in layers, modifiers that narrow down the field. Each layer gives a +1 to your effective Rank when it comes into play.

There may come a time when a specialization only kind of applies. In this case, it may be kind of helpful, as the max bonus that can be gained from it is +1.

So, when encountering a land predator in the Uchka Mountains, all three monster hunters would only gain +1 to their Rank.

That sort of super-focused study takes a lot of time and effort and man only has so much time and energy to give. The total number of specializations per Advanced Skill that a character can have is equal to half his Intelligence score.

A character can gain a specialization like any other skill; having his character go out of the way to learn more about his craft. The price is the base cost of the Advanced Skill times the number of layers in the specialization plus one.

A character can go back and increase the number of layers in his Skill Specialization after his initial purchase of it, but it costs additional amount of CrPs equal to twice the base cost of the Advanced Skill.

The Basics (Skill Checks)

Before we go off talking about Skill Challenges, time, equipment, and all those other things, it’s first important to understand the very basic mechanic all of those things will hang off of: Skill Checks.

Skill Checks are any checks made that move the Skill Challenge along and/or determine a success or failure.

At their very basic, Skill Checks have both sides rolling a d20!, adding any applicable Skill’s Rank, the Skill Modifier based on the Skill’s relevant stat, and any modifiers for difficulty. The person with the highest total wins and you successfully bypass or eliminate the Obstacle, depending on the situation.

If a Skill has more than one relevant stat, use the lowest modifier. A space on your character sheet has been provided to record this to make referencing during play quicker.

It is assumed that your character is trying their hardest to be successful in whatever they attempt and so any Check you make inflicts d4! Stress if they don't succeed by more than 5.

Answering a Question

Another use of a single use Skill Check is answering a question that you don’t know the answer to like “out of these two walls, which looks easier to climb?” Things that would be reasonable for them to be there, but you don’t know because you didn’t prepare for that question.

Skill Challenges

Skill Checks refer to a single roll against a single Skill, while a Skill Challenge refers to a host of Skill Checks. To use a metaphor: a Skill Challenge would be breaking into the castle. The Skill Checks would be climbing the walls, hiding in the shadows, sneaking past the guards, listening at doors, lockpicking any locks, etc.

OBJECTIVES AND OBSTACLES

A Skill Challenge doesn’t exist without something that your character wants and at least one thing that stands in their way.

This could be something straightforward: I want to get out of this jail cell, but a locked door is in my way, or it could be something more complicated like I want to capture this outlaw but he’s several days’ ride ahead of me.

These are your Objective and Obstacles, respectively.

Achieving your Objective is a matter of beating or getting past all the Obstacles in your way.

Obstacles are beaten through successfully rolling Skill Checks, which will be discussed more in the next section. Note that an Obstacle can continue to be a factor that needs to be considered, for example, a guard patrol, or it can be something that only needs to be taken care of once, for example, unlocking a door.

Obstacles also have Failure Threshold, which represents badly you have to fail against them to actually fail. More on this in the Complications, Boons, & Hard Failures section below.

The Single Check

Before we dive in, I think it's worth saying that there may be times when you have something that might call for a Skill Check but not a Skill Challenge. Most often you'll do this when there is danger but not a huge time crunch, like, for instance, players leaping over a cliff or when there’s a chance of failure, like the player not knowing a monster weakness.

In that case, it would be perfectly reasonable to just call for a single Jumping (or Monster Craft) Check. If the players want to do some Preparation or use any of the other tools at their disposal, they can.

Or, if there is a time crunch but it is so narrow players really wouldn't have the time to prepare, like having to jump the chasm while a horde of brigands with bows are closing it, you might also just default to the single roll: no need to break out these rules in that case.

In these cases, the Failure Threshold of the Check would be 1, meaning a failure is a failure, but you can spice it up by having the jump almost make it but now the player is just barely hanging out: however, much time you want to spend on it.

DIFFICULTY

Difficulty is a dice that is added to the Skill Check based on things that might be going on at the time to either help or hinder your success. This difficulty is noted just as a single dice (+d6!, for example) but you'll add a d20! to it by default.

Obstacles can have static, variable, shrinking, circular, growing, or universal difficulties. They can also be linked together.

STATIC means that the dice pretty much stays the same, outside of player interaction. This is often used for one off checks and not really used as the main part of a Skill Challenge because, let’s face it, doing the same Check over and over again isn’t that interesting.

What you'll mainly see is Static Difficulties linked together in an Obstacle. So, for instance, a rock wall that is slippery at the base, then has a section with a lot of handholds, and finishes with an overhang, would be three separate Checks, the first with a d12! difficulty for the wall, the next with a d4! for the players, and the final with a d10!, again for the wall.

SHRINKING means that it starts high but then the dice shrinks as time passes, often becoming static at a certain point. This is when the threat becomes less and less severe, and I would use this sparingly and with other types of Obstacles, but it can represent the fact that leaving a place is often easier than getting in.

GROWING is the opposite of shrinking: it starts low and then increases as time passes, again, sometimes becoming static at a certain point. This is used to represent threats that continue to grow, often times when there is time pressure.

UNIVERSAL This is a term for an Obstacle that will go off at sometime but won't be directly faced by the players. It represents a chance encounter, such as running into someone randomly, or a stroke of bad luck, like bad weather. Unlike other Obstacles, players won't make Checks directly against it but any Failure (or Success) against another Obstacle in that Challenge adds a like amount of Failure (or Success) to any Universal Obstacles.

This can also be used for timed Challenges, such as a chance or encroaching deadline. In that case you not only count both Boons and Failures, as they represent time passing, but also questions your players ask count as 1 Complication, representing them taking time to get stock of their surroundings, which you oftentimes don’t have as much time to do under pressure.

CIRCULAR means it starts at a difficulty, grows to a certain difficulty, and then shrinks down to its original difficulty, rinse and repeat, ad nauseam. It can also start shrinking, if you’d like. This is often used as patrols, like guards and such, but also a monster stalking an area would be represented by this type of Obstacle though you would have it be a bit more random to represent that unpredictability.

LINKED Obstacles are Obstacles that whose outcomes affect one another. So, for instance, if the players are in a wagon chase down a rocky road, with one player at the helm, stirring, and the others in the back firing crossbows, how well the player of the reigns does affect the attack rolls of those in the back. In this case, add or subtract the number of Complications or Boons to the Check of any linked Obstacles.

Note that Linked Obstacles will also be paired with another Difficulty type.

Multi-Layer Checks

Let's say that you're trying to deduce facts about bears before you go to fight one. The thing is, there is a lot to know about bears and your character probably isn't going to know all of it, so making a single Check is too binary while making multiple Checks is too tedious.

In steps the Multi-Layer Check.

In this case, the GM would assign Difficulty Dice to the different facts about bears based on how esoteric the knowledge is. He would then roll 1 d20! and all of those Difficulty Dice. You would only roll a single Check and the compare that to the difference totals to see if you recall those facts.

"Pausing" the Skill Challenge

The players don’t always have to be making Skill Checks during a Skill Challenge - they should only do so when it makes sense.

So, (using the above example) if the patrols aren’t very good and the guards get too far away from the players to reasonably hear them, no Check should be required.

But that doesn’t mean that time stops: if the players wait long enough, the guards will return, and Checks will need to start up again.

COMPLICATIONS, BOONS, & HARD FAILURES

Failing a Check doesn’t automatically mean that you’re instantly screwed: Failing a single Move Silently Check doesn’t result in the guards catching you. In Bonfire, there are Complications and hard failures.

Every Obstacle will have a number of Complications it can gain before it hard fails. This is called its Failure Threshold. You gain Complications by failing Skill Checks: every 5 points below what you needed to get gives the Obstacle 1 Complication, rounded up (so a failure by 1 - 5 is still considered a Complication).

Complications represent complications, such as the guard hearing something, or you leaving a clue behind that might give someone a heads up that you're there. An Obstacle gets +2 for every Complication is has on it.

When an Obstacle gets more Complications than its Failure Threshold, it hard fails. Hard failures are when something bad actually happens. In this case, it does result in you getting caught by the guards, or it results in your falling off the wall and taking damage. Even after a hard failure, you can sometimes try again, like in the case of falling off the wall.

Failure doesn’t diminish during the Skill Challenge, but it does reset for a new one.

BOONS are the opposite of Complications: they give you a small benefit or boost for accomplishing a test extra well. You get 1 Boon for every 5 full points above what you needed.

Complication in the Narrative

Complications don’t mean that the Skill Challenge grinds to a halt while the players keep reattempting that Skill: instead, it should represent the players coming closer to danger.

Strategies

ASSETS

These represent static pools of knowledge or information that you can pull from if you have time. So, for instance, a book on the subject, or a library are examples of an Asset but also an old friend who used to be a ranger and who could give you a few pointers could also be considered one.

Anything you can think of that might apply might be an Asset you can draw on.

Assets have two stats: their KNOWLEDGE and their ORGANIZATION. Basically, how much they know and how easy that knowledge is to get.

Each of these is given a qualifier of either POOR, AVERAGE, or GOOD.

For Knowledge, Poor represents a +3, Average +6, and Good +9 while for Organization Poor is Days, Average is Hours, and Good is Minutes.

Spending 1 unit of an Asset’s Organization gives you +1 bonus up to their Knowledge. So, if you’re searching through a poorly taken care of but extensive library (Knowledge: Good, Organization: Poor), spending 5 days there gives you a +5, while spending two weeks there only gives you a +9.

That bonus can then be redeemed on a Skill Check later on. Although it can only be redeemed once, it does apply to any rerolls made against the same Obstacle.

You don’t automatically know the Rank or the Time Investment of an Asset. This can also be applied to Weapon, Armor, and Shield Trainings through manuals and sparring.

Another benefit of Assets is that it is often multifaceted and can be used to get different bonuses. That old ranger friend can help you with navigation but also probably knows a thing or two about botany.

Assets can also be increased and expanded upon as well, increasing its qualifiers. A good relationship with a contact might give you information quicker, donating to the local library may increase its selection, or hiring excavators to dig up a ruin may unearth more artifacts that help you decipher that ancient script.

There may be some special cases where an Asset will take care of itself, but you may have to check back on it, such as Snaring in the forest. You set your trap and then a day or two later, you can go back and check it to see if you caught anything - in the meantime, you can get other work done.

REDEEMING CONTACTS Characters get a number of starting contacts based on their Charisma, with the expectation they'll gain more as they adventure, but these starting contacts can prove useful as they can be redeemed at any time and defined on the spot.

After that, of course, contacts can be used time and time again: they're part of the world.

How a contact helps is largely determined by the circumstances of why they were redeemed but the GM should, for the most part, consider them Assets starting with Poor Knowledge and Organization. A player can increase that when they redeem a contact by sacrificing additional contacts, raising one of their stats on a one-for-one basis.

ROLEPLAYING OUT A SCENE VS USING ASSETS Assets are not meant to replace specific roleplaying areas where you need specific pieces of information: they’re meant to reward players for remembering to do otherwise boring and mundane things that might still help their character. You can also combine the two.

Using Other Players as Assets

I think it's completely reasonable that players would want to use each other's characters as Assets and why shouldn't they? So, in this case the player’s Knowledge is instead based around the Rank they have in the applicable Skill with their Organization being based on their Characteristics.

If they have 3 or fewer Characteristics related to teaching or communication, they’re considered Poor; 4 to 6 they’re considered Average; greater than 6, Good.

GMs should also feel free to reward players who sit there and talk things out and plan by awarding the Asset bonus as well, even if they don't spend a full hour+ planning.

EQUIPMENT

Your kit can really pull you through in a pinch and these are catchall rules for the use of equipment that doesn’t already come with auxiliary benefits, such as weapons (damage) and armor (DR).

Players are assumed to be using all equipment that would help them with a Check if they have time so they shouldn’t feel the need to go through their list of climbing gear every time they scale a wall, although, if time is short and they need to rush, that may be appropriate.

On a Skill Check, the first piece of equipment you use gives you a free reroll, taking the higher of the two results. After that, each additional piece gives you a +1, although if this additional gear has Traits that apply, you can use that instead of the +1. More on equipment Traits is found in the Deluxe version of Chapter 10: Equipment.

Redeeming this bonus causes the tool degrades, giving it (and any other equipment you use) 1 Wear, whether you succeed or not. More on Wear can be found in Chapter 10: Equipment.

Assets & Equipment Based Skills

Some skills are only going to be useful if you have the proper equipment or the right Asset. For instance, if you’re not out in the wilderness, you can’t really use Snaring or if you don’t have the proper tools or a woodshop, Maintenance won’t do you any good. In cases, being able to make the Check in the first place is considered an auxiliary benefit and so this bonus doesn't apply. This will need to be handled on a case to case basis.

HELPER SKILLS

Let’s say that you’re tracking someone in the wilderness. You have Hunting at Rank 4 and Endurance at Rank 3. Seems like being able to move quickly over a longer period of time, should help you catch the guys, and it does.

If you have another Advanced Skill that you think might help you, you can add it as a bonus, however doing so costs you d4! Stress for every Skill you apply. This can't be reduced by Not Sweating It.

This may seem like it is nearly identical to Preparation, and they are very close. The difference is that Preparation is a general thing that applies to a Skill Check you’re going to make in the future, while using a helper Skill is in the moment and is specific to the scenario. You can use both at the same time, since the help Skill gives a bonus and Preparation gives a reroll.

Skill Mobbing

For GMs, note that Helper Skills are how you handle Skill Mobbing, where everyone just overpowers a roll by all rolling against it. Instead, only one person rolls and only those with an applicable Advanced Skill and willing to take that Stress add their Rank to help out.

MULTI-TASKING

Let’s be realistic here: you’re probably going to end up trying to do two things at once, like climbing a wall and doing so quietly.

If that’s the case, you’re going to have to “split” your d20! into smaller dice and assign those to each of the Checks you’re trying to make, because your attention is divided. The total max value of the dice can never exceed 20 but it can be lower than it. The other side will still be rolling full d20!s against you.

So, if you’re climbing a wall and trying to do so quietly, you’d have to make a Climbing and a Move Silently Check. You could split it like so: d12! for Climbing and d8! for Move Silently, or d10! for Climbing and d10! for Move Silently, or d12!+d4! for Move Silently and d4! for Climbing.

Or you could just say “screw being quiet” and roll a d20! for Climbing and take a 0 for Move Silently. In this case, the GM would just roll against your Skill Rank. So, if you choose to ignore Move Silently but have a Rank 4 in it, the GM would roll their dice, and you can hope they don’t roll higher than 4.

Either way, besides this, it works like a normal Check, except that, for the Stress gain, you're going to roll 1d4! for each Skill they're attempting but only use the highest if applicable. They need to succeed all Checks by 5 to completely remove the Stress gain.

Not Paying Attention

Multi-Tasking is also used when someone isn't paying attention, such as a guard who's on watch but he's been there for several hours at this point so he's not doing it so closely. In this case, start at a d10!, lowering it further as needs be.

Helping Others

It feels good to help people and Bonfire is all about group cooperation. The fighter helps the skill monkey survive combat and the skill monkey helps the fighter not look like an idiot while doing detective work.

And how you help other characters will really depend on the situation. Perhaps your Preparation can be used to help another person hide or perhaps you have a bit of knowledge that they don’t.

Really, this will be done to what feels right in the moment, but this note is here to draw attention to someone helping you as an Asset and someone adding their Rank to yours with a Helper Skill, and how they’re different.

And the difference is time. If you have plenty of time to coach someone while they’re climbing a cliff face, you’d be an Asset and you wouldn't take Stress.

But if you’re being chased by the guards and it’s a matter of seconds or minutes, you’d add a Helper Skill and you would need to take the Stress.

Note that if the skill monkey is also trying to climb the cliff face and coach as they go, that would be considered a d10! worth of effort for Multi-Tasking, though you don’t have to actually roll to see if you help.

NOT SWEATING IT

While the default is to assume that characters actually care about the outcome of the Check, that's not always the case since not everything is equally important. In the cases of lesser importance, the character can simply not sweat it.

In this case, they take no Stress from the Check but take a -4 penalty.

PREPARATION

Preparation is anything your character does to help a specific Skill Check that will be made in the future (even if that future is 2 seconds from now). Note that this doesn't have to be a Check you make: it can also apply to an ally's Check (if it makes sense).

Usually, these only take a couple of seconds but can vary widely depending on the circumstances. Throwing a rock is a matter of moments while constructing a gilly suit will take a lot longer.

As long as there is time, there is no chance of failure or, if the players have plenty of time, Preparation just happens. Mark what you did for later in the Skill Challenge.

However, if there is a time crunch or a chance of failure, Preparation works like a normal Skill Check with success means the preparation is actually useful.

Either way, you only get one Prep Check per Advanced Skill that applies for each upcoming Check, unless you have Assets but remember that they do take time.

That means that if you know you're going to have to make a jump, you can use Acrobatics to stretch, Endurance to do a few practice sprints to the edge, and Sports (long jumping) to remember techniques all to prep for the same Jump check.

When you redeem Preparation that you’ve readied, you can reroll Obstacle's d20, taking the worse of the two results.

Planning & Action Phases

While it isn’t entirely black and white, it’s helpful to think of Challenges as composing two phases: planning and action; the laying out the plan and then the heist.

Planning is gathering intel, getting your team and equipment together, and planning your route of attack. This is where you’ll use Preparation and Assets mostly.

Action phase is when you’ll be doing a lot of the Checks and Stress, as well as equipment and companions - using what you learned in the Prep Phase to help you get through the sticky parts.

But don’t get too hung up on separating these ideas though. Even during the heist, you might find it worth your time to sit on your heels and take your time while doing some Preparation as there will almost certainly be problems that crop up that you need to adjust to.

RUSHING IT

If you’re in a hurry to get the job down, you can just rush it. This lowers the time a Check actually makes but gives you a -5.

The bonus for this is that Complications you would get from the Check don't get added to Universal or Linked Obstacles in the Challenge, though Hard Failures do add 2 Complications to them.
