ATHLETICS SKILL SUITE

This suite covers all things that require physical prowess and, to a lesser extent, pure manual dexterity.

Check to Not Slowdown
SpeedDifficulty
Walking+d4!
Jog+d8!
Run+d12!
Sprint+d20!+d4!

ACROBATICS This covers your character's ability to stretch their body, do flips, and turn cartwheels. This allows the character to vault fences without slowing down or roll to avoid falling damage.

Reference the Check to Not Slow Down table to calculate the base Difficulty to, well, not slow down when you encounter an obstacle.

To reduce falling damage, remove 10 ft from the effective fall distance for every Boon you get.

CLIMBING This Skill covers climbing and repelling up and down walls of various heights and textures.

Difficulty should be based on height, with about every 40 ft increasing the Difficulty by 1 dice size.

Textures should also play a major factor in not just how tough the Check is but also how many Checks need to be made for a given wall.

So, if there’s a wall, where the base is stone at a 45% slant for 20 ft, then it moves to close knit stones for another 40 ft, and then finally to a wood overhang for just 5 ft, and then to a wooden wall for 10 ft, there would be 4 Climbing Checks in this order: +d4!, +d10! (d8! for base but because it’s 40 ft, it gets bumped up 1), d10!, and +0.

ENDURANCE Through training, a character can push his body past the limits of his base physical ability. The Rank of this Skill serves as DR against the damage you take while Running or Sprinting, although specifics are given in the Actions section of Chapter: 9 Combat.

ESCAPE ARTIST This allows the character to escape bonds and restrictions and is always rolled opposed, either against the Rope Use Skill of the person who tied them or against the quality of the manacles or binds the person was put in.

The character can make a straight +0 Check, not to break the bounds or get free, but to instead move his body to an advantageous position.

JUMPING When you need to cover a distance without touching the ground, jump.

Typically, a character can jump 16 inches vertically or 5 ft horizontally without a Check, however, if they wish to go further, they’ll need to roll.

Each Boon adds 2 inches to the vertical jump and 6 inches to the horizontally. Starting at a run doubles this.

Small creatures half these numbers while Large creatures double them.

SPORT (SPECIFIC) This covers the actual playing of a specific sport as well as an in-depth knowledge of the game’s rules as well as famous players and techniques.

If it becomes a plot point, the GM should feel free to make this Skill apply to only certain positions, like pitching or shortstop but this a fantasy roleplaying game so I doubt that’ll happen.

Move Silently Speed
Dice to Roll onSpeed
d20!Crawling/Strolling
d12!Walking
d8!Jog
d4!Run
0Sprint

MOVE SILENTLY When you want to move silently, you’ll want to use this Skill. This involves being able to feel your way along and compensate for creaks.

This is always an opposed Check vs any potential listener’s Listening, with a failure indicating that the listener has heard something suspicious, though the person attempting Move Silently may not be aware that they were detected.

Moving at speeds greater than a Crawl or Strolling speed is considered Multitasking. Refer to the following table for what to roll.

SWIMMING This Skill allows a character to not drown in water.

The Difficulty of the Check is determined by the water (or other liquid, I don’t judge) you’re attempting to swim in, though simply trying to float on your back and letting the current take you gives you a +d8! to your roll, though it is risky because you could get pulled into an aquifer or get pulled over a waterfall but that’s the chance you take.

LORE SKILL SUITE

This suite covers general knowledge, which is mostly academic in nature. Most of it is pretty heavy stuff but the basics are second nature or stuff that’s been picked up here and there.

ADMINISTRATION While they’ll never inspire the awe or respect that other leaders do, people who oversee the day to day functions of an organization keep the lights on so that others can make the speeches.

Administrators can make a Check at +0 to gain a clue about an item the party might need on their adventure, or one to retroactively remember that they did buy an item back at the market for just such an occasion.

Each of these Checks they make increases the Difficulty of the next one by 1 step.

HISTORY Everyone knows certain large events, but few can tie those events into an overarching narrative and understand their effects on later events.

The History Skill allows a character to not just recall events but also to link them to the present day, to certain traditions and rituals of a culture, or the behavior of certain members of a culture, giving insight on how to proceed.

LANGUAGE (SPECIFIC) A character receives this Skill for free in their native tongue with a Rank equal to their Int and it allows them to speak and be understood by others with Skill in that language.

Checks are only made when timing is critical, such as communication in a battle, or when understanding is key, such as when debating foreign policy.

If one of the characters is in a Confrontation with another in a tongue that’s not their native one, that person can only bring in as many dice per round as he has Ranks in that Language.

Additionally, when two native speakers are in a Confrontation, the one with the higher Language Rank gains an additional dice (see Applicable Skills in Chapter 8: Confrontation ). In case of tie, nothing happens.

The Lore Skill Suite can’t be used in place of a Language Check for tongues you don’t know unless you have the Language Skill in a related Language. Using a real-world example, someone with the Language (Swedish) Advanced Skill couldn’t use the Lore Skill Suite to understand a person with Language (French) but could use it when talking to someone with Language (Norwegian) or Language (Danish).

LAW (CULTURE) This Skill covers the intricacies of the legal system, including landmark rulings and common punishments for common crimes. A character can make their case or find loopholes to exploit the legal system.

A character’s Lore Skill can only be used to substitute for their native culture but not others’. If the character does wish to branch out, his mastery of Law for that new culture starts at 0, as he must learn everything from the ground up. Diving more into his own culture’s laws (buying this Advanced Skill for his culture) uses the Lore Skill as base, as per usual.

LITERACY (ALPHABET) This Skill allows a character to read and write in a language’s alphabet, giving them the power to pen books and poems, or passive aggressive notes. A character who's taken the Lore Skill Suite is considered to be literate in their native language's alphabet.

This Skill can be taken multiple times, each instance representing mastery of a new writing system. The scribe can then use that alphabet to pen any language they know, in the same way that we could use the Latin Alphabet to pen Arabic or the Korean Alphabet to write English.

To decipher a text, the person needs to know both the alphabet it's written in and the language it's using, which most of the time won't matter but can be used as a cheap way to do a cypher in a pinch.

MATHEMATICS While this may seem like just a Skill that allows you to be able to juggle figures and add totals and calculate the area of a circle like a huge nerd, mathematics has a more practical use: correctly guessing distances.

While you can try to eyeball how far away something is, a Mathematics Check vs +0 allows you to do rough calculations, giving you the ability to know exactly what penalty you’re going to get for using a ranged weapon or who's going to be affected by the Area of Effect of a spell you’re going to cast.

MEDICINE With proper treatment and nursing, a wound that would lay you out for weeks, may only keep you down for a couple of days. This Skill involves the knowledge of long-term care, when bandages should be changed, which poultices will have the greatest effect, and what minor surgeries need to be performed.

A character with this Skill can make a Check for a wounded person, adding the Severity of his largest Wound to the opposing roll.

So, if a person has a 5, 3, and 8 Severity Wound, he can make a Medicine Check vs d20+8.

Success means that the person can take 1 day off the healing time for every Wound every time it drops a Severity.

So, a success against a 5 Severity Wound means that it was treated properly and takes 10 days to completely heal ( 4 + 3 + 2 + 1 + 0 ) instead of the normal 15.

You may also increase the Difficulty modifier by half again as much - if you succeed, you take 2 days off per Severity. So, if you're against a d20!+9, you can make it a d20!+14 ( 9 + ( 9 / 2 ) ) for that bonus.

Additionally, when resisting Poison, Toxin, or Diseases, you can add your Medicine Rank, rounded up, to each round of the Confrontation.

MONSTER CRAFT This Advanced Skill is under both the Lore and Survival Skill Suite but still counts as 1 Skill, so you don’t have to buy it twice - they share their Rank. It simply represents the different ways that each Skill Suite approaches the craft.

Monster Craft gives you insight into the creatures that roam the Middle Realm. Simply put, each Boon gives you a (truthful) answer to a question.

Difficulty is based on how common the monster is. Common is +0, uncommon +d6!, rare is d12!, and legendary is +d20!.

RELIGION (CULT) This Skill acquaints the character with a knowledge of cults, their common Covenants and Miracles, as well as their hierarchies, means of advancement, and important members.

It also allows a character to gain a knowledge of their rituals and sacrifices, as well as the taboos of their clergy and how to appease their heavenly messengers and avenging angels.

The Religion Skill is taken for a single Covenant, but can be purchased independently for different Covenants.

A character adds the tens digit of this Skill to their chance of gaining Favor when making sacrifices to the god of that cult.

WORLD CRAFT This area of study covers the topography of the Middle Realm. It’s forests and rock formations and biomes. It helps predict whether or not it’s going to rain or whether the next summer is going to be a hot one.

Predicting what’s coming in the next hour is a Check vs +0, with the Difficulty increasing by 1 dice size for each time you double the prediction window. So, detecting the weather in the next 2 hours is vs +d4!, while doing so in the next 16 hours is vs +d10!.

STREETWISE SKILL SUITE

This suite covers knowledge that a character might pick on the street or in the school of hard knocks. While Lore is book smart, Streetwise is street smart.

CURRENT AFFAIRS A character with this Skill is well informed about the day to day affairs of regional powers and men and women of importance, their dealings and alliances, as well as their hatreds. He can pick out celebrities and know how and why someone got rich and famous.

They can also use this Skill to guess the Honor category of someone by watching how people react to them and letting them know about certain NPCs' Reputations.

Deception Check
DifficultyLevel of Lie
+0White Lie
+d4!Lie of Omission
+d6!Mostly True Lie
+d8!Half Lie
+d10!Mostly False Lie
+d12!Absolute Lie
+d20!Absolute Lie with Easy Evidence Against It

DECEPTION This covers all sorts of deception, where you want the person to believe the opposite of the truth, or, to put it simply, when you want to lie to them.

The level of Difficulty to pull off a lie is based on how much of what you’re saying isn’t the truth, strictly speaking. This is always opposed by either the other character’s Deception or Perception but only if the character has reason to suspect that you’re lying to them.

Even if you succeed, this isn’t a permanent way of changing their mind. New evidence presented to that person may cause them to rethink their opinion on what you tried to sell them so be careful about what falsehoods you spin.

FORGERY Mostly commonly used for creating fake currency, forgery is a Skill that allows a character to reproduce something effectively and fool others. This Skill acquaints the character with common forging techniques and knowledge with what possible agents will be looking for.

The forger must also have the appropriate corresponding Craft or Trade Skill, so he can’t forge coins if he doesn’t have the Metalworking Skill, though that’s within reason: a character forging an official passport with one at hand doesn’t need to have Literacy as he can just copy the letters, though he may also need to have Artistry (wood cutting) to create the heraldry on it, but someone trying to forge an official declaration from scratch does need to have the Literacy Skill in that language plus Artistry (wood cutting).

Forgery is opposed by Perception, the applicable Skill, or Forgery but only if the character looking has reason to suspect there’s something else. A lazy guard probably won’t Check your passport too closely right before lunch, but a particularly astute one who's on the lookout for a promotion will.

GAMBLING/GAMING This Skill doesn’t give the character a gift for winning games, just that he knows the rules and knows the odds, which could in turn lead to him winning the game.

INTUITION The ability to understand people and get where they're coming from can help you figure out what will and won't work with them better.

A Check vs +0 allows the character to get a feel for how open a person would be to a Confrontation over something or what would be definite deal breakers for them. It doesn't reveal any of their Characteristics or their strengths as it's more of gut feeling than anything.

Each Check on the same person increases the Difficulty by 1 dice size.

They can also use it to confirm their theories about what Characteristics a character has. The player needs to make a reasonable guess about the Characteristic first - so players who’re simply throwing out guesses automatically fail.

This is done at a Check vs +0 to start with but increases by 1 for every dice size per guess, whether the character succeeded at the last ones or not.

LISTENING While Perception handles the other senses, Listening has to deal with your character’s auditory senses. This goes beyond simply hearing something: listening allows the character to know when an otherwise innocuous noise is actually something to pay attention to though it might not always be apparent why at first.

Lock Picking
Lock DifficultyBase TimeTime Off
+01 Minute5 Seconds
+d4!5 Minutes30 Seconds
+d6!20 Minutes2 Minutes
+d8!30 Minutes3 Minutes
+d10!45 Minutes5 Minutes
+d12!1 Hour10 Minutes
+1 Dice SizeAdd. +15 Minutes+5 Minutes

LOCK PICKING It takes a lot more know-how than you might think to pick a lock.

The amount of time it takes to pick any lock is based on your Skill level and the quality of the lock. Subtract the Time Off * their Boons from the Base Time.

PERCEPTION This covers four of the five senses that a character has: sight, touch, taste, and smell. Technically, your character is always receiving inputs from these senses, but Perception helps filter out the unimportant ones. Can he detect if there are orcs in the nearby bush? Can she taste the hidden poison in her drink before she swallows? These are all Perception Checks

Like Listening, sometimes Perception will help the character notice something that may be important, even if it’s not obvious why it’s grabbing your attention.

SLEIGHT OF HAND This Skill covers all things that require you to do quick, delicate movements with your fingers. This may be slipping a card up your sleeve, picking a pocket, or doing cat’s cradle while bored.

SURVIVAL SKILL SUITE

This suite covers everything that a character might need to survive in the wild; Knowledge of what plants to eat and the Skills to hunt and breed animals.

BOTANY This gives a knowledge of what the herbs used in cooking, alchemy, and medicine look like in their natural environment and it allows you to identify their common uses. It also helps find food in the wilderness.

If halving their overland travel speed, a person with Botany can make a Check every travel period: if they succeed, they can consider themselves 1 step up on the Long-Term Exhaustion table. So, if they had nothing, they could consider themselves Rationing.

If they choose to stay put, a success nets them 2 steps up.

4 or more Boons results in doubling their output, meaning they possibly found themselves enough food for the next day.

Mostly, this is used for detecting poisonous plants, which is Check vs +d4! but is a common Helper Skill for both Medicine and Cooking/Baking.

FIRE BUILDING Against the cold, lonely nights out in the wild, there is only the fertility symbols you carve for yourself and the roar of the fire. This Skill allows you to build one of those things: the fire.

Under normal conditions, it takes about 30 minutes and a Check vs +0 to set up and light a fire, assuming you don’t have to go far out of your way to find the wood.

FIRST AID This gives the character a crude understanding of battlefield medicine: making splints and staunching wounds.

A character with this Skill can make a Check for a person wounded in that last 30 minutes, adding the Severity of any Wounds that he's treating to the opposing roll.

So, if a person has a 5, 3, and 8 Severity Wound, he can make a First Aid Check vs d20+16 or he can choose not to treat the 8 Severity Wound and make a vs d20!+8. Success means that the person can take 1 level of Severity off those Wounds. So, a 5 Severity Wound drops immediately to a 4 Severity Wound. You cannot go back and do a Check for a Wound that you skipped.

You have 30 minutes to perform First Aid Checks for a person, with each Wound taking 3 minutes, if applicable.

You may also increase the Difficulty modifier by half again as much - if you succeed, you hit 2 points of damage. So, if you're against a d20!+9, you can make it a d20!+14 ( 9 + ( 9 / 2 ) ) to heal 2 points of damage.

HANDLE ANIMAL (SPECIFIC) This Skill deals with the handling and care of a specific animal, from birth to the slaughterhouse. It also deals with training and common illnesses to make sure the stock is healthy and virile.

While most Checks are handled like normal knowledge Checks or on a case-by-case basis (such as calming down your animal during a storm), using a question-and-answer style, this Skill is also used for training, with the base number of tricks you can teach an animal equal to their Int (note that carrying things and handling a bridle are two different tricks).

The animal needs to have both the basic temperament and physical ability to learn a trick (no sheep becoming pack animals and no dogs learning to pick locks). The GM may increase or decrease this for particularly smart/dumb and obedient/obstinate animals.

After a month of training, a roll is made vs +0. If successfully, the animal learned the trick. If not, another Check can be made in a month, although every failure increases the Difficulty to learn that trick by 1 dice size.

The base price of this Skill is calculated towards domesticated animals. If the player wishes to learn how to deal with wild animals, this Skill costs thrice as much to purchase.

HIDING This allows a character to make the most of a situation or environment to cloak themselves against prying eyes. This is always opposed by Perception, with the Difficulty determined by the area. Characters can also use this to instantly get an idea of how well they can hide in the given space.

MONSTER CRAFT This Skill is the same as the Monster Craft under the Lore Skill Suite. Look there for details on it.

NAVIGATION Either using the stars or the position of the moons and sun, this character can track their way even through the most untamed wilderness without getting lost. It also allows them to tell the time.

Without proper equipment, a character can only give rough estimations of where they are, anchored on larger geographic features (like mountains or rivers but not towns or roads) to the nearest 10 miles.

SCAVENGING There’s a gift in high-speed appraisal. This is often used by those picking over battlefields for anything they could sell, but it’s also found a niche with adventurers who use it to find food and sustenance while traveling away from civilization.

A Check vs +0 tells a character which of two things considered is worth more. This can’t be used for coinage, but can be any other type of good. It also gives the character an idea of whether broken equipment can be reasonably salvaged.

This doesn’t give even a ballpark of what anything is worth, but it only takes a few seconds of consideration.

If using this Skill to scavenge for food, use the rules presented in the Botany section, however, two or more Complications results in you eating something poisonous.

SNARING This teaches the character how to properly create and place snares to trap smaller wildlife. It also gives some cursory knowledge on the best places to put them.

Snares have a chance of giving you food once a week, although you’ll only actually roll when you Check them. Every Boon you get gives you half a day’s worth of food.

HUNTING Most of the time, you’re not going to down your query in one go, and so the hunt is on as your watch for subtle signs of their passing. While this Skill was originally used to hunt wildlife, it has been repurposed by wardens and bounty hunters trying to capture the most dangerous game.

The Hunting Skill can be used to track your prey, get a sense of their movements, and predict where they’re going. It can also give insight into common and uncommon natural creatures.

If you’re using it for food, hunting is a boom or bust strategy: at the end of each full day you spend hunting, roll a Check.

For each Boon you gain 2 days’ worth of food, but either way, you gain 1 damage from exhaustion and possibly more if you suffer a Complication.

USE ROPE Covering all kinds of knots and bindings, the Use Rope Skill is pretty self-explanatory, though it should be noted that you can also use this Skill to get a sense of the tensile strength of a rope or how much you’re going to need for a certain job.

To keep your players on their toes, I suggest you make the Check, not when they tie the knot, but when it’s tested.

TACTIC SKILL SUITE

Combat isn’t just about raw physical power, but more about how it’s directed and used. This Skill Suite deals with logistics and making the most out of what you have.

COMBAT STYLE (STYLE) By studying the best tactics and how to fight in certain circumstances, a warrior can take advantage of his surroundings and combat styles emerge. Combat Styles can be anything but involved in parts: a situation and a metric.

This situation is when the Combat Style is most effective. For instance, it can be “in the forest”, “fighting on rooftops”, “being outnumbered”, “being in a duel”, “fighting while prone”, etc. Really anything (as long as your GM approves).

The second part of the Combat Style is the metric applied to. This can be anything you could normally specialize in.

Both the situation and metric are selected at the time of purchase and cannot be changed.

If the situation is applicable, the character receives a +1 to that metric for every 2 Ranks of that Skill he’s obtained.

So, a character with the Combat Skill (unarmed fighting, attack) at 5 who gets into a tavern brawl gets a +2 to attack as long as he doesn’t draw his weapon and simply uses fisticuffs.

Having a high Rank in Tactics doesn't automatically give you Combat Style bonuses under all circumstances and buying this Skill for the first time starts it off at Rank 0, instead of the Tactic Suite's Rank.

Distraction Check
DifficultyTime
+01 Minute
+d4!2 Minutes
+d6!5 Minutes
+d8!10 Minutes
+d10!30 Minutes
+d12!1 Hour

DISTRACTION More than simply yelling “hey, look” at someone, the art of distraction is the art of holding people’s attention.

The amount of time that someone is delayed is based on the Difficulty of the Check and how bent on their current activity they are.

On a success, the person (or persons) is distracted for the amount of time according to the Difficulty * half the number of Boons, rounded up.

This isn’t magical: an obvious threat to their person will cause the person to focus in.

This Skill is less effective when the person knows they’re in immediate danger. In this case, as long as they’re not actively engaged in melee with someone (in which case it’s an instant failure under most circumstances), the person is distracted for seconds, instead of minutes.

Each successive Check’s Difficulty gets increased by 2 dice sizes in these cases.

LEADERSHIP The difference between a leader and an administrator is that the latter gets stuff done and the former gets others to get stuff done but hooking into what they believe and how they view themselves.

Assuming you have a willing audience, you may make a Leadership Skill Check vs +0 pointed at a Characteristic you think the person or group might have.

If you succeed the Check and they have the Characteristic you’re looking for (or close enough - you don’t have to be exact), you increase their Panic threshold by 1 step for the next d4! hours. Gaining 4 or more Boon increases it by 2 steps.

You can increase the number of Characteristics you’re aiming for by increasing the Difficulty dice size of the Check by a similar number.

QUARTER MASTERING There’s an art to packing and making sure that everyone is well fed and prepared. If the quartermaster is using a personal container of any kind, he adds 2S for each Rank he has in this Skill. Otherwise, he adds 1S per Rank. This also applies to any person he packs for.

RALLY When manure hits the windmill, no speeches or grand narratives will keep a person from bolting. Only the cold will of a competent commander can keep a battle from becoming a route.

A captain who successfully makes a Check vs +) for someone who is currently over their Stress Threshold, heals that person a number of Stress equal to 3 * his number of Boons. This is opposed by the enemy captain, if applicable, and each Check against the same target increases the Difficulty by 1 dice size, regardless of whether it was successful or not.

RECRUITING Knowing where to find the right person is a crucial Skill for any long-term expedition. A character with this Skill can find a random person willing to hire on with a Check vs +0 in 2d6! days.

Now, finding specialists or someone with a certain Skill is another matter. Every additional criteria increases the Difficulty by 1 dice size.

Where you’re looking also makes a difference, as well.

This doesn’t guarantee that the person found will take the job or doesn’t have some serious issues, like a crippling fear of dogs: it only guarantees that they have the Skills you’re looking for and that they’re somewhat interested in being hired on. Pay and comfort make a lot of difference to a prospective hire.

RIDING This Skill teaches a character how to maintain their stability while on horseback and makes them capable of feats of equine prowess.

The bonuses for this Skill are varied and many with the specifics spelled out in Chapter 9: Combat under the Mounted Combat section so they won't be listed here. Seriously, go Check it out.

SIGNALLING This is the knowledge of how to communicate over long distances, either using semaphore, smoke signals, signal lamps, or horn blowing.

When using this means of communication, each side rolls a Check based on how complicated the message is and how quickly they need to send it.

Signaling is an ad hoc language with no grammatical rules or complicated tenses and so even at the best of times, only simple messages can be sent.

WARFARE The Warfare Skill hands directing troops on the battlefield, weighing options, and devising plans on the fly.

Those with this Skill can roll it to temporarily pause combat to ask one question and receive one answer from a specific member of the party, or to simply tell them something. On top of this, you can also use this, out of combat, to confer with players who’re characters are not present in the scene.

Checks start at +0 Difficulty but increase by 1 dice size each time they’ve been rolled that combat.

Warfare also has additional benefits and uses that will be outlined in Crowns of Fire, the kingdom management and mass combat supplement for Bonfire.

TRADES SKILL SUITE

This suite covers the crafting and creating Skills. While there are a wide array and breadth of professions, this list is pared down to those areas of knowledge where the common man and the adventurer overlap in their needs.

APPRAISAL (SPECIFIC) It’s wise to know what something is worth before selling and buying it. This Skill handles that and is taken for a specific type of good, such as books & scrolls, livestock, jewelry, arms & armor, and so on.

If a character has the appropriate Skill covering the item he’s looking to sell/purchase, a Check will tell them what kind of deal they're getting on the item - how much they’re being ripped off or how much of a steal it actually is.

Additionally, the character should get a bonus if he has any Skill that’s applicable to the thing he’s purchasing.

ARTICULATION You may think that the truth is powerful enough to carry your argument, but you can be beat out by a master of deception. Articulation is the Skill of rhetoric and formulating the truth in such a way that makes it the most convincing.

The level of Difficulty to convince someone is how much evidence you can supply to back up your arguments. This is opposed by Deception or Articulation but only if someone is actively trying to deceive or convince the same person as you.

Note that the Difficulty of their Deception Check may add bonus dice to your Articulation Check.

Even if you succeed, this isn’t a permanent way of changing a person’s mind. Others may lie more effectively than you can tell the truth and that may cause them to rethink their opinion on what you tried to sell them.

ARTISTRY (SPECIFIC) While some may not find the Fine Arts a worthy way to spend time, others may disagree. Artistry covers all artistic endeavors, including painting, sculpture, embroidery and anything else that is done for art’s sake.

COOKING/BAKING On the road, a hot meal can count for a lot. A character who has a hot meal gains 1 Relaxation for every soft success the cook had on their Check.

On top of this, a character can prepare otherwise unpalatable or poisonous food in such a way as to make the most of it, though it is a Check vs d12! to do so.

Unless the character is trying to prepare a feast worthy of His Imperial Majesty, basic daily cooking only requires a Check vs +0.

CRAFT (SPECIFIC) This Skill covers any Skill that makes something that isn’t noted here, such as carpentry, tailoring, basket weaving, pottery, etc. The GM may adjust the price for a particularly difficult to master study.

LEATHERWORKING From the moment it leaves the beast to the moment the final touches are finished, leatherworking handles the process of making and crafting works from the hides of animals, including skinning and tanning.

MAINTENANCE The Skill of tinkers and adventurers, this gives the person a general knowledge of easy and ad hoc fixes that can be done on the fly.

A successful Check lowers the Wear on the item by 1. The level of Difficulty in repairing something is equal to the Wear on the item, rounded up to the nearest dice size.

So repairing a spear with 1 Wear is a d4!, while repairing one with a 5 Wear is a d6!.

Another Check can't be made until the item gains more Wear.

METALWORKING This covers the process of changing crude ore into a beautiful weapon, armor, or decorative piece. It also covers the construction and repair of more mundane things, like plows, but if you’re picking this Skill up, I doubt you’re doing it to corner the farmer’s market.

MUSICIAN (SPECIFIC) This covers the mastery of specific instruments, including singing. At the end of the day, the dulcet tones of a neatly played mandolin can ease the ache of a long day.

A character who hears someone play an instrument gains 1 Relaxation for every Boon the player had on his Check. This doesn’t stack with others playing; however, you will take the highest roll and use that to determine Relaxation. It also does no good if you’re in a stressful situation, like being hunted.

Unless the character is trying to serenade a queen, basic daily ditties only require a Check vs +0.

PERFORMANCE This Skill covers everything from making your case before a court or a stirring speech before charging into battle.

On a success, anyone listening gains a temporary Devotion to what the performer wants: whether that’s themselves or an organization or a case. If the Devotion already exists, the size is temporarily increased.

The Devotions strength is equal to the number of Boons the performer had.

WEIRDCRAFT SKILL SUITE

The science of the Weird is an oft studied but little understood branch of knowledge that requires a deep knowledge of the nature of the Painted World.

With this Skill Suite, someone can identify a spell, point out needed regents and processes for ritual shapings, detect if something is touched by the Weird and what its properties are, or even detect if a spell has been cast in an area, and have a chance of finding out what it was.

ALL ADVANCED WEIRDCRAFT SKILLS Unlike other Advanced Skilled, the Weirdcraft Advanced Skills pretty much work the same and so don't need their own section.

The first bonus that having an Advanced Weirdcraft Skill gives you is that it gives you further insight into a particular Weird Tradition, allowing you to detect it better. For more information on what each Tradition specializes in, head over to Chapter 11: The Weird.

The other thing it does is allow you to shape cantrip versions of spells from that Tradition, regardless of Archetype. The ability to shape is inherit in all living things though it takes decades of practice, a strong family bloodline, and/or a natural gift to do what Weird-Adept Archetypes do, a form of practical "folkweird" is often passed down as part of the tools of the trade.

This doesn't, and will never, allow someone to shape the full version of a spell but it can give them a boost or an edge. The specific details should be left up to the GM and player, but they should always be appropriate to the Tradition and never be more powerful than a spell that does the same thing. Most commonly this will mean it will get used as a Helper Skill.

Shaping a cantrip is still shaping and is stressful and so that anytime any of these Skills are used to shape, the shaper gets 2d6! Stress.

Confrontation

Your character is a multi-faceted representation of a fictional persona. She has her hopes and her dreams, her strengths and her weakness. All of these add up to hopefully make someone that has a compelling story of victory over her flaws, or defeat from the same.

In game play terms, these are represented by 6 characteristics:

GOALS represent what your character is trying to achieve.

TRAITS represent what sets your character apart from other characters.

DEVOTIONS represent their relationships, either with people, organizations, or otherworldly powers.

REPUTATION represent how other people see them - what are they rumored to have done or what kind of people do others think they are.

FLAWS are also considered Characteristics so they're back!

These characteristics will be provided dice that will be used in Confrontations addressed below and represents how strong it is, with the bigger the dice, the better it is.

Goals

Characters can start with up to 3 Goals, but needs to have at least one at all times. They receive Experience and Honor, as well as increasing the other 3 Characteristics, as you progress along the path to completing them.

What does you character want? Why can’t they get it? These are the two fundamental questions that should be answered for each Goal.

Overlapping Characteristics

You may think you’re pretty smart by having a Trait and Devotion both be the same thing so that you always get to roll them at the same time. However, consider that you’re putting your eggs in one basket and it would be worth it to vary it a little to cover more bases, allowing you to use them more often and perhaps leveraging characteristics to bring in others.

Ideally, they should include other party members and the overarching plot of the campaign.

These goals can be anything from the incorporeal (“I want to find a home” or “I want to deal with this anger inside me”) to the very concrete (“I want to find my father’s sword” or “I want to stop this invasion”).

The best goals are those that are measurable and obtainable.

Being motivated by a Goal allows you to push yourself beyond what you thought was possible. When a Goal applies to a Confrontation, when you lose an Appeal, you take half the Stress.

Starting Characteristics

If you’re bringing in a new character to a new campaign, it’s highly probable that you won’t know what the game is going to be about, especially if the GM wants to keep it a secret.

It’s perfectly acceptable to leave your Goals, Traits, and/or Devotions blank until you’ve got your feet under you, but you should have at least a few Medium term goals and your strongest Trait filled out relating to your character’s personal arch.

Traits

Trait Dice

Traits are things that stick out about your character. Things that people tend to notice about them or that the character defines his identity by. These can be something specific (“I have blonde hair”) or something general (“I have an intimidating demeanor”) or somewhere in between (“I’m an orc”).

Traits don’t have to be physical in nature. It could be how your character views himself (“I’m confident” or “I’m good at math”). They can also be something about your character that he just can’t explain (“I’ve always been good with dogs” or “I can read people easily”).

The sky's the limit when it comes to Traits, so go wild, though they can't have exceptions. So, "I'm an angry person" works but "I'm an angry person but I don't let it affect my work" doesn't.

You start off with 5 Traits of varying levels: 2 weak, 2 average, and 1 strong. These are represented by dice of varying size. How strong these Traits are depends on your Charisma. So, if you have a 13 Charisma, you gain 5 Traits - two at d4, one 2d6, one 2d8, and one at 3d8

While naturally charismatic characters come out of the gate with strong personalities, as you adventure, your character will also grow and change, gaining and strengthening their Traits. This can be done by either increasing your Charisma, which also raises your Traits, or by buying Traits up directly.

Thinking of Traits

Thinking of Traits on the fly is hard. For new players, there's two ways of handling this: either picture a character from fiction you like or find interesting, and try to describe them. These are their Traits, and you can crib off them to start with.

Or if you have no idea where to start or are just a risk taker, you can use the Trait Generator, which will give you a random Trait. These Traits may not always make sense, but they can often serve as a jumping off point for your imagination.

You can find it in Chapter 9 on the Bonfire SRD

ASSIGNING YOUR TRAIT POINTS

If you want a little more control over your Traits, their strength and how many, instead of just accepting what's on the above chart, you can use your Trait points from Charisma to modify your Traits how you will. You start off with 5 Traits of varying levels: 2 weak (1d4 each), 2 average (2d4 each), and 1 strong (3d4). This is instead of what you would have gotten.

From there, you buy up your Traits using those points in the same way as if you were buying them up with CrP.

You can also then go back and further increase them with CrP but only after you're done using all your Trait Points.

INCREASING TRAITS WITH CrP

Trait Increase Cost
Weak (1dX)Medium (2dX)Medium (3dX)Strong (4dX)
Xd4741010

Xd123201026

If you want to increase your Traits further, you can spend CrP to give them a boost. This represents your character spending time developing their personality rather than spending time learning other things. If you built your character using the free version of the rules and are now switching over to Deluxe, you can refund your Trait buy ups to redo them, but only once.

Weak, Medium, and Strong Traits all cost different amounts to raise. Why? Well, in the Basic game, there was a very simple strategy to winning and we wanted to keep things simple so you could learn the basics. Now we're giving you the power to try different ways of convincing people so we needed to make sure the numbers made sense and that you weren't "wasting" your CrP were it wouldn't benefit you, so you'll notice that Weak Traits actually get cheaper the more you buy.

You can also buy new Traits for the base Xd4 price.

Please note that you can't buy a Trait past a d12

Starting Characteristics

If you’re bringing in a new character to a new campaign, it’s highly probable that you won’t know what the game is going to be about, especially if the GM wants to keep it a secret.

It’s perfectly acceptable to leave your Goals, Traits, and/or Devotions blank until you’ve got your feet under you but you should have at least a few Medium term goals and your strongest Trait filled out relating to your character’s personal arch.

Racial Temperament

Your Racial Temperament also tends to come into play fairly regularly during Confrontations. Like a Trait, you can add its dice in an Appeal. But what is the dice size? Well, it's your Honor Dice.

So, basically, if your Racial Temperament applies, you get your Honor Dice that round. Pretty easy, pretty straightforward.

Devotions

The final aspect are the Devotions that your character has. What relationships does he have? What organizations does your character associate with? Is he religious and, if so, is his loyalty more to his cult or to his god? How does he feel about that thing?

Relationships between individuals don’t need to be reciprocal or even contemporary. A young fighter may be inspired by a girl who doesn't love him back or by a long dead king he greatly admires. These are still viable candidates for his Devotion.

Everyone receives two free Devotions: one to their character’s clan/family and another of their choice. Each Devotion comes with a "relationship verb" and the thing itself. So, his clan Devotion could be "Hate Clan" or "Have mixed feelings about Clan" or "Loyal to Clan"

These Devotions start a 2.

Devotions are a more powerful driving force than other Characteristics, meaning that, if a Devotion applies, you automatically subtract 1 point for every point you have in it. So, if you approach a blood enemy, trying to convince him to help you, even if you’re being entirely reasonable, it’ll be much harder to do so.

BUYING NEW AND INCREASING DEVOTIONS

All new Devotions start at 1 and cost 4 CrP to purchase. From there, you can increase their size which costs 6 + (2 * your current Devotion). So, to go from a 2 to a 3 Devotion, it'll cost you 10 CrP ( 6 + ( 2 * 2 ) ).

Reputation

Reputation, in a nutshell, is what your character is known for and how other people see them. So, if you want to convince someone that you’ll keep your word, having a Reputation for doing so will help you out.

Reputation takes the form of 3 incomplete sentences starting with “I’m known for...”. Each time you level up, your GM will finish or change out one or more of those sentences and assign points to them that represent their strength. She’ll choose how to finish them based on how your character has been acting or the results of their actions.

That’s right: just like in real life, you don’t really have control over your Reputation, though there is a way to influence it as you go.

In a Confrontation, Reputation counts as a form of Evidence, but instead of getting the standard 3 points, you instead get the Reputation’s strength in points. It can be combined with other Evidence or adds a number of Honor Dice equal to its strength if you're using it as an Appeal.

Flaws

Let's circle back to Flaws because they are considered part of your Confrontation Characteristics, after all, they make up who your character is as well. You start with your Flaws giving you 1d4! + your current total Stress you have in Confrontations should you bring them in.

Using your Flaws in such a way is extremely relaxing and so removes any Stress gained during that Confrontation.

When To Use These Rules

These rules may not be appropriate to break out every time two people talk to each other, or even disagree on something. They’re more of a framework that help you track how compelling a side is and, you’ll find, that you can quietly use these rules in the background as your players roleplay.

While there are other reasons to start a Confrontation, they’ll mainly be started by you for a specific purpose: things situations are covered by the Game Master’s Guide so what we’ll talk about here is when to know when a player-initiated Confrontation should happen and that’s fairly easy.

Think of your NPCs in terms of their GOALS and METHODS. Goals are pretty obvious and map one-to-one with the Goal Characteristics, but Methods are how they get things done based on their Characteristics. Methods are kind of the NPC’s morality.

If the NPC feels like what the player is asking them to do aligns with their Goals and their Methods, no Confrontation happens: they don’t need to be convinced.

If, on the other hand, the Goal aligns but the Methods do or if the Methods align but the Goal doesn’t, a Confrontation is a great tool for determining whether the NPC agrees.

And if neither Goal nor Method aligns, no Confrontation happens: The NPC can’t be convinced.

Of course, if you think it’s reasonable, the players can enter into a Confrontation to convince the NPC that their Goals and Methods align, but that’s up to you and how much the players are trying to abuse it.

Playing Out the Confrontation

The Confrontation is done in a series of back-and-forths called “rounds”, in which each person is trying to get the other person to back down. This involves an argument-counterargument structure.

A round starts when someone puts forth an argument and ends when the other person feels they’ve countered it or they’ve had to concede, so a round can be multiple exchanges with each side talking back and forth, asking and answering questions.

Both sides begin with points equal to any applicable Devotions they have, with the side who didn’t starting with an extra 1 point.

Arguments come in two flavors: Evidence and Appeals.

EVIDENCE

Evidence is facts: things that are believed to be true, even if they’re not true in actuality.

These are flexes in power: I’m the king and so do you a favor if you do this for me.

These are also things you know about the other person, or subjects involved: if you know that a person is caring or has a temper, you can use that against them as Evidence.

If your opponent concedes to your Evidence, you get 3 points, otherwise no one gets anything. Note that the only thing your Evidence needs to be considered counted by your opponent is the fact that your opponent believes it, honestly.

So, while a normal person has to concede to the sky being blue, a color blind one could counter with the fact that the sky isn’t blue to them and that’s valid.

Evidence is the surest way of convincing your opponent, but it also tends to be more work: you have to know about your opponent and know their situation.

Generally, this is signaled by placing a finger up in the air or pressing it against the table.

APPEALS

Appeals are appeals to a person’s emotions, their sense of self, or their Honor.

Traits are often (but not always) used this way. It can sometimes be a jab at someone’s character or an insinuation of skill, through bragging about how good of a climber you are or maybe displaying your weapon in a threatening manner. It can also be how famous your character is.

Appeals vary in the number of points they get you.

Versus Evidence, Appealing is considered to be talking past someone to go straight for the emotions. The Appealer gets them as many points and Stress as dice you put up, but it also gives the other side 3 points.

Versus another Appeal, each person rolls the dice assigned to the Characteristic they’re using.

The person who rolls the highest total gets that points equal to the number of dice they rolled and half that much Stress, rounded up. So, if they roll 3 dice, and win, they get 3 points and 2 Stress.

The other person gets nothing but gets Stress equal to the number of dice they rolled.

This makes this a sound move for very charismatic people, but it is still risky.

This is signaled by placing the dice in front of you, or holding them up, though you’re not obliged to reveal how many or their sizes.

Tracking Points

Each side is responsible for their own points but to make it easier, you can use the E/A method.

Write an E and A on top of each other, and then draw a line between them. When you gain points through Evidence, put a single tally next to the E.

When you win an Appeal, note how many dice are added by the A.

When you're totaling your points at the end just multiple the tallies next to E by 3 and add that to the sum of the numbers by A. This should allow you to quickly jot things down and keep them straight during the Confrontation.

Here’s some areas you can use to Appeal to your enemy and what their corresponding dice might be:

HONOR Your standing can carry you through the day, even if your arguments are weak. The character with the highest Honor gets to apply a free use of their Honor die to their pool.

STRESS When your opponent is overworked and they're at maximum whelm, it's much easier to get them to give in. You can redeem a d4! worth of Leverage for every Stress penalty your opponent has, however, you don't have to redeem all the d4!s all in one round and can spread them out over the course of the Confrontation.

EQUIPMENT It may be the case that equipment can sway an argument. Often this is through imitation or torture, but gold can also persuade a hesitant sellsword or the right equipment might convince a thief to take on a risky job. A badge of authority may also win you some influence.

Equipment used for this purpose gains the character a base d8. Equipment that’s substandard or that’s being re-purposed from its original use (a knotted rope used to whip a victim, or a broken glass bottle used to threaten someone) only nets a d4.

STAT CONFRONTATION DIE Having an exceptionally high Strength or Dexterity might be relevant to the situation. If that’s the case, add that Abilities Confrontation Die to your pool.

APPLICABLE SKILLS You may roll an additional die for any applicable Advanced skill based on that Skill’s Rank. Take the Rank of that Skill and round up to the nearest dice size. So, a Rank 5 Skill would net a d6 dice while a Rank 14 Skill would net a d20.

But that is by no means a comprehensive list and plays should be rewarded for out-of-the-box thinking. Appeals start at a d4!, but this can vary. For instance, a very skilled swordsman with a lot of Advanced Training in his weapon of choice makes a more powerful Appeal than a rookie.

You can use the same Appeal multiple times during a single Confrontation.

Characteristic as Evidence vs Appeals

There’s no hard rule that can be given of when a Trait qualifies as one over the other, but there are some guidelines.

Generally, if the person whose Characteristic is being used is not directly involved and they’re known by both parties, it is Evidence.

If, however, one of the people is involved in the argument, especially if it is defense, or you’re trying to bring in the Characteristic of someone that the other person doesn’t know, then it is considered an Appeal.

Evidence as an Appeal

Truthfully, there may be a time where you have Evidence but it's in your best interest to reinforce the idea with emotion that makes it closer to an Appeal than Evidence.

In this case, you treat the Evidence as an Appeal with a base dice pool of your Intellect or Charisma's Confrontation Die, a die from your Articulation Skill (if you don't have that skill, you don't get this dice), and your Honor Die for the argument itself. From there, you can add other Characteristics to the pool.

The GM can say no to a proposal if the counter argument doesn’t directly relate to the argument, so careful phrasing could limit what your opponent can do. This is usually the indication that the round isn’t finished yet and the person who was rebuffed can try a different tact or argument.

Bluffing, or in other words, Lying

As per normal, a character only needs to roll a Deception Check if the other person is suspicious of them, but even then, if one side accuses the other of something, trying to get them to reveal a secret, they can use Deception to try and bluff, hiding their actual reaction.

If the person is, in fact, telling the truth but someone is still suspicious of them, they’d roll an Articulation Check to convince their accuser of their sincerity.

PANIC THRESHOLD

Starting Panic Threshold
HonorPanic
GreatNever
HighCritical
AverageWounded
LowBloodied
DishonorHurt

A strong willed or well disciplined person, when faced with insurmountable odds will often fight and/or argue long after the cowards have run, either gaining victory or assuring his death. Targeting these weaker willed people might also make or break a side. This is represented by a character’s Panic Threshold.

Check the character’s Honor to determine their starting Panic Threshold. Record this for your character by circling the Wound Category in your Vitality Section. When you reach that Wound Category, you become Panicked.

Panicked people have several disadvantagous: the first being that they half their Stress Threshold until they're out of danger or the argument they're in (often just conceding to get away).

The second is that they gain double the amount of Stress from Appeals, win or lose.

In combat, a Panicked person can't take aggressive actions: they'll still attack, but if the other side flees, they won't chase them and they'll try to fall back to more defensible positions, if they can.

If a person goes above their Stress Threshold, they immediately lose the Confrontation. If they're in combat, they simply turn and flee, unable to face their own morality. Captains can try and rally them with a Check immediately.

If cornered and given no space to run, these routed fighters enter a frenzy - only using aggressive Tactics and becoming immune to Stress penalties.

FAST TALKING

There may be times when you don’t want to/can’t get into a protracted argument and just want to overwhelm your opponent into agreeing with you. For example, you need to fast talk your way past a guard or convince a henchmen to go first down a trap filled corridor before he remembers he doesn’t have insurance.

In those cases, you want to fast talk the person.

This is, essentially, a Confrontation in a single round: either by showing a blatant, time-sensitive, piece of Evidence (“Let me in! The orcs are RIGHT THERE”) or by making an Appeal that stuns the person with your Charisma.

If the person can’t match you or beat you, you won them over: for the next 30 minutes or so and then they’ll come calling.

Fast Talking is not a way to permanently get a person on your side - it is a band-aid tactic to buy you a little extra time.

ENDING THE ROUND

Like I said, a round ends when an argument is countered or conceded.

Quickly jot down the points gained that round and move on.

These points are kept secret until the end of the Confrontation.

Multiple People in a Confrontation

You can, of course, have people help out in a variety of support roles during a Confrontation but they can often trip over each other, giving the opposition a chance to rebuttal.

The big thing to note is that, if you’re not careful, you can step on each other’s toes as the opposition can choose which argument to focus on if many are provided, allowing them to peak the weakest one.

So, if multiple emotional Appeals are presented, he can pick the lowest result.

This doesn’t mean that those arguments are wasted: they can be reused later in the Confrontation and, in fact, seeing which arguments the opposition chooses to ignore might give you some clues about where their argument is weakest.

Players may take sidebars, of course, (See the Taking a Break Sidebar below) but they may also use the Warfare Advanced Skill to temporarily pause and discuss with each other.

If you’re facing multiple people, note that any Evidence has to apply to/be believed by everyone on the opposition to be effective, thus making Evidence less and less helpful in a situation where you have to convince a group or mob.

TRUMP CARDS

There are some arguments that are so good that they can counter multiple points. These are considered trump cards and should be played carefully because they can only counter arguments that your opponent has already put forward.

Trump cards give a number of points equal to their base times the number of arguments they counter.

So, if you put forward Evidence that counters 3 arguments, it would give you 9 points, while having a 4 dice Appeal that counts against the same number gives you 12 points.

It doesn’t matter if the arguments have already been counter, in fact, that’s when you get the most benefit out of trump cards.

ESCALATING A CONFLICT

A debate between friends is on a different level than two enemies mudslinging or threatening to cut each other’s throat if the other doesn’t listen. This is represented by levels of escalation.

At baseline, the Confrontation is simply a battle of ideas, with each side having no person stake in the matter. It is the default and only inflicts Stress.

However, one or either side can make it PERSONAL, which means pride and personal image is starting to get in the way. This happens when one side uses more than 3 Appeals in a Confrontation or when one side purposely makes an insulting comment.

When a Confrontation becomes Personal, Appeals become more powerful, being worth 1 extra point on a success, however, people often dig their heels into the ground when you start questioning their character, making others things more dangerous.

The first is that you need to not just beat your opponent, but beat his total points by 5 plus a roll of his Honor Dice (which represents his mood).

But, it can be to your benefit: the winner gains Honor equal to how much he beat his opponent by, while the loser loses that much.

Above Personal Confrontations are INTIMIDATION Confrontations. This means that you’re now threatening personal harm to either the person, or someone the person cares about. You can now bring in that shiny blade or talk about what a shame it would be if that person’s house burned down.

This is similar to a Personal Confrontation, except that, if you lose and you don’t then escalate to violence and follow through on your threats, you lose face, losing 5 Honor.

But, if you escalate to violence and also get your buttkicked, you lose 10 Honor so if you’re going to start threatening people, make sure you either win or that you’re as tough as you say you are.

You can jump up levels, going from a standard Confrontation to intimidating them in a single round, however, you can’t de-escalate.

PUSHING THE POINT

When one side feels they may have the upper hand and that the other has run out of arguments, they can try to push the point, or end the Confrontation. He simply tries to push the other side to make a decision.

If it turns out that the other person does still have more to say, the Confrontation continues, gaining 1 point.

If, however, it turns out that the pushed person does, in fact, have no more to say, than the Confrontation ends

Taking a Break

It may take days or weeks to sway someone, making sure you know them, their likes and dislikes, and that you’ve got all your bases covered.

In this way, it is perfectly acceptable, should it make sense, that you suspend the Confrontation, possibly indefinitely.

FOLDING

Folding is what happens when you want to try and give them a lie or are not planning on doing what the winner wants. In this case, you give in early.

If your opponent pushes, you can choose to Fold by saying that you have no more arguments, but if the other person suspects that you’re Folding they can try and call you on it, in which case it's an opposed Deception Check if you are and a Articulation Check if you’re not.

The Articulation Check is to make it harder to meta-game whether or not you're bluffing.

If you are Folding and you fail the Deception check, the Confrontation continues.

Note that obviously your accuser now knows you were lying but that doesn’t give them a way to prove to other people that was the case. It’s communicated to them with a definite drop in the voice or the way you looked away.

If you’re Folding and succeed at your Deception Check, or if you weren’t and you fail on your Articulation, the accuser pushes the issue but there’s no proof and so he loses face.

The accuser gives you all the Honor he would have gotten from the win and only gains it back if he can prove publicly that you were lying.

Ending The Confrontation

At the end of the Confrontation, both sides reveal their points. The one with the most points gets their way.

Combat

Starting A Combat

Combat engages as soon as both sides are within eyesight, and both know that the other intends harm.

The CLOCK

The Clock begins at 1, and then progresses to 2, 3, 4 etc, ad infinitum. When the Clock matches a character’s Initiative, they go. Each of these numbers represent 1 second of time passing. What second a character's next action is referred to as their initiative (or "where they are on the Clock")

This can be a difficult when you first start so we recommend that you start with only running two or three enemies until you get the hang of it. We've also provided a tool that can help you keep track of the Clock and enemies easier. You can find it here.

STARTING INITIATIVE & SURPRISE

Each side rolls an initiative die. The lower the die, the more prepared they are for the attack, though typically the instigator goes on second 1. Those that know the battle is about to start (like being warned by a predetermined sign) use a d4, and the completely surprised receive a d20, while everyone else typically falls on a dice between that.

Those whose initiative hasn’t come up are surprised and continue to do what they were doing as if nothing is wrong. They can take no other actions: they’re completely unaware of what’s going on.

Should someone attack them during this time, they are completely helpless, defending on a d8!.

If the surprised person is hit, the pain quickly brings them into the reality of the situation, and they may act 2 seconds later (or before that if their initiative was the next second).

ACTIONS

Every action takes a certain amount of time. On a character’s Initiative, they declare their action and are told how long that action will take. After that time, the action is complete.

So, if a character wants to walk across a room, which will take 8 seconds, and his Initiative is 5, once the Clock reaches 5, he starts walking and once it reaches 14, he’s gotten the other side of the room.

At any point, you may choose to forfeit your action and change your course. If, when halfway across the room (at second 9), the character sees that his buddy is in trouble, he can immediately decide that, no, he’d rather be there, his character stops walking across the room and instead heads over to help his friend.

Keeping track of this can be tricky for new players unused to the system. To help players make the shift, we've created the Basic Combat Cheat Sheet that has a strip where you can keep track of when your next action is going to happen. It also includes handy references to other rules found in this chapter as well.

MOVEMENT

While, for the most part, you’ll be using your commonsense to determine how long things will take, to unify at least one thing, movement rates are given below.

A person may move up 1 movement category or down 2 in a second.

Every 10 seconds while Running you take damage. This starts at a d4! but increases by 1 dice size every 10 seconds, capping at a d20!.

For Sprinting, this happens every 5 seconds.

This damage is reduced by your Endurance (or Athletics) Rank, down to a minimum of 0.

You can push your character as hard as you'd like, continuing to take damage until they die from fatigue but if you take damage from Running or Sprinting and you stop, you can't Run or Sprint again until you've waited 10 seconds for every time your damage dice was increased.

Also, moving from a Run to Sprint, or vice versa, doesn’t reset that count, so don’t think you can skip taking damage by moving from a Sprint to a Run, you cheeky devil.

While Running or Sprinting, you're unable to attack or defend yourself

Movement
Speed
Size
Stroll/CrawlWalkJogRunSprint
Small2.5 ft /sec2.5 ft /sec5 ft /sec10 ft /sec15 ft /sec
Medium2.5 ft /sec5 ft /sec10 ft /sec15 ft /sec20 ft /sec
