TEACHING YOUR SPELLS TO OTHERS

Magic spells are complex things with more layers than an onion, so it’s not a simple task to teach another a spell you know, even if they’re using the same magic system.

The first step is to be taught the basic of the spells. This is an Weirdcraft Skill Check with the penalty being set by which type of magic is doing the teaching and learning.

This takes a 1d4! days of study and teaching, as well as ‘dry’ runs, after which the Check is made.

If it’s successful, the person has the basics and may gain that spell as part of their normal level up (instead of rolling a random spell) or they may learn is instantly, but this takes additional work, costing them CrP to the tune of 25 - the learner’s Int score, as they have to devote additional time to finally cementing it in memory, time that might be taking up with other things.

A failure indicates that more time and study must be taken, increasing the days of study by 1 dice size (d6! days of study for the second try, d10! for the fourth attempt and so on).

Shape Rudiment Descriptions

Note that all shapes glow slightly with strange luminesce, alerting people where the spell is.

CIRCLE

DRAIN 2

The Circle is the most basic Shape. It extends from the Origin with a Radius equal to the Base Range of the Effect. Anyone within the Circle is affected by the spell. If it deals damage or inflicts Stress, this occurs on the Interval or if a person enters/re-enters the shape. If not cast far enough away, this could also include the weird-adept.

CHAIN

DRAIN 0

This is the most primal Shape a spell can come in. The weird-adept casts the spell and it chooses 1 viable, random target within the Range of the Spell. After half the spell’s Interval, it then leaps to the next. Anyone hit by the spell suffers its Effects for the entire time the spell is cast.

People may be hit multiple times, which simply counts as the spell Stacking on them, but the weird-adept may try and redirect the spell, causing it to skip over a person, but they take Stress equal to the number of times they’ve done so.

CONE

DRAIN 3

The Cone starts with its tip at the Origin and then extends in a 45-degree arch from it up to the spell’s Range. Anyone within the Cone is affected by the spell. If it deals damage or inflicts Stress, this occurs on the Interval or if a person enters/re-enters the shape.

The Cone can also be moved and shifted, rotating around its Origin, moving a facing every 3 seconds.

SALVO

DRAIN 5

The Salvo is the spell chucked up to 3 * its base Range from the spell’s Origin. It requires a ranged attack to hit (though ignoring Cover). On a miss, it follows the normal ranged miss rules. Anyone that is hit, suffers the full effects of the spell. If it deals damage or inflicts Stress, this occurs on the Interval.

From where the Salvo's touch location is, that is where the Shape of the spell is placed. Those within the Base Range of the Effect of that Shape (even on a total miss) suffer the effects of the spell for half its Interval.

SPHERE

DRAIN 5

The spell takes on the shape of a 2 ft diameter sphere that flies around, coming into being at the spell’s Origin. While the weird-adept has complete control over the direction with only minimal effort (so it doesn’t affect what else he’s doing), it still has some limitations. The first is that it only goes 10 ft / second, no faster, no slower, and the weird-adept may only turn it 45 degrees every 3 seconds.

Anyone touched by the sphere suffers the Effects of the spell.

RAY

DRAIN 2

The ray is a thin line of magic that extends from the spell’s Origin up the 10 times the spell’s Range. It manifests in a single instant, requiring a roll to hit, but those that it hits, suffer the full Effect of the spell, though he can only try once per second, and this does eat into the Interval.

If no one was hit and the spell is still being cast, the weird-adept can manifest another ray and try again until he hits or he decasts the spell, though he can only try once per second and this does eat into the Interval.

WALL

DRAIN 2

The wall is a line that starts at the spell’s Origin and extends up to its Range, but also into the air and below the ground up to 50 ft. It also doesn’t have to be a straight line, weaving, twisting and turning, however, no part of it can get within 5 ft of another part. It must also be anchored to the ground. The wall cannot be moved once placed unless it has an Aura Origin.

Anyone passing through the wall is affected by the Spell. Those that are in the wall’s way when it is cast, get a defense roll vs a ranged attack to get out of the way.

Range Rudiment Descriptions

DOUBLE

DRAIN 1

This makes the Range of a spell twice its Base Range.

FULL

DRAIN 0

This makes the Range of a spell just its Base Range.

HALF

DRAIN 1

This makes the Range of a spell half its Base Range.

PERSONAL

DRAIN 2

This makes the Range of a spell just a single individual.

Origin Rudiment Descriptions

AURA

DRAIN 5

This makes it so the Origin starts at the weird-adept (and any equipment he carries) and then extends out from them, moving as they move.

TOUCH

DRAIN 2

This makes it so the Origin starts at whatever the weird-adept touches and then extends from there. If the target is trying to resist being touched, the weird-adept needs to make an Unarmed attack against them: the weird-adept is considered armed.

NEAR

DRAIN 1

This makes the Origin of the spell from the Effect's Base Range to up to double the Effect’s Base Range. This never affects the caster.

FAR

DRAIN 3

This makes the Origin of the spell from double the Effect’s Base Range to up to triple the Base Range.

Effect Rudiment Descriptions

ALARM

TRADITION Occultism

BASE DRAIN 1

BASE RANGE Trigger 50 ft, Alarm 25 ft, modified separately

INTERVAL 3 Hours

EFFECT When the defined type of being enters the Shape of the spell, it triggers the alarm, alerting everyone in the alarm range. The default definition is “Anything Humanoid” but this can be modified to make it more specific once.

STACK Make the trigger condition more specific by 1 step. If two definitions contradict one another, they are both cancelled out. You can also add another trigger condition.

ALTO SCREAM

TRADITION Glamour

BASE DRAIN 1

BASE RANGE 30 ft

INTERVAL 5 Seconds

EFFECT A high-pitched, blood-curdling scream infects the Shape of the spell, dealing 1 Stress to everyone inside.

STACK Increase the Stress by 1.

ANCESTRAL LORE

TRADITION Occultism

COMPONENTS Fire, the Weird-Adept’s Blood

BASE DRAIN 1

BASE RANGE 15 ft

INTERVAL 3 Skill Check or 6 Hours, whichever comes first

EFFECT By channeling the link in your blood, you can summon an ancestor spirit to temporarily endow you with some of their knowledge. A person within the Shape of the spell increases a Int, Wis, or Char based Skill Check by +3. Anyone within the Shape of the spell may “steal” this bonus - it is first come, first serve, regardless of what the weird-adept wishes - and it can be done after they roll.

STACK Increase the bonus by +2.

ANIMATE CORPSE

TRADITION Animism

BASE DRAIN 5

BASE RANGE 30 ft

INTERVAL 4 Hours

EFFECT Animates, or assert control over, a corpse of a used-to-be sentient being within the Shape of the spell, and up to Medium in size, into mindless undead. To gain control over already raised undead they need to both be unintelligent and uncontrolled by another. This undead doesn’t think for itself and can only follow simple commands like “Stand here and attack anyone that comes through”. It can’t speak or even defend itself properly (being unable to employ Combat Tactics or gain any bonus from Flanking) and has no survival instincts. See the Animated Corpse entry in the Bestiary.

STACK Animate an additional corpse or a corpse 1 size larger.

ARCANE VORTEX

TRADITION Sortilege

BASE DRAIN 3

BASE RANGE 50 ft

INTERVAL 30 seconds

EFFECT All spells that have shapes that overlap with the Spell Vortex are changed into Spheres and are attracted to the center or edges of this spell’s shape by the most direct route. If at the edge, they simply circle the edge. Spell caught this way cannot be released until the end of their Interval.

The direction is dictated by the weird-adept and can be changed only once. For Arcane Vortexes that are Walls and Ray, the spells move to either end.

STACK The direction of spells can be changed an additional time during each Interval.

AUGUR SECRET

TRADITION Occultism

BASE DRAIN 2

BASE RANGE 15 ft

INTERVAL 30 Seconds

EFFECT This finds anything that is purposely hidden from others, including hidden doors or a love letter sequestered away, within the Shape of the Spell.

The weird-adept doesn’t automatically know what is hidden; they only know its exact location and general area the item takes up. The weird-adept is also unaware if the object is moved but instantly knows the object if they touch it, even if it has.

STACK 1 more detail about the object is revealed to the weird-adept. This is usually in the form of, first, who is hiding the secret, and then a one-word adjective that describes it.

BANISH

TRADITION Calling

BASE DRAIN 5

BASE RANGE 10 ft

INTERVAL 5 Seconds

EFFECT Everyone within the Shape of the spell is temporarily banished to the Astral Plane of existence until the spell is released. Those that are banished have a sense of what is going on in the Middle Realm, though they are unable to interact with it at all.

Called creatures, demons and elementals, are permanently banished to their home plane.

STACK Increase the Base Range by 10 ft.

BAR PORTAL

TRADITION Investiture

BASE DRAIN 1

BASE RANGE 50 ft

INTERVAL 1 Hour

EFFECT This spell locks and seals any door or latch in the Shape of the spell. Anyone trying to bust through needs to make a Strength check vs d20! + 3 to successfully break down the door.

STACK The portal is further strengthened, giving it an additional +3.

BESTIAL SIGHT

TRADITION Animism

BASE DRAIN 3

BASE RANGE 15 ft

INTERVAL 30 Seconds

EFFECT This bestows everyone in the Shape of the spell one type of special vision. This covers dark vision, infrared vision, 360 vision, or aquatic vision.

STACK Either increase the Base Range by 15 ft or you may exclude a person in the Shape of the spell.

BIND ELEMENTAL HEART

TRADITION Calling

BASE DRAIN 3

BASE RANGE 20 ft

INTERVAL 30 seconds

EFFECT This spell either conjures an elemental heart from its realm or binds one that has gone rogue.

Once in this realm, the elemental heart robes itself in nearby sympathetic elements, giving a form with which it can then move. Without its dead kin around, the heart becomes inert and defenseless. So, while there are Order and Chaos Elementals, neither of those two things have a physical manifestation in the Middle Realm and so they simply lay there.

A conjured elemental with a Weird of d4!. The higher the Weird, the more powerful the elemental. Stats for elementals are found in the Bonfire Bestiary.

Elementals are ‘liquid’ and can shift and change their form. Their Weird can be invested to increase their baseline stats and special abilities. How much this costs is determined by the type of heart summoned. Weird can assigned at the time of summoning but also rearranged after, though this takes 1 second per point shift

A summoned elemental heart appears in a random location within the Shape of the spell, determined by d12 for direction (12 being where the weird-adept is facing and 6 being directly behind him) and d20 for distance, and rolls a d12 initiative dice. During this time, the elemental is getting its bearings and forming itself proper.

Elementals are intelligent creatures and will struggle to overcome their bindings. Anytime you change an elemental’s command, the elemental rolls a d8! + its Weird (and the Weird of any other elementals controlled by the weird-adept) in a one round Confrontation. If it wins, the weird-adept loses control and the elemental goes rogue, first seeking out the weird-adept to try and kill them as quickly as possible

The weird-adept can try to cast Bind Elemental Heart again to try and regain control. If the Weird you could have summoned is greater than the rogue elemental’s Weird, you regain control... for now.

If this spell is cast in any other Shape than Circle, the elemental is forced into that shape and unless the Shape can be moved, the elemental is rooted to the spot, only able to attack people who get within their Measure of that spot.

Shapes that require a roll to hit (Salvo and Ray) and do count that as the Elemental attack and thus include the Elementals damage or special attack.

STACK Increase the summoned Weird of the Elemental by d4!.

BIND TO THE AVERAGE

TRADITION Sortilege

BASE DRAIN 2

BASE RANGE 50 ft

INTERVAL 30 seconds

EFFECT Any roll within the Shape of the spell moves 1 point towards the average. If at the average, they gain a + or - 1 depending on the whims of the weird-adept.

STACK Either the roll moves an additional point towards the average or the bonus/penalty for being there is increased by 1.

BINDING GLYPH

TRADITION Investiture

BASE DRAIN 2

BASE RANGE 45 ft

INTERVAL 8 Hours

EFFECT This binds another spell to a random item within the Shape of the spell. The item is marked with a faintly glowing sigil that requires a Perception check to see if you’re not looking for it specifically.

On a condition indicated when the weird-adept first casts the spell the bound spell goes off as if cast from the item in question.

The mage is, in effect, shaping two spells at one time and needs the SP to cast both for this spell to work. After she’s done, she receives double the normal Stress.

STACK Lower the Stress taken by 2: this can lower it below the base amount you would get.

DIVINE OBJECT

TRADITION Occultism

BASE DRAIN 1

BASE RANGE .5 Mile

INTERVAL 30 Minutes

EFFECT This locates the closest object in the Shape of the spell that matches the description, which, at base, is a single noun. While the spell is active, the weird-adept knows the exact location of the object in relation to themselves. After it’s over, the memory remains but the inner compass has faded. In the case of the object being a sentient being, it doesn’t have to know it fulfills the qualifications, making this the favored spell of Dark Overlords seeking out Children of Prophecy.

STACK Gain an adjective to describe the thing (and narrow down the responses). So, a “gold necklace” is a single adjective, and “A gold necklace with 3 rubies” is two adjectives.

DOPPELGANGER

TRADITION Glamour

BASE DRAIN 5

BASE RANGE 35 ft

INTERVAL 20 Seconds

EFFECT This spell creates 1d4 phantoms of everyone within the Shape of the spell. These phantoms appear within 5 ft of the person and move in sync with them, following them.

The target is in a superimposed state, being, at once, one of the phantoms and none of them. Thus, she can strike from anywhere there is a phantom

These phantoms disappear on the following condition: the target makes an aggressive action of any kind, whether that’s spell shaping, shooting a bow, or striking with a weapon. Even if unsuccessful, all the phantoms disappear.

And whenever someone strikes a phantom, there is a 1 in X chance of actually hitting the real person, with X being the number of phantoms that person has left. Should they actually hit the person, all the phantoms disappear. If the blow does land on a phantom, only that phantom disappears.

STACK Increase the number of phantoms created by 1 dice size.

DOMINATE

TRADITION Calling

BASE DRAIN 5

BASE RANGE 10 ft

INTERVAL 5 Seconds

EFFECT By means of this spell, the weird-adept is able to link everyone within the Shape of the spell, by linking their bodies and offering a way to allow them to do tasks they would not otherwise be able to do.

People who do not wish to surrender control can choose to grossly misinterpret the commands of the controller, but they still have to do what they’re ordered, unless it would result in obvious death (such as jumping off a cliff or slitting their own throats). They don’t, however, have to follow the order to the best of their ability.

They may also try and seize control through a Confrontation with the current controller starting with 1 point. While playing out this Confrontation may take a while, in game terms it happens within 1 second. This is a battle of wills. The winner of the Confrontation takes full control over the other dominated creature.

A person can freely surrender, allowing them to mimic more intricate movements. This allows every person to roll any physical Skill Check using the controller’s Rank or to fighter using the controller’s Trainings.

STACK Increase the number of points the controller starts with by 1.

DREAM STRIDE

TRADITION Occultism

BASE DRAIN 5

BASE RANGE 5 ft

INTERVAL 1 Hour

EFFECT All willing creatures in the Shape of the spell have their spirits pushed out of their bodies as an incorporeal semi translucent form. For the first 10 seconds, the spirit is disoriented and is unable to locate their body.

While traveling in this form, the person is almost transparent, requiring a Heroic level Perception Check to notice something off. The spirit can travel up to 10 miles per hour, unhampered by terrain. The astral projection can’t speak or interact with the Middle Realm; simply passing through walls and objects but stopped by magical wards and living beings.

It’s recommended that you return to your body before the spell is released. Otherwise, your spirit is automatically thrown back into your body, which is an upsetting experience, and nets you 1 Stress per mile you are away from your body.

While under the influence of this spell, the person’s body is completely autonomous, with the weird-adept being completely unaware about what’s going on with his body unless he’s killed in which case he’s trapped as spirit between worlds, which is a bummer.

STACK The spirit travels faster, increasing its speed by 10 miles per hour.

BASE RANGE 20 ft

INTERVAL 5 Seconds

EFFECT The weird-adept imbues a small object with potential, that lets out a sudden flash of light in the Shape of the spell. Blinded and startled by the flashbang, creatures in the Shape of the spell reroll their Initiative on a d4 and then adding the current second on the Clock and initiative modifier. Everyone that is affected is considered surprise with all associated penalties until their initiative comes up again.

FLATTEN

TRADITION Charm

BASE RANGE 5 ft

INTERVAL 30 Seconds

EFFECT Everyone within the Shape of the spell becomes 2D, able to be seen from a certain angle but unable to interact with the 3D world but the 3D world may interact with them. They remain plastered on the nearest flat surface, bending freely around corners as if it’s nothing and slipping through cracks.

Those in 3D space can interact with them, dealing damage if they’re facing perpendicular to the 2D person.

STACK Increase the Base Range by 5 ft.

FORCE BIND SPIRIT

TRADITION Calling

BASE DRAIN 10

BASE RANGE 50 ft

INTERVAL A Year and a Day

EFFECT By sheer force of will, the Caller binds the escaped spirit to its body, forcing a horrible bastardization of life.

This affects all the dead in the Shape of the spell, regardless of how long it’s been dead for. This can bring them back as a skeleton or zombie based on how much meat is left.

The body continues to deteriorate, however, subtracting 10 from the max Vitality of the Bound Spirit for every month the spell wears on.

This bound spirit is stunted in many ways, as its mind and body still rots away. The bound spirit starts at its full Vitality but is unable to heal wounds by natural, magic, or divine means. Additionally, they’re unable to heal Stress. They’re also unable to gain Experience or level and their Honor is permanently set at Dishonorable.

But it’s not all bad: the bound spirit is immune to the effects of Fatigue.

STACK Slow the deterioration by 1.

INTERVAL 15 seconds

EFFECT All those within the Shape of the Spell gain a “luck” point, which acts as temporary Honor, and acts and behaves like Honor for the duration of the spell. If not spent, it disappears when the spell is over.

STACK Gain an additional point of luck.

BASE DRAIN 5

BASE RANGE 5 ft

INTERVAL 10 Seconds

EFFECT Anyone within the Shape of the spell becomes surrounded by an unbreakable binding dweomer. This dweomer affects a random limb determined by a d4!

1: right hand

2: left hand

3: right leg

4: left leg

5+: random piece of equipment

Those affected by this are unable to use that limb and can no longer move, only pivoting, if it’s a leg. Equipment that is bound is unusable.

Double the dweomers against demons.

STACK Increase the number of dweomers by 1. No limb can be affected twice. Those affected by a dweomer on both the left and right side of their body can no longer pivot.

HOOKGATE

TRADITION Calling

COMPONENTS A token to be destroyed

BASE DRAIN 5

BASE RANGE 500 ft

INTERVAL 1 Week

EFFECT The Hookgate is a spell developed by conjurers that harnesses the innate teleportation abilities of their Weird Tradition. The weird-adept creates a summoning circle and links it to an object, normally a scrap of paper or small stone. When it is destroyed, the person who did so is taken back to a random location within the Shape of the original shaping.

You may only have one Hookgate active at a time. Shaping this spell again destroys any previous summoning circles.

The sudden jerk while being summoned is not at all comfortable and so the summonees gain 5 Stress for every 15 miles they travel.

STACK You can bind an additional object. If one is destroyed, all those holding a token are transported back with their tokens also destroyed.

BASE RANGE 30 ft

Should anyone die because of a fall within the Area of Effect, they burst into flames as part of their death. Note that, this counts for even the most minor changes in evaluation, so someone’s footing becoming uneven suddenly does the damage of a 10 ft fall.

IMPROBABLE STAIR

TRADITION Sortilege

COMPONENTS Something that could be seen as a stair

BASE DRAIN 5

BASE RANGE 20 ft

INTERVAL 1 Minute

EFFECT Constructed by ancient wizards, the Improbable Stair was a means for the magi of ancient times to travel great distances instantly, however, since the deaths of the old masters, the secrets of how to use the properly Improbable Stair effectively have disappeared.

The Stair is accessed by seeing a stair in an unlikely place but within the Shape of the spell; a pile of crates or a sketch on a wall. It only has to suggest that a stair is there to work. The weird-adept then steps on to the ‘stair’ and onto the Stair.

Every minute on the Stair allows the weird-adept to travel d12! yards if walking, d12! miles if jogging, or d12! days’ travel if running, rolled secretly by the GM.

Others can be brought along by gripping hands with the weird-adept and with each other, but should they let go while climbing, they’ll be lost somewhere in time and space.

STACK You gain more control over where you end up: shift the result of the travel distance dice up or down by 1.

LIMINAL PLATFORM

TRADITION Charm

BASE DRAIN 1

BASE RANGE 5 ft

INTERVAL 6 Hours

EFFECT This shapes magic into a spectral platform that allows the mage to dump his excess baggage on it. It happily follows its summoner around until it dematerializes, holding up to 1 Medium item.

The basic shape is a disc, but this can be changed to the weird-adept’s desired shape to better hold things, such as a bowl or hand shape but can only be as large as the Shape.

No matter the shape or size, the platform is translucent purple and is incapable of articulated action. So, a hand shaped platform can hold a weapon, but it's unable to use it to fight: it simply sits there in the air, inert.

Liminal Platforms can be lowered to the ground or up to a max of the hip height of the weird-adept (from the ground. You can’t raise it to your hip, get on it and then raise it again). The platform doesn’t move if the weird-adept is on top of it.

STACK Increase the Base Range by 5 ft and increase the holding capacity by 1 Medium item.

EFFECT This spell infuses the Middle Realm with the essence of one of the Weird Traditions. Any spells of the selected Tradition that are cast in this spell’s Shape lower their Drain by 1. You can't use this ability if you're a Runegalder. If you rolled this up as one, have a free reroll on us.

STACK Lower the Drain by 1, down to a minimum of 1.

MARIONETTE

TRADITION Investiture

COMPONENTS A Small Object

BASE DRAIN 2

BASE RANGE 20 ft

INTERVAL 5 Minutes

EFFECT By means of this spell, the weird-adept can animate a Small object in the Shape of the spell, causing it to move about without being touched. The object in question only moves by hops and at points of articulation, so it doesn’t gain the ability to bend unnaturally.

In this way, a teapot or candlestick may hop about in a primitive form of locomotion, while a lock may only move its tumblers and an actual puppet may move as a person does, though this control is crude.

STACK Increase the size of the object by 1 Small.

On top of this, any attempt to magically conceal the object or person from the weird-adept doesn’t work.

PERFUME

TRADITION Glamour

BASE DRAIN 1

BASE RANGE 30 ft

INTERVAL 5 Minutes

EFFECT This spell can replicate any smell that the weird-adept is familiar within the Shape of the spell. The fragrance may be magical, but it does have some mental benefits:

If it is an unpleasant scent, all those affected gains a + 5 to Checks when dealing with airborne effects of all kinds. If the effect is simply applied without a Con check, its penalties are lowered by -2. If it is a pleasant scent, swap those bonuses for penalties as people naturally breathe in deeper.

Either way, Perception Checks to detect anything airborne is also harder, gaining a +15 and if a character is normally allowed a chance to defend against it (such as quickly covering their nose or refusing to breathe in from that point forward) that is forfeit.

STACK Either increase the bonus to Checks and automatic affects by +/-5 and +/-2 respectively or make the Perception Checks harder by +5.

PHANTOMBINDING

TRADITION Calling

BASE DRAIN 2

BASE RANGE 15 ft

INTERVAL 6 Hour

EFFECT While the spell is cast, all those in the Shape of the spell have an ancestral spirit following them around. This is obvious to anyone seeing the target. This prevents the character from effectively sneaking (as the ghost will make no effort to hide itself) and it keeps the person it's haunting up at night with nightmarish visions of its past life - preventing the person from healing Wounds or Stress.

Every morning, the spirit enters into a Confrontation with the target with d12! Appeal to try and persuade the target to visit their burial site. If they fail, they travel towards its grave, however, they get a chance to resist the next morning.

STACK Increase the strength of the spirits Appeal by an additional d12!.

SHOCK

TRADITION Charm

BASE DRAIN 5

BASE RANGE 10 ft

INTERVAL 10 Second

EFFECT Everyone in the Shape of the spell takes 1d2 points of damage which hits the pain centers of the brain. Those hit need to make a Trauma check vs d20!.

STACK Increase the damage dice by 1 size. Give the person making Trauma Check an effective -3 to their Con.

SHROUD OF INNOCENCE

TRADITION Glamour

BASE DRAIN 5

BASE RANGE 15 ft

INTERVAL 5 Seconds

EFFECT Those within the Shape of the spell are filled with a calming feeling, making them look favorably on one another. This lowers any negative Devotions of everyone by 1 and prevents aggressive actions to be taken. People on the outside don’t gain this benefit, so someone attacking from outside the Shape into it, can be attacked back.

STACK Decrease negative Devotions by 1. If this would bring them to below 0, they instead gain a positive Devotion to the thing they felt negatively towards.

SLOWFALL

TRADITION Charm

BASE DRAIN 3

BASE RANGE 20 ft

INTERVAL 5 seconds

EFFECT This changes the kinetic energy of any falling person within the Shape of the spell to potential energy, slowing their fall to a leisurely pace, 5 ft / second.

While the spell is cast, targets don’t take any fall damage. Additionally, if this spell was cast but doesn’t last the duration of the fall, the targets only take damage for the space they fall at full speed.

STACK Increase the fall speed by 2.5 ft / second. This doesn’t affect how much damage is taken after the spell is released.

SLOW METABOLISM

TRADITION Animism

BASE DRAIN 3

BASE RANGE 50 ft

INTERVAL 1 Week

EFFECT Everyone in the Shape of the spell doesn’t need quite so much food and water. Lower the food that everyone needs by half pounds, full pounds, two and half pounds respectively, and water by eighth gallon and half gallon, respectively. Once the spell is released, those affected don’t suddenly become super hungry: they just go back to their normal intake.

STACK Lower the need for food by .5 lb/1 lb/2.5 lb and water by eighth gallon and half gallon

SMOKESCREEN

TRADITION Charm

BASE DRAIN 3

BASE RANGE 50 ft

INTERVAL 10 seconds

EFFECT The smoke screen clouds everything, making it hard to see. The Illumination level for the area is lowered by 1. Additionally, shooting into or through the screen gives the targets a +5 to their ranged defense.

The smoke also chokes the lungs. Anyone passing through it gains a -1 to Fatigue until they can take 10 seconds to cough out enough of the black smoke to function again.

STACK Lower Illumination by 1. Targets gain +5 to defense and those passing through gain -1 to their Fatigue.

SILENCE

TRADITION Charm

BASE DRAIN 2

BASE RANGE 20 ft

INTERVAL 2 Minutes

EFFECT This dampens all sound in the Shape of the spell, increasing all Listening Check difficulties by +5.

STACK Further increase the difficulty by +5.

STITCH FLESH

TRADITION Animism

BASE DRAIN 3

BASE RANGE 50 ft

INTERVAL 5 Seconds

EFFECT This forces the wounds of all people within the Shape of the spell to stitch themselves together. While effective, this is an extremely painful process and is not kind to the body. This heals 1d4! points of damage off a single wound of each target and inflicting that much Stress.

Double this damage to determine whether it triggers a Trauma Check

STACK Add another d4!.

STRENGTHEN YMIR

TRADITION Occult

BASE DRAIN 2

BASE RANGE 10 ft

INTERVAL 1 Hour

EFFECT All Miracles within the spell’s Shape have their dice size lowered by 1. If multiple Favor was spent, this only shrinks 1 dice. If this would lower the dice to below a d4!, simply remove it.

STACK Lower the dice an additional size. If you remove that dice and still have power left-over, you may move onto lowering another die until you’ve reached your limit.

STROBE

TRADITION Investiture

BASE DRAIN 2

BASE RANGE 20 ft

INTERVAL 5 Seconds

EFFECT The weird-adept launches a ball of Bright strobing light that makes everything in and on the other side of the Shape of the spell hard to track. Ranged attacks, or spells that require a ranged attack, made into the flashbanged area or at targets behind them have their dice sizes reduced by 1.

STACK Decrease the dice by an additional size.

TELEKINESIS

TRADITION Charm

BASE DRAIN 3

BASE RANGE 15 ft

INTERVAL 5 seconds

EFFECT This allows for remote manipulation of things as if his hands were there, allowing him to push, pull, as well as do complex tasks from a safe distance.

Essentially, the weird-adept can act as if he were present up to the edge of the Shape of the spell.

STACK Increase the Base Range by 5 ft.

TONGUES

TRADITION Occultism

BASE DRAIN 1

BASE RANGE 10 ft

INTERVAL 10 Minutes

EFFECT Through mystical means, this spell gives all within the Shape of the spell the ability to read any script, even in a dead or unknown language but only if the weird-adept is already literate in the first place and also gives the power to speak another language, effectively giving them Rank 3 in that Language and Literacy Advanced Skill.

Tongues also has an additional power: the power to spot, read, and identify glyphs without setting them off.

STACK Increase the Rank of those temporary Skill by 3.

TOUCH OF THE OTHERWORLD

TRADITION Calling

BASE DRAIN 2

BASE RANGE 20 ft

INTERVAL 30 Minutes

EFFECT Anyone within the Shape of the spell feels themself uplifted, as if suddenly connected with a higher plane of existence. Because of this, they feel more confident in their beliefs. Anyone within the Shape of the spell rerolls the lowest dice result on Appeals in a Confrontation.

STACK Reroll an additional dice.

TURN

TRADITION Charm

BASE DRAIN 2

BASE RANGE 50 ft

INTERVAL 10 Seconds

EFFECT By means of magical force, the weird-adept is able to turn aside Undead, Elementals, and Demons, keeping them at a distance. Any Demons, Elemental or Undead inside the Shape of the spell flees at full speed until they’re out of it. Those inside it are invisible to them while the spell is active.

Undead, Elementals, and Demons that are trapped and unable to flee, begin to tear their own flesh as the mind-numbing pain floods their systems, dealing them d6! damage.

STACK Increase the damage by a d6!.

TWIST TONGUE

TRADITION Glamour

BASE DRAIN 1

BASE RANGE 10 ft

INTERVAL 10 Minutes

EFFECT Those in the Shape of the spell suddenly lost the part of speech. They reduce one of their Advanced Language Skills by 3 Ranks.

STACK Reduce the Rank of the same or another Advanced Language Skill by 3. If the person has all their languages reduced to 0, they become mute, unable to make any sound.

VERTIGO

TRADITION Glamour

BASE DRAIN 3

BASE RANGE 20 ft

INTERVAL 15 Seconds

EFFECT Everyone’s depth perception becomes all wacky. Everyone within the Shape of the spell lowers their ranged attack dice by 1 size.

This includes spells, but also placing spells in general becomes difficult. Spells with the Near and Far Origins are d6 ft/d10 ft closers or further away from where the weird-adept meant them.

And those affected also have a hard time reading elevation. Things look higher or lower than they actually are, causing those to stumble over smaller elevation changes. Knock-Back thresholds are reduced by 5.

STACK Reduce ranged attack dice by 1 size. Near and Far Origins variance are both increased by 1 size and Knock-Back Thresholds are reduced by 5.

VISUAL ILLUSION

TRADITION Glamour

BASE DRAIN 3

BASE RANGE 15 ft

INTERVAL 30 Seconds

EFFECT This spell creates a 2D visual illusion up to 5 ft x 5 ft anywhere within the Shape of the spell, that may be placed either on the ground or as a freestanding ‘wall’. This illusion hooks into the minds present but has no weight or substance to it, so anyone touching it immediately knows something is up (though touch doesn’t dismiss the illusion).

STACK The illusion gains additional area equal to 5 ft x 5 ft.

WALL WALK

TRADITION Investiture

BASE DRAIN 3

BASE RANGE 10 ft

INTERVAL 5 Seconds

EFFECT This endows a wall, magical or otherwise, within the Shape of the spell to be scaled with a Climbing Check, moving up down or sideways freely, with their feet on the wall and their body out-stretched as if standing. Other than this looking very odd, normal physics apply. Their movement is limited, however: people moving on this wall can only move up to a Crawl.

Crawling on a magic wall doesn’t cause its spell to be cast on that person.

STACK Increase the maximum Movement Category by 1.

WEAPONSHARP

TRADITION Investiture

BASE DRAIN 3

BASE RANGE 25 ft

INTERVAL 3 Attacks or 6 Hours, whichever comes first

EFFECT All weapons within the Shape of the spell have their lowest damage dice increased by 1.

STACK Increase the lowest damage dice by an additional size.

WEB

TRADITION Charm

BASE DRAIN 1

BASE RANGE 15 ft

INTERVAL 5 Minutes

EFFECT This covers the Shape of the spell in a thin gossamer of sticky arcane webbing that restricts movement down to Strolling speed.

Anyone wishing to move faster can make a Strength check vs d20! +5 for each movement category above a walk.

STACK Increase the penalty for moving above a Stroll by +5.

The Divine

Anatomy of the Divine

COVENANTS

Divines have spheres of power that represent their aspects. These are codified into Covenants, or promises they make with their servants in exchange for a portion of the Divine’s power.

Cults of that Divine typically pick one, maybe two Covenants, of their chosen Divine to focus on.

This means that priests of different cults may not get along with each other and there can even be intra-faith wars to purge heretics (those that focus on different Covenant from them).

The main bonus of Covenants is that they make Miracles within them easier to invoke. The specifics are elaborated on in the Invoking Miracles section below.

COSMIC LINKS

The Higher Planes are those that exist above the crude and primitive world and so, naturally, the Divines are linked to the events and behaviors of the celestial bodies that make their homes in the heavens.

A Cosmic Link is the specific celestial body that the Divine is associated with, and it usually gives an insight to the personality of the god. The Cosmic Link doesn’t necessarily mean your Patron is primarily the Divine of that Cosmic thing. So, a Divine associated with the moon might not be primarily a moon god, in the same way that while Venus was associated with the Morning Star, she was primarily viewed as a love goddess by the Romans. Still, your holy symbols may incorporate the moon motif commonly to represent her.

For clarification’s sake: when something says “decrease” in this section’s explanations, you go down the chart by that many steps. If it says “increase” go up, so increase will always be a bonus, and decrease will always be bad.

COMET This is associated with fervent but fleeting powers. Whenever you invoke a Miracle, you gain two Honor Dice with a +3 but lose an additional Favor.

EVENING STAR The evening star is a source of strength and beauty: it's the first star to rise in the evening. When you invoke a Miracle, if you roll below the average, you gain the average instead. So, if you roll d8 and get a 3 or less, you get 4 instead.

MOON The moon is a steady force, its effects are subtle but constant. When you invoke a Miracle, if you roll two Honor Dice, keeping the highest.

MORNING STAR The morning star is the last star in the heavens before day and is a lone watcher. When you invoke a Miracle and roll the minimum amount, you don’t lose any Favor.

SUN The sun is the lord of heaven, strong and unbending, its power unquestioned. When you invoke a Miracle and roll the max amount, you don’t lose any Favor.

CYCLICAL Often hailing from older, more primitive times, the Cyclical deity represents earthly inevitabilities in a dichotomy, sometimes with themselves and sometimes with an opposing deity. This can be Spring and Summer, life and death, creation and destruction. They may be weak now, but they will wax unstoppable. When you invoke a Miracle, and roll under its average, your next Miracle gains a +1. This is cumulative.

If you roll above its average, this bonus is then removed, and you get a -1 to your next Miracle. Again, this is cumulative and resets when you roll below.

So, if you have a d6! Honor Dice, and you roll a 2, the next Miracle you invoke gets a +1. That next Miracle you roll, you get a 3 for a total of 4 (because of the +1), giving you a +2 the next roll. On that roll, you roll a 5 for a total of 7 ( 5 + 2 ). The next Miracle you then invoke gets a -1.

Favor of the Divines

WHAT IS FAVOR?

Favor is a measure of your standing with a given god. It’s not an absolute measure, however, but more a measure of the chance that a Divine will answer your prayer. How far your Favor goes ranges widely based on how devoted you are to a god and how Honor you are.

LEVELS OF DEVOTION

There are 3 levels of commitment to a Covenant, that determine how often you get Favor and how much Favor you can have:

UNANOINTED are the lowest level: those outside the cult and its mysteries. They gain no benefits of any kind.

ANOINTED are those that are the lay members of the faith. They gain small bonuses to their max Favor for the deity they’re devoted to. You can only be anointed to one Covenant at a time.

If you have a positive Devotion to a deity, one of their cults, or one of their Covenants, you can choose to begin the game as an anointed to that deity. Otherwise, you can become Anointed during gameplay once you have that Devotion.

You can only be anointed to one deity at a time.

SERVANTS are the highest rung of the commitment ladder and serve as the officers of the cult of the god. They’re priests, abbots, hierophants, pontiffs, nazarites, hermits, etc. These are men and women that have taken vows to devote their life to the cult. In game terms, this means that these are those who have a Servant Archetype as either their Primary or Secondary Archetype.

ACQUIRING FAVOR

Servants turn their eyes from the earth below to higher worlds, both literally and metaphorically. In this way, they’re the keeper of the times and seasons, as well as the calendar to note the occurrence of Holy Days.

As such, players who play Servants will need to keep track of the passage of time. Doing so gives them special bonuses according to the schedule laid out below. You’ll note that it follows the Gregorian Calendar layout with holy days happening according to the Judeo-Christian traditions. The assumption that the characters will be following an in-game calendar with random Holy Days specific to their cult but we’re “translating” into the Gregorian calendar, in the same way that we assume the characters are actually speaking in their native fantasy tongues and not in English. Doing this makes it easier for players to keep track because the calendar is a familiar shape. They won’t have to track out a whole year and remember that Beltane is on the 5th of Seed’s Row.

Rules for using your own calendar and keeping all Servants relatively balanced against each other is going to be the Deluxe Rules.

Favor is unique to the Divine you’re petitioning. Gaining Favor with another Divine, means that you lose an equal amount of Favor with all others because gods are bad at sharing.

DAILY SACRIFICES (EVERY DAY) These are small, daily sacrifices. These tend to cost about 1 or 2 sc, 5 to 6 points of Stress, or 1 or 2 Vitality, depending on your Divine's preferences. They can be the sacrifice of a small, sacred animal, the burning of a portion of your meal, or the lighting of incense during morning prayers. They net 1 Favor for Servants of that Divine.

SABBATIC HOLY DAY (EVERY 7 DAYS) This is a day of rest and contemplation, where the faithful are instructed to put aside the things of the world and focus on the Divine with activities related to their Covenant. There is an emphasis on ritual over practicality to emphasize this divide, so while a Divine of Battle encourages his followers to fight every day, on his sabbath he only wants them to focus on ritualistic combat and controlled bloodshed, as opposed to actual combat. Again, this is to remind his followers of the holiness of the action and by forcing his followers to stop and think about their actions, he forces them to contemplate the deeper realities of combat. The sabbath takes up 1 to 3 hours and the rest of the day can be spent at the faithful wants.

Servants who observe the sabbath of their Divine gain all Favor back, while anointed worshippers gain their Min Favor from Charisma if they roll a 4 or better on their Honor die adding one Devotion related to that Divine. Unanointed worshippers gain nothing.

LUNAR HOLY DAY (4 SABBATIC HOLY DAYS) Where normal Sabbaths are days of rest, Lunar Holy Days are about sacrifices and consecration, which are thematically appropriate to the cult’s Covenant. Those observing the holy day need to stop and spend the whole day or they gain no benefit.

Servants gain all Favor back plus extra Favor equal to their Min Favor. This extra Favor is reset on the next Lunar Holy Day (which means you can’t stockpile it). The Anointed gain all Favor back, while the unanointed who celebrate gain 1 Favor.

SOLAR HOLY DAY (EVERY 3 LUNAR HOLY DAYS) These holy days celebrate the turning of the seasons and where the other festivals can be severe, with fasting and reading and nerd stuff like that, Solar Holy Days are about feasting and letting loose a bit. The Divines demand their faithful to party all day.

Servants gain all Favor back plus extra Favor equal to a roll of their Devotion. This extra Favor is reset on the next Solar Holy Day (which means you can’t stockpile it). The anointed faithful gain their full Favor back and the unanointed gain their Min Favor from Charisma if they roll a 4 or better on their Honor die adding one Devotion related to that Divine

ANNUAL HOLY DAY (EVERY 4 SOLAR HOLY DAYS) The Annual Holy Day either celebrates the new year or an important event in the cult, such as the birth of their messiah or the founding of their faith. It is a 2 day affair and is often occupied by feasting, gift giving, public rituals, and other such nonsense.

Servants and Anointed followers gain all Favor back with Servants also gaining extra Favor equal to their Devotion and the Anointed followers gaining extra Favor equal to a roll of their Honor die. For Servants, this extra Favor is reset on the next Annual Holy Day (which means you can’t stockpile it). The unanointed gain 1 Favor.

TAKING AN OATH (SPECIAL) Not a sacrifice or holy day parse, Taking an Oath is essentially getting Favor on loan from the Divines for the promise that, if you get out the bad situation you're in, you'll make a huge sacrifice to them soon after. By Taking an Oath, you gain a die worth of Favor for every 20% of treasure you gain from the adventure you promise to the Divine, should you survive.

This die is equal to their Honor dice related to the Divine you're petitioning if you're Anointed to them. The Unanointed must also promise to become Anointed in addition to the cash and goods, in which case they gain a d6! worth of Favor. This Favor can put you over your max but must be spent on a Miracle immediately.

The Divines are extremely litigious. If you don't fulfill your oath in 1 month + 1 for every Honor Category higher than Average Honor you're in, they will seek vengeance. You may no longer gain any Favor with any Divine that shares a pantheon with the one you're in and what you do have will decay, causing you to lose 1 Favor per day. Priests of the Divine will also condemn you as an oath breaker, a very serious accusation, causing you to drop 1 Honor Category per month and preventing you from increasing your Honor. Should you fall into Dishonor, you gain the Excommunicated Flaw.

CRUSADES & PILGRIMAGES (SPECIAL) There are holy places to visit and holy things to be done. Crusades and Pilgrimages are special rewards the GM can give out for furthering the Divine’s will. This can either be through an actual holy war or by waging a spiritual war of conversion. These don’t even need to be things done on purpose and can be part of the campaign.

The GM should award a roll of the crusader or pilgrim's Honor dice, allowing it to go over the Max Favor allowed, and awarding them Honor for furthering their deity’s influence in the Middle Realm. Additionally, if it was an amazing feat of faith, the GM may also increase the character’s Devotion size.

The unanointed gain no benefit from crusades and pilgrimages.

CONDEMNATION & ABSOLUTION (SPECIAL) Servants and Anointed followers are expected to hold to the Divine’s tenets more closely and so can come under condemnation for disobeying their deity. GMs may subtract Favor from Servants and Anointed followers for sins against their religion or prevent them from gaining Favor for prolonged transgressions. Servants and Anointed followers with the Religion Advanced Skill in their Covenant receive a warning before they act (having studied their religion to some extent).

Those that have transgressed must seek absolution before they gain the benefit of holy days and sacrifices again. What this means varies based on the magnitude of the sin.

Maximum Favor
Honor CateMax Favor
DishonorableCannot Invoke

MAXIMUM FAVOR

A person can only have so much Favor, with the Divines giving a little extra leeway for those of strong character. The Max Favor a person can have is limited to their Honor Category.

Anointed members increase this threshold by 1 while Servants increase their Max Favor by their level, but both cannot gain any Favor while in the Dishonorable Category, regardless of level.

Should a person drop an Honor Category, if their Favor is above their new max, it automatically drops.

Invoking Miracles

Now that you’ve got a nice stash of Favor, you probably want to spend it. That’s pretty simple: pray out loud for the Miracle in question. Silent prayers don’t work because no Divine is going to answer a prayer they’re not going to get credit for.

For every Favor you spend, you get another use of your Honor Dice but comes with a few differences: the first, and most major, is that you can spend it on ANYTHING - you want to run faster or jump higher? You want to heal your wounds? You want to attack slightly faster? You can with Favor, however, the effects are only temporary, of course.

The second is that you can spend to change the world around you. Every Favor you spend can change a 5 ft square area with the following restriction: it can’t directly contradict things that have already been said.

Miracles are also bound by Covenant: you can’t pray for something your Divine doesn’t have power over, so a Divine of the city can’t really help you in the mountains, for example.

But this is where being in a pantheon does help out: you can pray to another Divine in your pantheon for their blessing instead, but it requires twice as much Favor and you don’t gain the benefit of your Cosmic Link.

The other restriction is that the Miracles need to be subtle: no angels coming down from the skies to keep you from falling to your death but perhaps there’s water or a passing hay cart that catches you just in time to soften your landing. There needs to be room for doubt.

SACRED & PROFANE SPACES

Holy places are those areas that are closer to the God’s Realm, where the Middle Realm is weaker. There the faithful can almost feel the Divines walking around.

In a sacred space dedicated to a certain Divine, the Honor Dice you get becomes 1 size larger. It also fills the devoted with a sense of purpose, temporarily increasing their Devotion by 1 for Confrontations and, if defending the space, their Devotion applies to Morale, of course.

There are also those areas that are abhorrent to the gods. Desecrated altars, dwarven holds, and other spaces the Divine presence is absent.

These Profane spaces net Honor Dice 1 size smaller, down to a d2 for each Favor spent to the Divine space is Profane to. The unanointed are completely unable to invoke Miracles.

Character Progression

A person who sets off on an adventure doesn’t return the same person as they were when they left. Trials and hardships not only hone their skill, but also who they are and what they stand for.

In Bonfire, this change is measured by Experience (Ex), which is counted at the end of every session.

Gaining Experience

560020

The only way to gain Experience is to move towards your Goals or help others move towards theirs.

At the end of each session, if you've moved towards a Goal, whether your own or another player's, whether your character knew about it or not, you gain 25 Ex. If you moved towards additional Goals, you get a extra 10 Ex for each one you helped with. However, they only get the bonus Ex for helping another person if their goals aren't identical to yours.

So, let's say that you moved towards one of your Goals and helped another person with theirs. You would get 35 Ex (25 + 10). Or let's say that there wasn't enough time to do anything on your Goal, but you managed to help two other players; you'd still get 35 Ex at the end of the session (25 for the first, 10 for the second). Or, or, if you were a real wunderkind, and moved towards your Goal AND helped the two other players, you'd get 45 Ex (25 + 10 + 10).

There is a bonus of another 25 Ex for each member if everyone in the party has moved towards their Goals that session.

On top of this, if a party member actually completes one of their Goals, they (and anyone else who helps them) gains an additional 10% of their current Ex as well at 5 Honor (though this only applies to the person who completed it). If multiple goals were completed, you get an additional 5% Ex but no additional Honor.

The GM may award additional Ex for completing plot important points in the story.

You don’t receive Ex for random things, such as winning a Confrontation, Combats, or Skill Challenges. Those are more about gaining Honor.

You gain Ex for challenging who your character is. If they gain Ex from a Combat, it is not from just defeating a random foe or just being in Combat. It could be from your character facing their fears or rival, killing a person for the first time, or learning to be a leader in a stressful situation.

Those things are a means to an end, not an end in and of themselves.

FOLLOWER EXPERIENCE

Followers don't gain ex like normal characters: instead, getting half the ex of their boss. They get no other ex unless they're Proteges.

In this case, they’re treated like a normal PC in terms of gaining ex with the expectation that the player only needs to move towards his or one of his protege’s Goals to count towards whether or not everyone has moved towards their Goals.

Additionally, a character can give up to 50% of their earned ex from a session to their protege in forms of advice, training, and general guidance.

They do come at a cost and with a requirement. The requirement is that the candidate for protege must have a Devotion to the character. The cost is that they count as 2 followers towards your limit.

Once a follower has been declared a protege, they cannot go back to being a regular follower: they must either be killed, dismissed, or promoted to a full character.

Leveling Up

Once a character has received enough Ex to total level, they must take a week to think and meditate on what they’ve learned.

During this week, they reflect on their journey and how they’ve changed. Each day, they complete one of the steps of leveling up.

This self-reflection takes a large amount of the day. If the character is interrupted by any strenuous activity, they’ve lost the day and must pick up their reflection when they can from the same point.

SPECIALISTS & TOTAL LEVEL

If you purchase your Specialist Archetype after first level or independently of one another, your total level is going to be different than your individual Specialist level. So when you see a Specialist refer to “at first level”, it refers to its first level, not your total level.

Your total level is the levels you gained in your Generalist Archetype plus the levels you gained in your first Specialist Archetype.

DAY 1: RECEIVE CrP

At the start of his reflection, a character receives a number of CrP equal to his LvL CrP from his Intellect. This behaves exactly like CrP from Character Creation and can be used to buy things at any stage or reroll everything but Vitality.

You can spend these are different points over the level up process, but you can also save them up to purchase more expensive things if you don’t currently have enough CrP for what you want.

DAY 2: INCREASE STAT SCORES

Today you may spend CrP to improve any of your Scores as per Step 6 of Chapter 1: Character Creation.

At 3rd level and every 5 levels after that (8, 13, 18, etc.), you may increase 1 of your Stats by 1

And at 5th level and every 5 levels after that (10, 15, 20, etc.), you increase a random Stat by 1. This is rolled on a d6, with 1 being Strength and 6 being Charisma. You may influence with your Honor or spend 15 CrP for a reroll.

None of these options (either spending CrP or the random boosts), can bring a stat above 20. If it would, you don't recieve the bonus that level.

DAY 3: ASSESS PERSONALITY

FLAWS A character can grow, overcoming things that used to hold her down. A character can buy off a mental or behavioral Flaw for its CrP bonus (regardless of how much you got for it). If you do so, you gain a 4d6 Trait “Overcame X” with X being the Flaw. Background Flaws that have resolved through play can also give you this Trait according to the GM's discretion.

TRAITS As a character grows, things that used to be important to them no longer are and things they never used to identify with become a part of them.

A character can switch around their Traits, switching a Strong one for a Medium one, or a Medium one for a Weak one. This swaps the number of dice - not the size of those dice. So, swapping a 1d8 trait for 3d10 trait makes one 3d8 and the other 1d10.

They may also swap out a Weak one for an entirely new one.

After 3rd level, they may only do this swap once per level, however. Before then, you may swap your Traits around freely: after all, you may still be getting on your feet in terms of the type of character that would best fit in the group and campaign.

GOALS During this time, the character carefully turns over their aims in life and can ask themselves if this is really the path they want to travel down.

Goals may be switched out, dropped or added freely at this stage but can't total more than 3.

DAY 4: INCREASE ARCHETYPE ABILITIES

Before you begin this day, it's time to decide whether or not you want to purchase your Archetype Specializations, if you haven't already. This follows the normal rules set forth in Chapter 4: Archetypes.

Small note: if you're Specializing at an odd level where you get a reroll, you're going to use the new Vitality Dice to do the roll but you're still rolling against your last roll.

Once you do that, check your selected Archetypes (or new Specialist Archetype(s)) to see if they have any of their Abilities that either grow stronger (i.e., the Thug’s Precision Strike), gain additional free Skills (i.e., any of the Expert Archetype’s Skill Focuses), or gain something else for free (i.e., the Weird-Adept Archetypes gaining new Rudiments).

DAY 5: TRAIN AND RETRAIN

Now, it’s time to home in on what you’ve learned and any new skills you’ve acquired or hidden talents you’ve discovered during your travels.

At this stage you may spend your CrP to purchase and improve your Skills, Trainings, and Characteristics.

A character may also replace old knowledge with new. He may refund one of his Trainings and Skill purchases, gaining the CrP he spend on them back to spends on something else.

After 3rd level, he may only do this once per level up for each. Before that point, he may do this freely. He can never refund free Trainings or Skills earned from his Archetypes.

DAY 6: INCREASE VITALITY & STRESS THRESHOLD

Finally, it’s time to reflect on the fact that your travels have made you just a little bit tougher, a little bit better at facing what life throws at you.

At every even level, the character gets a free reroll of their Vitality Die from their last level, taking the higher of the two rolls, however, if both rolls are under their Minimum Vitality from their Constitution, they receive that value at least.

At every odd level, they gain a free roll that’s added to their total Vitality. This is not affected by their Con’s Min Vitality and is just a straight roll. You’ll need to record it on your character sheet.

If your Primary has a “choose the higher of 2” for their Vitality die, your Vitality Dice drops to one of those dice. So, “the higher of 2d6” becomes a single d6 for subsequent levels.

Remember to recalculate your Wound Categories

Your character also gets mentally tougher: at every level, the character also increases their Stress Threshold. This is based on your Primary Generalist Archetype. Experts receive +d8, Socialites & Weird-Adepts a +d6, and Fighters a +d4.

So, a Knight receives a +d4 while a Ranger gets +d8

DAY 7: ADJUST HONOR & REPUTATION

Now the other players will have a chance to adjust your HONOR by silently judging the character, rating him 1 to 10 in 3 categories: Flaws, Teamwork, Respect.

FLAWS How well has this player played their Flaws? Do they only seem to be brought up when it’s convenient but then forgotten they need to get away with something?

Does she use her Flaws to further the story and character development or does she use them to annoy others?

A character that leans more to the former, rather than the latter, deserves a higher score.

TEAMWORK Does this player work well with others? Do they pull their load and put themselves on the line or do they pick fights that derail the session? Are they of top on things and help set up or are they late and spend all their time on the phone?

Again, a character that leans more to the former, rather than the latter, deserves a higher score.

RESPECT How do you think this character is viewed by those he interacts with, by both the party’s character and NPCs? Has he kept his word (or at least, not gotten caught) or does he have a habit of backstabbing others?

The GM should then take the scores and average them across each category and then subtract 5 from each of them. Those three modified averages are then totaled: this is how much Honor they gain or lose.

The individual scores and who gave them should be kept a secret, though the player can know how much they scored in each category to help them improve.

The GM will also adjust your REPUTATION and complete your Reputation sentences as she deems appropriate. She gets to add 1 point at this point, but she can also move as many existing points around as she wants. She may also change the ending to any Reputation sentences she wants.

She may also ‘free’ them up to distribute later: so, if your character moves far away where people haven’t heard of them, you could lose your Reputation, which might be good or bad.

Note to GMs: while you can complete the sentences at any time, giving the player a heads up as to where their Reputation is headed, it isn’t advised that you start putting points into the other two Reputations until the character reaches 5th level.

If you’ve reached 10th level, your GM should also roll to see if you’ve attracted a follower.

Learning Non-Standard Abilities

Players who go out of their way to roleplay their character learning a new ability can get that ability irrespective of leveling, Archetype combination, and/or CrP spending, but only if they’ve taken some penalty for doing so (suffered for it) and only at the discretion of the GM.

The rule of thumb is that a player must have gotten in at least 2d4!+2 situations where penalties they accrued in pursuit of their new ability have come into play. So, the fighter needs to go out on 5 adventures with his higher Stress for him to gain that ability.

You can adjust this as a GM: suppose the fighter got into a combat where his weapon broke due to him not repairing it and he nearly died because of it. In that case, you can count that as more than one.

The primary purpose of this is to dissuade players who are just trying to game the system and dipping here and there for specific abilities.

REWARDS BEYOND WONDROUS ITEMS Non-standard abilities can also be used as a reward in lieu of Wondrous Items. So, if you would give out a Relic or Occult Item, give out an ability instead, either through a divine boon or because of some talent a character has discovered they have.

LEVELING ABILITIES You can also give out leveling abilities but, once gained, the character will need to continue to sacrifice and train to increase them: they don’t level up automatically as they don’t come naturally to them, although this can be for a lesser cost.

If you don’t want to keep track of that (and I don’t blame you), you can have these abilities increase at half the rate as they normally would but still increase automatically at level up.

MADE UP ABILITIES Maybe you can’t find an Archetype ability that matches what your player is going for. A common example that I’m sure will come up for you is ambidexterity.

In this case, use the same rules but give them that ability.

So if a character is constantly using his off-hand in combat, giving him a heavy penalty, after 2d4!+2 combats, he’s gotten the hang of it and gains ambidexterity.

CRP DISCOUNTS FOR SKILLS & TRAININGS Beyond abilities, you can also use this to reward players by either discounting Skills and Trainings or just giving them to them. So, a character who uses a weapon they don't have Basic Training for, can get that Basic Training at a discount or for free at the next level up (or even during play).

Again, this is used to reward players who roleplay their character well and not for min-maxers to abuse so feel free to adjust these guidelines as you go for each individual player.

Attracting Followers

While a character may use the Recruiting skill to find hirelings at any time, after a character reaches level 10, they start having people seek them out. At that point, and at every level (or 2 for those with a Weird-Adept Archetype) level above that, the GM rolls on the Follower Attracted table found below but to give context to it, let's talk about the different types you can attract.

FOLLOWER TYPES

These come in three varieties:

GROUPIES These are those that wish to swim in the wake of the big fish, primarily profiting off the other followers of the party and are often washerwoman, prostitutes, or errand boys. They don’t ask anything of the party but are happy to be hired for specialty jobs as long as they pay well.

They’re also the least loyal and they’ll never put their lives on the line for the party.

HIRELINGS Hirelings make up the paid help. They often seek out the party directly and have a basic skill or two they can offer. The idea is that the party will help them further their craft and connections for a bit of pay. They’ll make themselves as helpful as possible - such as repairing armor and weapons for the cost of room and board.

Hirelings won’t break contracts unless the captain of the party falls into Low Honor and will be more loyal than groupies, however, they’ll only risk their lives if it’s in their contract to do so.

RETAINERS These are those that could be full adventurers on their own but has hitched their wagon to your train in hopes of getting more. They’re there out of loyalty but they do demand a greater share of the loot due to the fact that they bring more to the table.

These are, essentially, lower-level characters that you can run.

SIDEKICKS Sidekicks are something special. A Sidekick is a person who is completely loyal to a character. They would lay down their lives for a character. A character has a limited number of Sidekicks that he can call upon over the course of his whole lifetime.

Sidekicks are childhood friends, people who deify the character, or other such unquestionably loyal followers so you only get 1 in their entire life.

A Sidekicks is essentially a second Player Character that the player gets to run.

Any new follower can be declared by the player to be a Sidekick, having sought out the party, he is recognized as an old friend or a new friend who swears undying loyalty to the character. Additionally, a follower can be elevated to the status of a Sidekick if he or the character saves the other’s life.

Even before level 10, a character can search out his Sidekick, however, they must be old friends from his past in this case.

Only severe abuse can break the bond between the hero and his Sidekick but should this happen, the Sidekick becomes an enemy of equivalent zeal.

ATTRACTING FOLLOWERS

As stated above, your GM will roll on the following table to determine what followers come find you. Note that this will also be modified by the second table based on your actions.

*If you already have/had your Sidekick, you instead attract a Retainer

**A natural roll of 20 means you roll two additional times, regardless of the penalty.

If a character’s maximum followers has been hit (as dedicated by their Charisma), instead, they just gain another Groupie.

Follower Attracted

Miscellaneous Rules

Stat Score Damage

Stat Score damage occurs in several places and it’s fairly straightforward. Then why have this section, you ask? As a quick aside to keep the game moving.

The sudden change in ability is incredibly unnerving, meaning that until the person can stop, take a breath and re-adjust to their new reality (meaning the player can adjust the stats on his character sheet without breaking off Combat, a Confrontation, a Challenge or any narrative tension the GM has built up), he gets a penalty of 1 for each point lost to anything that Stat Score influences. So, a -3 to Dexterity would net a temporary -3 to Attack, and Defense, +3 to Initiative, all while reducing the Confrontation Die by 3 sizes, if applicable.

If the amount drained is more than the score, the person becomes appropriately incapacitated, but not dead, until the Stat Score damage is healed.

Diseases & Poisons

These rules will reference poisons, as they’re the most common use case, but they equally apply to disease.

They have 3 dimensions to a poison: its Lethality, Speed, and Symptoms.

Poisons are handled like Confrontations, with each round happening as noted by its Speed starting at the time the poison is put into the body. Each round the poison rolls the dice associated with its Lethality. The infected person can add their Con Confrontation Die each round while other characters can add their Medicine Skill as an additional dice each round to help.

Losing a round denotes that the symptoms are getting worse. Symptoms are what the poison attacks. This could be one of the character’s Stat Scores, their Stress, their Fatigue or any combination of these choices.

If one the character’s Stat Score falls below 0, the Stat Score damage multiplied by 10 and then done to their Vitality in a single Wound that simply becomes more severe. In the case of Stress, Vitality starts to be eaten away when you reach your Stress Threshold.

Every success counts against the Lethality of the poison, removing 1 dice from it. Once all the dice have been removed, the Confrontation is over and the person begins to recover: healing Stress and Vitality as normal and healing 1 point of Stat damage per day.

There’s no germ theory in the world of Bonfire and so illnesses are seen as mysterious forces controlled by the Divines, that can be controlled and even less understood. As such, there won’t be any discussion here about how a particular disease is spread and how to avoid it. GM’s should use them as they see fit for plot purposes and have logical ways of catching it, however, should the players get really into trying to deduce the logic behind it, the GM should feel free to change the ways to catch it to throw them off.

Falling Damage

When your character falls, they take damage based on how far that surpasses their DR from armor, however, they can do somethings to help their decent.

Illumination

For sake of simplicity, there’s five categorizations of how much light there is in an area:

BLINDING This is like staring into the sun. It's very painful and not very pleasant.

Assuming that you cover your eyes, you'll be acting as if you're blind. Even then, a moment's exposure even temporarily results in a d10! second delay as you try to recover. If you continue to expose yourself to this level of illumination, you'll be unable to act at all and will do blind in a number of seconds equal to your Con.

BRIGHT This is the level of light of starting into a fire or just having your eyes near it. It sucks but it probably won't do permanent damage.

This doesn't really affect your aim or anything like that, but it does make it difficult to focus on things, delaying any action by 1d4! seconds as you try and squint and see what you're doing.

Skills Checks that require sight are also rolled on a d12! and take longer.

NORMAL This is normal daylight and occurs no operating penalties.

DIM-LIGHTING This the equivalent of a dark room or nighttime. There’s some visibility; the character can make out shapes and shadows but no fine details.

In melee combat, those in dim-lighting defend and attack with a 1d12! and using ranged weapons is even more of challenge. However, if you insist, you’ll be attacking with a 1d6!.

Skills Checks that require sight are also rolled on a d12!.

Additionally, Sprinting is impossible without acquiring a Stress per second moved.

DARK This is pitch black with the character not even being able to see their hands in front of their faces. This is a dungeon after the torch goes out.

Combat becomes difficult as anyone in darkness defends and attacks with a 1d6! And ranged combat is right out, but, if you insist, you’ll be attacking with a 1d4.

Skills Checks that require sight are also rolled on a d6!.

And moving above Strolling speed is extremely nerve racking, netting a Stress per Speed Category per second. So, moving at a Run for 3 seconds gives you 9 Stress (3 for the Run for 3 seconds).

src="../../../assets/images/lights.png" alt="the different areas of light"

There are currently three sources of light. How they shed their light is noted on the left:

The white is considered Normal, the light grey is Dimly Lit and the beyond that is Dark, assuming no other light sources are provided.

Long-term Exhaustion

Long-Term Exhaustion
NeedNothingRationing
Foodd6! Stress, d6! Damage1d6! halved damage, 1d6! halved Stress, rounded up
Water2d6! Damage1d6! Damage
Sleep2d6! Stress1d6! Stress

Your character isn’t immortal, or at least, they didn’t start out that way, and so still needs to fulfil their basic needs of food, drink, and sleep. Without those basic requirements, he may find himself a bit more lethargic or, worse case scenario, dead.

There are three things your character needs to take care of, as mentioned above: food, water, and sleep, and three levels associated with each, normal, rationing, and nothing, which related to how much you have of each.

If a person sleeps the normal amount (assumed to be 8 hours), eats a healthy amount of food, and drinks a good amount of water, they take no damage or Stress.

However, if they cut back on any of three (called rationing) or don't get any sleep, food, or water (called nothing), they take the associate damage and/or Stress as noted by the table.

This is on 1 Wound per need but does stack: having no food and water gives you 2d6! damage and d6! Stress. Additionally, a Wound doesn't heal until the associated need is returned to normal.

SMALL & LARGE SIZED CREATURES

Obviously, a smaller creature requires less food while a larger one requires more, so Small sized creatures half each threshold while Large creatures double it.

RPGs give things somewhat arbitrary sizes because things affect you differently when you're different sizes. Here’s a handy chart to allow you to ballpark the Size Category something would be in if it ever comes up. These are given in real life, non-fantasy terms to be more helpful.

Most of the time this refers to area, but you can also determine size by weight, if it's applicable. A Ghost could be considered both Medium or Tiny by the metric - go with whatever applies best in that situation.
